1001 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Bowman v. Board of Regents of Universities & State Colleges


No. 1 CA-CV 88-300


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


162 Ariz. 551; 785 P.2d 71; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 249; 43 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 23



September 21, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 7, 1989. Review Denied January 30, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-465897, The Honorable Norman D. Hall, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff faculty member challenged the order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which on the motion to reconsider brought by defendant university and its president, rejected the application of the doctrine of promissory estoppel and ruled that the faculty member had willfully abandoned his employment with the university as a matter of law. The board cross-appealed from the denial of its request for attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: The faculty member filed his action based on 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, the United States Constitution, and state contract law contending that his termination at the university was in retaliation for his exercise of the right of freedom of speech. The state superior court granted the board's motion for reconsideration of its refusal to dismiss the faculty member's complaint, and the faculty member appealed. The court held that: (1) the motion to reconsider was not an attempt to bring an impermissible "horizontal appeal;" (2) the trial judge properly reconsidered the motion for summary judgment because the motion for reconsideration raised issues that the board had not had an opportunity to address; (3) Ariz. Board of Regents Ordinance § 7-207 mandated the form of the contract and not the time limit within which the faculty member's response was due; (4) the issue of promissory estoppel was a factual issue that could not be resolved on a motion for summary judgment; and (5) the court was without subject matter jurisdiction to address the board's argument regarding the propriety of the trial court's reinstatement of the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that awarded summary judgment in favor of the board and the president in the faculty member's action for breach of contract.

 

1002 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Steiger


No. 1 CA-CR 88-657


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


162 Ariz. 138; 781 P.2d 616; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 252; 43 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 31



September 21, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied October 26, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of MARICOPA County, Cause No. CR 87-09227, The Honorable Ronald S. Reinstein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted defendant under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1804, which was entitled "Theft by Extortion."


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of theft by extortion pursuant to § 13-1804. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1804(A)(8) was unconstitutionally vague and that the statute provided a real, credible and substantial threat of arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement. Section 13-1804(A)(8) was unconstitutionally vague both because it provided insufficient guidance to those who must make demands on others, and because it permitted arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement. Not only did ambiguity exist as to what was a legitimate directive for someone like defendant, but also the statute had a chilling effect on expression by others in the political world. Therefore, § 13-1804(A)(8) significantly jeopardized first amendment expression for those not before the court. The legislature had to narrowly draw a statute if it wished to prohibit political intimidation. The court left to the legislature the task of narrowing § 13-1804(A)(8) with such specificity to cover conduct which was within the legislature's power to prohibit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which convicted defendant of theft by extortion and found part of the relevant statute unconstitutionally vague.

 

1003 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


St. Joseph's Hosp. & Medical Ctr. v. Maricopa County


No. 1 CA-CIV 88-047


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


163 Ariz. 132; 786 P.2d 983; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 236; 42 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 41



September 7, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied February 26, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-544264, The Honorable Bernard J. Dougherty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hospital sought reimbursement from appellee county for services provided to the patient, who was allegedly indigent under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 11-297(B)(2). The county denied the claim and the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) granted the county's motion for summary judgment. The hospital appealed.


OVERVIEW: Because the value of the separate property of the patient's wife exceeded the statutory maximum, the county determined that the patient was not "indigent" and was therefore not eligible for county health services. The county denied the hospital's claim for reimbursement of the patient's hospitalization charges. The court determined that the "resources of all persons in the household" unmistakably indicated an intent to include a spouse's separate property. No limitation of the type of resources, separate or community, was expressed in the statute. The court also held that the regulation did not lack sufficient rationality to satisfy the requirements of due process. It was not, however, irrational that the legislature expect that those possessing sufficient separate assets would voluntarily pay for a spouse's necessary medical care, nor did the regulation effect a taking of the hospital's property without just compensation. The state did not "invade" the hospital, but simply required hospitals, as a condition of doing business in Arizona, to accept emergency patients without regard to their ability to pay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1004 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Knight v. Superior Court


No. 1 CA-SA 88-189


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


161 Ariz. 551; 779 P.2d 1290; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 234; 42 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 24



September 5, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Special Action from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CR-88-05386, The Honorable Gloria Ybarra, Judge, The Honorable Walter Lee Jackson, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION GRANTED; RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner brought a special action from his trial before respondent Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), where he was awaiting trial on two counts of armed robbery, to challenge whether he was given constitutionally adequate access to the courts in his attempt to represent himself in his trial.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was awaiting trial on armed robbery and was granted his motion to waive counsel and proceed pro se, with a public defender to act as his advisory counsel. The prisoner filed a motion seeking, among other things, a court order allowing him physical access to a law library instead of the paging system whereby he had to request legal research. The motion was denied. The prisoner then brought a special action to the court, alleging he was denied his constitutional right of access to the courts to prepare his defense. Specifically, he challenged the "paging system" in use to provide inmates with legal research by use of a paralegal instead of a an attorney. The court found the use of a paralegal instead of an attorney in the paging system was not a constitutional deprivation because the paralegal could help direct the prisoner's legal research in the same way an attorney would. Because the paging system was not constitutionally infirm, there was no obligation to transfer the prisoner to a prison where he would have physical access to the courts. Finally, there was no unconstitutional denial of supplies, and the prisoner was not entitled to a typewriter.


OUTCOME: The court accepted special action jurisdiction, but denied the prisoner his requested relief.

 

1005 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. MacGillivray


No. 1 CA-CR 88-261


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


162 Ariz. 539; 785 P.2d 59; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 230; 42 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 16



August 31, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 23, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CR-164338, The Honorable Frank T. Galati, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment and sentence of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him, after a jury trial, of one count of fraudulent schemes and artifices, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2310, 10 counts of submitting fraudulent insurance claims, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1220, and onr count of theft, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1802.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered into a scheme that obtained reimbursement under Medicare, Part B, for ineligible services. Defendant billed Medicare by charging for other, approved treatments. The state alleged that the overall scheme constituted the fraudulent schemes and artifices charge. He was also charged with 10 counts of submitting fraudulent insurance claims, and a theft count. A jury convicted him of all of the charges, and the trial court enhanced his theft sentence based on the fraudulent insurance claims convictions. On appeal, the court reversed the convictions for fraudulent insurance claims. Medicare Part B was not a contract of insurance, which was a required element of a fraudulent insurance claim pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1220. The court affirmed the fraudulent schemes and artifices conviction, and the theft conviction, but vacated the sentences, and remanded for resentencing. The theft conviction was no longer subject to an enhanced sentence without the previous conviction. The court vacated the proper sentence on the fraudulent schemes because it appeared the erroneous belief that the theft conviction required an enhanced sentence may also have affected that sentence.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the defendant's convictions on 10 counts of submitting fraudulent insurance claims. The sentence on the theft count that was enhanced based on the convictions for submitting fraudulent insurance claims was set aside. Although the conviction and sentence on the fraudulent schemes and artifices count was valid, the sentence was set aside and the matter was remanded for resentencing on both convictions.

 

1006 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Hoyle v. Superior Court


No. 1 CA-SA 88-230


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


161 Ariz. 224; 778 P.2d 259; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 209; 40 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 23



August 1, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 22, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. DR-87-13218, The Honorable Edward C. Voss, Judge, The Honorable Rufus C. Coulter, Judge, The Honorable Irwin Cantor, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner putative father sought review of an order of respondent, the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which denied, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-846(F) (Supp. 1988), the putative father's request for a jury trial in a paternity action filed against him by real party in interest, the State of Arizona. The court accepted special action jurisdiction to consider the putative father's claim that § 12-846(F) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The state filed a paternity action against the putative father, who requested a jury trial. The trial court denied the request. Upon accepting special action jurisdiction, the court denied the putative father's request for a jury trial. The court concluded that § 12-846(F) did not abrogate a statutory right to a jury trial in paternity actions because no such right existed when it was enacted. The court held that Ariz. Const. art II, § 23, which preserved the right to a jury trial in those actions in which the right existed at common law when the state constitution was adopted in 1910, did not render § 12-846(F) unconstitutional because no common law right to a jury trial in paternity actions existed in 1910. Finally, the court held that Ariz. Const. art. IV, pt. 2, § 13, which required that a legislative act's title set forth the act's purpose, did not render § 12-846(F) void. Although the title of § 12-846(F) did not state that it required paternity actions to be tried to the court, this did not change existing law, and therefore it was not necessary for the bill's title to provide notice of § 12-846(F)'s purpose.


OUTCOME: The court accepted jurisdiction of the special action but denied the putative father the relief he requested, holding that he was not entitled to a jury trial in the state's paternity action against him.

 

1007 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Belcher


No. 2 CA-CR 88-0516


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


161 Ariz. 133; 776 P.2d 811; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 212; 39 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 61



July 18, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. CR-23858, Honorable Bernardo P. Velasco, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which convicted defendant of one count of third-degree burglary and sentenced him to an enhanced mitigated term of nine years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a male companion were apprehended taking several pair of blue jeans from a department store without paying for them. On defendant's conviction for third-degree burglary, he argued that the burglary statute was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed the conviction and held that the statute was not vague in its use of the word "unlawfully" where that term was a word of common usage. The term did not need to be specifically defined in an instruction or statute as it was generally understood to denote an act done without authorization.Further, no jury instruction was necessary to define the terms "licensed, authorized or otherwise privileged" because those terms were commonly understood by the average person without a dictionary. Finally, the evidence was sufficient to prove defendant's intent where he remained in the store after concealing the jeans because it was clear that he intended to steal the two pair of jeans by putting them on under his own trousers in the fitting room.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for third-degree burglary based on sufficient evidence of his guilt.

 

1008 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Carrow Co. v. Lusby


No. 2 CA-CV 88-0352


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


163 Ariz. 450; 788 P.2d 1201; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 169; 36 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 66



June 13, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted December 18, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. 249461, Honorable Michael J. Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a husband and his wife, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee company on appellants' counterclaim for personal injuries resulting from a motorcycle accident. The company filed the complaint against appellants to recover the value of a heifer that the husband collided with.


OVERVIEW: The company was engaged in cattle ranching. Its cattle grazed on open range territory. The husband was driving his motorcycle in open range territory. A heifer owned by the company suddenly crossed in front of the husband. A collision resulted in which the heifer was killed and the husband suffered injuries. Appellants argued that the superior court erred in not finding that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 24-502 was unconstitutional. They alleged that § 24-502 violated Ariz. Const. art. II, §31, as well as Ariz. Const. art. XVIII, § 6. In affirming, the court found that the threshold question was whether any cause of action existed in 1910 when the constitution was adopted because common law rights and remedies existing at the time of the adoption of the constitution were preserved. The court concluded that no cause of action existed at the time the constitution was adopted. Thus, the two constitutional provisions were inapplicable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1009 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Berger


No. 1 CA-CR 88-522


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


164 Ariz. 46; 790 P.2d 744; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 163; 36 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 45



June 6, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted September 26, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause Nos. CR 87-09693 and CR 87-06925 (Consolidated) The Honorable Lindsay Ellis Budzyn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction for attempted molestation of a child and dangerous crimes against children in the second degree entered by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) upon defendant's guilty plea. Defendant also sought review of his sentence to 15 years of imprisonment and to lifetime parole upon his release from prison pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604.01(I).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his guilty plea was involuntary because he was not advised that he would not be entitled to early release credits pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 41-1604.06 and 41-1604.07. Defendant also argued that the trial court improperly imposed lifetime parole. On appeal, the court determined that the imposition of lifetime parole was not impossible to enforce and did not violate separation of powers as defendant was convicted of dangerous crimes against children in the second degree. Because defendant was eligible for release after serving half of his sentence, if he were to violate parole, he could have been returned to prison to serve the balance of his sentence. The trial court's imposition of lifetime parole did not invade the province of the Arizona Board of Pardons and Paroles as the Board retained discretion on whether to release defendant on parole at all. The court found that the trial court did not commit reversible error by failing to inform defendant that he was ineligible for early release credits as he was clearly informed of the earliest release date and the maximum sentence possible as a result of the plea.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1010 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Bruce Church, Inc. v. Superior Court


No. 1 CA-SA 89-059


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


160 Ariz. 514; 774 P.2d 818; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 146; 35 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 6



May 23, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action, Yuma County Superior Court No. 49877, The Honorable H. Stewart Bradshaw, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court accepted jurisdiction pursuant to Ariz. R. P. for Special Actions 1(a) over the special action of petitioner corporation against respondents, the superior court and the union that was the real party in interest. The petition for special action concerned the adequacy of the supersedeas bond fixed by the trial court to stay the execution of the unconditional money judgment rendered by a jury against the union.


OVERVIEW: The corporation filed an action against the union. After trial, the jury rendered a verdict in favor of the corporation, and the trial court entered judgment against the union in the amount of $ 5,403,016.00. The union subsequently filed a motion to stay enforcement of judgment . The trial court set a supersedeas bond in the amount of $ 250,000.00. The corporation filed a petition seeking relief. The court accepted jurisdiction because there was no adequate remedy by appeal to correct the alleged error of the trial court. Ariz. R. P. for Special Actions 1(a). The court found that the judgment was not secured by the bond fixed because the trial court erred in fixing the supersedeas bond in an amount substantially less than the judgment. The court also found that the trial court failed to provide a hearing to explore the alternatives to a supersedeas bond. The court, therefore, granted relief and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


OUTCOME: The court accepted jurisdiction, granted relief, and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion. The court also ordered that the stay of execution pending either the setting of a bond securing the judgment or the setting of a hearing to explore alternatives was to remain in effect until the trial court acted.

 

1011 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Copeland v. Yuma


No. 1 CA-CV 88-266


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


160 Ariz. 307; 772 P.2d 1160; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 101; 32 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 49



April 11, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Yuma County, Cause No. 53980, The Honorable B. L. Helm, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, City of Yuma and employee, disputed a judgment of the Superior Court of Yuma County (Arizona) entered in favor of appellees, injured wife and husband, after a jury verdict. Appellants argued that the jury was incorrectly instructed on the subject of contributory negligence, opposing counsel's comments during closing argument were improper and prejudicial, and evidentiary rulings by the trial court were improperly restrictive.


OVERVIEW: At appellants' request, the superior court gave R.A.J.I. Negligence Instruction 5. Appellants did not object to the inclusion of the bracketed portion of the instruction in the charge. On appeal, the court held that appellants in effect stipulated to the instruction, and there was no fundamental error permitting them to inject the issue before the court. The court held that, by using the word "companies" in closing argument, appellees' counsel made an indefensible reference to insurance. But, appellants neither objected during or at the conclusion of oral argument, nor requested a curative instruction, nor moved for mistrial. Thus, they waived the chance to raise the misconduct on appeal. The court held that the admissions of appellees' counsel in another personal injury case brought by the wife were admissible in the superior court trial under Ariz. R. Civ. P. 81(d)(2)(D). The superior court excluded the evidence in the interest of judicial economy. The court held that, because the record submitted by appellants did not include the relevant transcript, the court had to assume that the evidence supported the trial judge's determinations. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment. The city and the employee did not properly preserve their issues for appellate review.

 

1012 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Able Distrib. Co. v. James Lampe, Gen. Contr.


No. 1 CA-CV 88-074


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


160 Ariz. 399; 773 P.2d 504; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 105; 32 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 38



April 11, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-584917, The Honorable Joel M. Glynn, Judge, pro tem.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant garnishee sought review of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) ruling which granted judgment for appellee garnishor on a garnishment action. The garnishee contended that the amount owed to defendant debtor was a contingent liability, the debt was not liquidated, the garnishee was denied due process, the trial court excluded evidence of back charges, and arbitration was mandatory.


OVERVIEW: Following judgment for appellee garnishor against defendant debtor, the garnishor sought garnishment from appellant garnishee, which allegedly owed money to the debtor for plumbing work. The trial court, after a hearing, held that the garnishee owed money to the debtor, who owed money to the garnishor. Judgment of garnishment was entered for the garnishor. On appeal, the court affirmed the ruling, finding that the garnishee's debt to the debtor was not a contingent debt merely because it was disputed, because the debtor's work for the garnishee was substantially completed. The debt was liquidated, as evidenced by the contract, invoices, and accountings upon which the trial court determined the parties' obligations. Due process was not denied the garnishee, as both it and the debtor had notice of the hearings and issues, and had an opportunity to present evidence. The court remanded the exclusion of one back charge claimed by the garnishee, even though it was offered after the writ was served, as it arose out of the contract at issue. An arbitration clause did not apply to the garnishor because it was part of the contract between the garnishee and the debtor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling for appellee garnishor, remanding for consideration of one exhibit related to back charges. Appellant garnishee's debt to the debtor was not a contingent debt merely because it was disputed, as the debt was substantially satisfied. The debt was also liquidated, as evidenced by the contract, invoices, and accountings. The garnishee was afforded due process, and the garnishor was not subject to the arbitration clause.

 

1013 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Corbin v. Tolleson


Nos. 1 CA-CIV 8999, 1 CA-CIV 9898, 1 CA-CIV 88-079


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


160 Ariz. 385; 773 P.2d 490; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 98; 31 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 33



April 6, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 30, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-557962, The Honorable Thomas W. O'Toole, Judge and The Honorable Frederick J. Martone, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant businessman appealed the order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which issued preliminary and permanent injunctions prohibiting the sale of his home video course and awarded summary judgment to plaintiff state on the grounds of consumer fraud, racketeering, and forfeiture.


OVERVIEW: A businessman marketed a home video course on how to become a millionaire. The state filed a consumer fraud and racketeering complaint against the businessman alleging that he had falsely and deceptively represented the course to consumers, falsified income information, operated an illegal enterprise, and failed to pay state sales tax. The court held that both the state's proof and the trial court's findings fell short of what was constitutionally required to sustain an injunction of the course. The state never placed the course itself before the trial court, and it failed to establish that the course was entirely commercial speech. In fact, portions of the course were non-commercial, motivational, or informative, and therefore the preliminary and permanent injunctions banning the course were unconstitutional. Summary judgment for the state on consumer fraud grounds was proper where the course promotions and advertisements, as deceptive commercial speech, lacked First Amendment protection. However, in the absence of undisputed evidence of the requisite intent, there was an insufficient basis for the award of summary judgment on the racketeering and forfeiture charges.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the injunctions and reversed the grant of summary judgment based on racketeering and forfeiture.

 

1014 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Petitioners for Deannexation v. Goodyear


No. 1 CA-CIV 88-110


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


160 Ariz. 467; 773 P.2d 1026; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 77; 30 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 30



March 23, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted June 20, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CV 87-19086, The Honorable J. D. Howe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent city sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted petitioners, owners of annexed lands, judgment in an action seeking to have the owners' lands deannexed from the city pursuant to 1986 Ariz. Sess. Laws ch. 45, § 4.


OVERVIEW: The state legislature passed a law that allowed the deannexation of territory from a city or town and return of the territory to the jurisdiction of the county under certain conditions. The law allowed deannexation from a city or town having a population of less than 10,000 people. Owners were residents of lands that were annexed by a city. The owners filed suit seeking to have their lands deannexed from the city pursuant to 1986 Ariz. Sess. Laws ch. 45, § 4. The city challenged the law as an unconstitutional special law. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of the law and granted the owners deannexation. The court reversed, declaring the deannexation provisions unconstitutional. The court held that a statute was an unconstitutional special of local law if it was plainly intended for a particular case. A statute had to be capable of application throughout the state.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment granting deannexation to the owners of the annexed lands and declared the deannexation provisions unconstitutional.

 

1015 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


In re Appeal in Pima County Juvenile Action


No. 2 CA-JV 89-0004


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


162 Ariz. 97; 781 P.2d 74; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 136; 33 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 52



March 16, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Redesignated as Opinion and Publication Ordered April 26, 1989. Review Granted July 13, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. 74802-2, Honorable Gilbert Veliz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The juvenile appealed from the finding of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) that he was in violation of his probation and the order committing him to the Department of Corrections.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was accused of sexual abuse in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1404. He was a 16-year-old at the time, and was found to have fondled a 14-year-old girl's breasts with her consent. The juvenile argued to the trial court that § 13-1404 was unconstitutional as applied to him and other juveniles. His argument was that while the statute was clear as applied to adults, it was unconstitutional as applied to juveniles engaged in consensual sexual activity. The court found that the plain language of § 13-1404 prohibited the conduct engaged in by the juvenile. The statute was not vague nor was it overbroad. Therefore, the trial court acted correctly in finding that the admitted violation of the statute justified the revocation of the juvenile's probation and his commitment to the Department of Corrections.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1016 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


In re Appeal in Maricopa County, Juvenile Action


No. 1 CA-JV 88-038


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


160 Ariz. 90; 770 P.2d 394; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 61; 30 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 16



March 14, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. JV-114428, The Honorable Chris E. Wotruba, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed from the order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) suspending his license until his eighteenth birthday pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-249(D) after he was adjudged delinquent and placed on intensive probation.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was charged with delinquency for one count of the sale of marijuana, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3405(A)(2). At a pre-adjudication hearing, the juvenile agreed to admit to an amended allegation of possession of marijuana for sale. Before accepting the admission, the trial court obtained the concurrence of the father in the plea, advised the juvenile of his constitutional rights, and determined that the admission was knowing, voluntary, intelligent, and had a factual basis. The trial court found the juvenile to be delinquent. The trial court placed the juvenile on intensive probation in his parents' custody. The trial court also ordered his driver's license be suspended until his eighteenth birthday pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-249(D) (1988). On appeal from the license suspension, the court affirmed the order. The court ruled that § 8-249(D) did not violate the juvenile's equal protection rights because it was reasonably related to the legitimate state purposes of discouraging juvenile drug abuse and keeping them off of the roads. The court also ruled that the juvenile system had adequate safeguards to satisfy due process requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order suspending the juvenile's license until his eighteenth birthday after he was adjudged delinquent.

 

1017 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Anchor Equities v. Joya


No. 1 CA-CV 88-117


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


160 Ariz. 463; 773 P.2d 1022; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 52; 29 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 22



March 2, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied June 20, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-573019, The Honorable William P. Sargeant, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant home builder sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which denied the home builder's motion for a new trial following judgment in favor of appellee mortgage bank for damages it suffered as a result of a fraudulent scheme perpetrated by the home builder and by other defendants.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that a loan officer, with the help of a home builder and other defendants, falsified loan applications in order to defraud the mortgage bank. The trial court denied the home builder's motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court applied agency principles and affirmed the denial of the motion. The loan officer's knowledge of the misrepresentations was not imputable to the mortgage bank because he was acting adversely to the mortgage bank's interests. The mortgage bank was not liable under apparent authority principles. The home builder did not identify any conduct on the mortgage bank's part that led him to believe that it had given the loan officer the apparent authority to accept or submit fraudulent loan applications. Nor did the home builder demonstrate that his reliance upon the loan officer's apparent authority was reasonable. The home builder was fully aware of the fraudulent nature of the scheme. Knowledge of the results of an investigation performed by the loan officer was not imputable to the mortgage bank because the loan officer was acting adversely to the bank's interests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the home builder's motion for new trial.

 

1018 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. White


No. 1 CA-CR 88-395


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


160 Ariz. 377; 773 P.2d 482; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 43; 28 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 15



February 23, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 3, 1989. Review Denied June 13, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County, Cause No. CR-12532, The Honorable Richard Anderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona), which imposed consecutive sentences for the separately charged offenses for which defendant was convicted. Defendant had pled no contest to hit and run, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-661, manslaughter, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1103, aggravated assault, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1204, assault, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1203, and endangerment, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1201.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving his car and struck four teenagers who were walking alongside the road. He fled the scene without rendering aid. One of the victims died, a second was seriously injured, and the other two were less severely injured. There was evidence that defendant was extremely intoxicated at the time of the accident. He entered a plea of no contest to hit and run, manslaughter, aggravated assault, assault, and endangerment. Sentences of varying lengths were imposed, and each sentence was to be consecutive to all other sentences. Defendant was sentenced to a total term of 21.7 years of imprisonment. On appeal, defendant contended that the imposition of consecutive sentences in this case constituted a violation of the state and federal double jeopardy clauses as well as a violation of Arizona's double punishment statute because he was being punished with consecutive sentences for his single act of recklessness. The court found that for purposes of the state and federal double jeopardy clauses, the term "offense" referred to the result of the act rather than the act itself; thus, a defendant could be charged with each and every criminal result flowing from his single act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Clay v. Gilbert

Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contestants, who were qualified electors, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which confirmed the results of an election conducted by defendant town for the acquisition of a electricity distribution system and for the issuance of revenue bonds to finance the acquisition.


OVERVIEW: The town conducted an election for the acquisition of an electricity distribution system and for the issuance of revenue bonds to finance the acquisition. Both issues had passed by a close vote. The court held that the trial court erred in holding that the election was a "referendum" election that required a publicity pamphlet. The court affirmed the trial court's decision to excise the unconstitutional "who are taxpayers" language from Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-514 because severability of the statute did not contravene legislative intent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that confirmed the results of the election conducted by the town for the acquisition of a electricity distribution system and for the issuance of revenue bonds to finance the acquisition.

State v. Wilhite


No. 1 CA-CR 10582


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


160 Ariz. 228; 772 P.2d 582; 1989 Ariz. App. LEXIS 22; 26 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 85



January 26, 1989 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 23, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Apache County, Cause No. CR-2195, The Honorable John L. Claborne, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Superior Court of Apache County (Arizona), which convicted him of custodial interference as a class three felony in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1302.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the biological father of the child. Defendant's parental rights were terminated, and the child was adopted by defendant's brother. Thereafter, defendant took the child and a young female to a lake for a number of days. Defendant molested the young girl and deserted both children at the lake. Defendant was charged with kidnapping, interference with child custody, and child molesting. The trial court dismissed the child molesting counts on the grounds of lack of jurisdiction, and defendant was convicted of interference with child custody. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's convictions. Defendant was not a parent for purposes of the interference with child custody statute set forth in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1302, even though he was the child's biological father, because following his termination of parental rights, he had no parental custodial interest assertable in the trial court. Thus, defendant was not entitled to have the conviction reduced to a class six felony. The state violated defendant's right of confrontation by admitting the child's testimony by videotaped deposition; however, this error was harmless because the testimony was cumulative.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for interference with child custody.

State v. Jonas


No. 2 CA-CR 88-0160


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


162 Ariz. 32; 780 P.2d 1080; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 381; 26 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 99



December 22, 1988

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Superior Court of Cochise County (Arizona), which convicted him of one count of trafficking in stolen property and one count of transferring marijuana to a minor under the age of 15 years. Defendant had admitted to a prior felony conviction. The trial court imposed the maximum sentence, 21 years for the trafficking and 25 years for the marijuana sale; the sentences were to run consecutively.


OVERVIEW: A 14-year-old boy informed the police that he had stolen a gun and later gave it to defendant to sell for him. State v. Bauer


Nos. 1 CA-CR 11628, 1 CA-CR 11631


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


159 Ariz. 443; 768 P.2d 175; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 366; 23 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 56



December 13, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied March 14, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CR-147826, The Honorable Francis P. Koopman, Judge pro tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED FOR IMPOSITION OF NEW TERMS OF PROBATION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, adult bookstore and its owner, sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted them of production, publication, sale, or possession of an obscene film, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3502 (1978). The judgment of conviction also ordered appellants to forfeit their permits and licenses, including a city license for running a video center and a patent medicine license.


OVERVIEW: Appellants challenged their convictions under the Arizona obscenity statute, arguing that the trial court erred in instructing the jury on the meaning of the term "prurient interest" as used in the Arizona obscenity statute. The court agreed with appellants that the term "prurient interest" could not encompass normal, healthy sexual interests, and determined that the trial court properly did not include references to "lust" or "lustful desires" in the instructions. The court affirmed the convictions, but vacated the term of probation imposed. The trial court, as a condition of probation, ordered appellants to forfeit any licenses issued to either of them. The court rejected the state's argument that the forfeiture was merely punishment for past behavior, holding that a statute must be analyzed as to its effect and that the effect of forfeiting the video store license was to restrain the dissemination of all materials, those protected under U.S. Const. amend. I as well as those that were obscene. The court held that forfeiture of the patent medicine license did not act as prior restraint because appellants could continue to sell protected materials even without this license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the obscenity convictions of the adult bookstore and its owner, but vacated the term of probation and remanded with instructions that the trial court impose probation in a manner consistent with the court's opinion that requiring the forfeiture of the video store license acted as an unlawful prior restraint on protected speech, although forfeiture of the patent medicine license was not an impermissible prior restraint.

Arizona Water Co. v. Arizona Dep't of Water Resources


No. 2 CA-CV 88-0213


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


160 Ariz. 66; 770 P.2d 370; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 351; 22 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 28



November 29, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied April 11, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY, Cause No. C-586249, Honorable Stanley Z. Goodfarb, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff water company appealed a decision from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which affirmed the decision of defendant Arizona Department of Water Resources (DWR), which denied the water company's applications for Type Two non-irrigation grandfathered water rights under the Groundwater Code, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 45-462 (1956).


OVERVIEW: The water company sought Type Two non-irrigation water rights, but were denied by the DWR. The water company sought judicial review, and the trial court affirmed the decision of the DWR. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that the water company was not entitled to the water rights because it did not come within the purview of § 45-464(C). The court found that the word "includes" in that section operated as a word of limitation, and that any "non-irrigation user" meant someone other than a city, town, or private water company. The fact that one of the water company's wells was located within its service area as defined by the Groundwater Code, but outside its certificated area, as defined by the Arizona Corporation Commission (commission), did not render §§ 45-402(26)(b), 45-464 unconstitutional. The court found nothing in the definition of "service area" under the Groundwater Code conflicted with the grant of power to the commission under Ariz. Const. art. XV, § 3. The court held that the DWR did not perform a taking because the water company still pumped water under its service area rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that had affirmed the DWR's decision that the water company was not entitled to Type Two non-irrigation water rights.

State v. Byrd

Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A

In re Estate of Kopely


No. 2 CA-CV 88-0141


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


159 Ariz. 391; 767 P.2d 1181; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 337



November 10, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied February 22, 1989. Motion to Set Aside Dismissal Denied February 22, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. P-13917, Honorable Alice Truman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant creditor sought review of the judgment for appellee personal representative in the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which held that the creditor's claim for personal injuries against the estate of a decedent was not timely filed and, thus, barred.


OVERVIEW: The probate court found that the creditor's claim against the estate was not timely filed after the first publication of notice to creditors and barred. In an underlying tort action against the estate, the creditor had recovered a judgment, but this action was not timely under the probate claim statutes, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 14-1801 and 3803. The personal representative had raised the issue of the untimeliness of the claim under § 14-3803, but the trial court declined to rule on the issue. On review, the court vacated the probate court's decision, noting initially that the doctrine of res judicata did not apply when the trial court clearly showed its intention not to rule on the timeliness issue. The court found that §§ 14-3801 and 3803 were unconstitutional under the Due Process Clause because they allowed claims of readily ascertainable creditors to be barred after giving notice only by publication. The case was remanded for a determination of whether reasonably diligent efforts would have identified the creditor and uncovered his claim. If the creditor's identity was known or reasonably ascertainable, the barring of his claim without actual notice violated due process.


OUTCOME: The order of the probate court finding that the creditor's claim against the estate of a deceased was barred because of an untimely probate filing was vacated and the matter was remanded to the probate court for further consistent proceedings.

In re Appeal in Yavapai County Juvenile Action


No. 1 CA-JV 88-001


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


158 Ariz. 356; 762 P.2d 643; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 301; 18 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 45

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review from the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona), which entered a decision finding that the juvenile was delinquent for having violated Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-244(9) (Supp.1987), which prohibited a minor from consuming alcohol. The juvenile challenged the suspension of his driver's license pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-249(A) (Supp.1987).


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was stopped for a traffic violation and the smell of alcohol was observed on his breath. He was arrested pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-244(9) for being a minor consuming alcohol even though he was not intoxicated. His driver's license was then revoked for two years pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-249. The juvenile challenged the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-249, because it purported to extend the juvenile court's jurisdiction beyond age 18 by authorizing a two year license revocation. If such a revocation was applied to a 17 year old, it would extend past age 18. However, the court noted that Ariz. Rev. Phoenix v. Superior Court


No. 1 CA-SA 88-144


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


158 Ariz. 214; 762 P.2d 128; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 292; 18 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 35



September 27, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Special Action, Maricopa County Superior Court cause No. CV-88-14849, The Honorable Joseph D. Howe, Judge, JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner city sought special action relief from the preliminary injunction issued by the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) enjoining the city from enforcing or implementing its annexation of an unincorporated area after the trial court found that the city's annexation was an unconstitutional "taking" of the business interests of respondent garbage collection agencies. The court accepted special action jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: In response to the trial court's preliminary injunction enjoining the city from enforcing or implementing its annexation of an unincorporated area, the city sought, and the court accepted, special action jurisdiction because the issue was one of law with statewide significance. The trial court had granted the motion for injunctive relief filed by the garbage collection agencies, after finding that the city's annexation was an unconstitutional "taking" of their business interests without just compensation, in violation of Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 17. Under special action jurisdiction, the court determined that the enactment of an annexation ordinance that complied with statutory requirements was not in and of itself confiscatory. The court pointed out that the mere acquisition of the right to exercise governmental powers pursuant to the annexation ordinance did not itself constitute a "taking" of property because some additional act of the city in the exercise of that power had to be undertaken. The court therefore reversed the trial court's order enjoining the annexation and directed the trial court to enter an order quashing the preliminary injunction.


OUTCOME: The court accepted special action jurisdiction and granted the relief requested by the city in its challenge to the preliminary injunction issued by the trial court that enjoined the city's enforcement or implementation of the annexation of an unincorporated area. The trial court's order enjoining the annexation was reversed, and the trial court was directed to enter an order quashing the preliminary injunction.

State v. Marcham

Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


160 Ariz. 52; 770 P.2d 356; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 280; 17 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 56

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of aggravated assault and sentenced him to 11.25 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of aggravated assault and assessed a punishment of 11.25 years imprisonment. Defendant's trial counsel withdrew after trial and defendant obtained new counsel for the appeal. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that defendant failed to raise any objection to a deaf juror at trial and therefore did not preserve the issue for appeal. Fund Manager v. Corbin


Nos. 1 CA-CIV 9739, 1 CA-CIV 9667


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


161 Ariz. 348; 778 P.2d 1244; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 256; 14 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 13



August 2, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted March 13, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause Nos. C-565072 and CV-87-10301, The Honorable William P. Sargeant, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; DISMISSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, defendant State appealed orders from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff retirement system fund manager (fund manager) as to whether it had complied with the provisions of the Arizona Procurement Code (code), Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 41-2501 to -2652 (Supp. 1987), and dismissed the State's action against plaintiff law firm, the fund manager's outside counsel.


OVERVIEW: As an initial matter, the court rejected the fund manager's contention that the State, through its attorney general, lacked "standing" to challenge the constitutionality of the state law that amended the code. The court noted that in the present case, the attorney general was acting pursuant to a specific grant of authority; therefore, the fund manager's motion to dismiss for lack of standing was denied. Turning to the merits of the appeal, the court then found that the only reasonable interpretation of 1987 Ariz. Sess. Laws ch. 180 (SB 1098) was that contracts for goods and services approved by the fund manager, such as the agreement between it and the law firm, were retroactively exempted from the requirements of the code. Thus, the fund manager was not in violation of the code, as the State contended, and was entitled to summary judgment in its favor. The court further found no merit in any of the specific constitutional challenges to the adequacy of SB 1098 and concluded that the law impaired no constitutionally protected vested rights. Accordingly, the court affirmed the summary judgment and dismissed the other appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the entry of summary judgment in favor of the fund manager and accordingly dismissed the appeal of the dismissal of the State's action to recover allegedly illegal payments of public monies made to the law firm by the fund manager.

 

1031 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Tucson v. Fahringer


No. 2 CA-SA 88-0072


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


162 Ariz. 159; 781 P.2d 637; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 254; 13 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 81



July 21, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted January 26, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: SPECIAL ACTION PROCEEDINGS, Pima County Superior Court Cause No. 228625, RELIEF GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants state and city appealed an order of the Pima County Superior Court (Arizona), which granted the motion of plaintiff passengers to strike their affirmative defense. The passengers had sought to recover for injuries sustained in a car accident and alleged that the road was negligently maintained. The defendants had asserted that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-820.03(2) precluded liability for certain injuries attributable to a drunk driver.


OVERVIEW: Where injuries were partially attributable to a drunk driver, § 12-820.03(2) barred any claim by the driver or his adult passengers against a public entity. The trial court held that § 12-820.03(2) violated Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 6, which barred abrogation of the right to recover damages for injuries. The trial court found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-820.03(2) required a plaintiff to overcome practically insurmountable defenses given the number of uninsured drunk drivers. On appeal the court reversed. Because the passengers' right of action did not exist at the time the constitution was adopted, it was not protected by Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 6. Also, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-820.03(2) did not abrogate a negligence claim by creating insurmountable hurdles for those whose injuries were partially attributable to a drunk driver. The passengers could prove that the driver was not drunk or that the accident was not his fault. In addition, § 12-820.03(2) did not violate equal protection under Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 13. The classification created by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-820.03(2) was reasonably related to deterring drunk driving and avoiding extensive public expense due to drunk driving.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that granted the passengers' motion to strike and its finding the statute was unconstitutional. The court remanded with instructions to reinstate the defendants' affirmative defense.

Thurston v. Phoenix


No. 1 CA-CIV 9773


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


157 Ariz. 343; 757 P.2d 619; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 241; 12 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 13



July 7, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-531215, The Honorable William P. Sargeant, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and city council, sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which ruled in favor of appellee citizens in their action seeking to set aside Phoenix. Ariz., Ordinance G-2700, by which over nine square miles were annexed by the city.


OVERVIEW: The city council enacted Ordinance G-2700, annexing approximately 9.49 square miles. The citizens filed a petition to set aside the annexation, claiming that the annexation statute was unconstitutional and that Ordinance G-2700 was adopted in violation of the Open Meeting Law, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 38-431 to 38-431.09. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of the citizens, declaring the annexation statute unconstitutional. On appeal, the Arizona Supreme Court found the statute to be constitutional and remanded the case to the trial court. After remand, the trial court entered summary judgment in favor of the citizens on the Open Meeting Law violation. On appeal, the court found that the city failed to satisfy the agenda requirement of the Open Meeting Law, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 38-431.02, which provided that at least 24 hours prior to the meeting, the city had to provide the public with an agenda listing the specific matters to be discussed. The court then found that the information provided to the public failed to indicate that an additional tract would be annexed. The court concluded that the notice was, at best, confusing and may have actually been misleading.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1033 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Larson


No. 1 CA-CR 12145


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


159 Ariz. 14; 764 P.2d 749; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 240; 12 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 6



July 5, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied August 18, 1988. Review Denied December 13, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. LCA-87-00493, The Honorable John H. Seidel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which vacated the city court's order dismissing a domestic violence assault, a class one misdemeanor, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1203(A)(1), and remanded the matter for trial.


OVERVIEW: The city court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3981(B), requiring the prosecuting attorney's recommendation before the misdemeanor offense of domestic violence could be compromised and dismissed, constituted an unconstitutional invasion of the powers of the judiciary. The city court dismissed defendant's domestic violence charge. On review, the trial court vacated the order. On further review, the court affirmed the trial court and held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3981(B) was constitutional and did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. The legislature had the constitutional power to legislate on any subject unless restrained by the constitution. The legislature properly exercised its constitutional authority pursuant to Ariz. Const., art. 4, part 1, § 1, when it enacted the compromise statute in its present form, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3981(B). The legislature clearly expressed its intention that crimes of domestic violence not be subject to the general compromise statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court finding that the domestic violence charges against defendant could not be compromised unless recommended by the prosecutor.

 

1034 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Emergency Medical Transp. v. Tempe


No. 1 CA-CIV 9577


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


157 Ariz. 260; 756 P.2d 929; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 148; 8 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 41



May 19, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 5, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-605067, The Honorable Frederick J. Martone, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ambulance company, upon learning of a contract between respondent city and respondent competitor and the approval of respondent Director of Arizona Department of Health Services (DHS), filed a petition for special action relief. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) accepted jurisdiction, but denied relief, and the ambulance company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city awarded a contract for emergency ambulance services to the competitor as sole provider, and DHS approved. Ariz. Const. art. XXVII, § 1 provided for regulation of ambulance service and Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 36-2232 to -2244 bestowed regulatory powers upon DHS. The court held that, by entering into the contract, the city had not engaged in regulation, but had instead acted lawfully pursuant to its home rule charter and its police powers. The fact that one party to the contract was a municipal corporation did not convert that agreement into regulation. The court held that the city had not undertaken to regulate in the area of ambulances and ambulance services. The contract was in compliance with the laws of Arizona and the rules and regulations of DHS. Because the city had not undertaken to regulate, it followed that DHS could not be said to have delegated regulatory power. Furthermore, DHS had maintained control over all important aspects of ambulances and ambulance services, including issuance of certificates of necessity and the fixing of minimum rates and response times. The decision was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying relief to the ambulance company was affirmed.

 

1035 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Lawhon v. L.B.J. Institutional Supply


No. 1 CA-CIV 9398


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


159 Ariz. 179; 765 P.2d 1003; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 144; 8 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 25; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P11,802



May 17, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 20, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause C-484313, The Honorable Joseph D. Howe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff survivors filed a wrongful death action, naming defendant restaurant and identifying the manufacturer and distributor as "John Does." An amended complaint named the manufacturer and distributor as defendants. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) granted a motion for judgment on the pleadings on grounds that any action against the manufacturer and distributor was barred by the statute of limitations. The survivors appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent suffered a fatal reaction to a sulfite agent used by the restaurant. The wrongful death action included products liability counts based upon the sulfite agents in the food. After filing the first amended complaint, the survivors eventually learned that the distributor had sold a sulfite product to the restaurant before the decedent's death and that the distributor had purchased the sulfite product from the manufacturer. The second amended complaint was filed more than two years after the decedent's death. The court held that the cause of action "accrued" when the survivors discovered or by the exercise of reasonable diligence should have discovered that they were injured by a particular defendant's negligent conduct. The cause of action did not accrue until the survivors knew or should have known of both elements of causation, what and who caused the injury. That was a factual issue not determined by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1036 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Jurgella v. Danielson


No. 2 CA-CV 88-0121


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


158 Ariz. 542; 764 P.2d 27; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 124; 46 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1182; 6 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 65



April 21, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition and Cross-Petition for Review Denied November 22, 1988. *


*  Gordon, C.J., of the Supreme Court, did not participate in the determination of this matter.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY, Cause No. C-550534, Honorable Alan S. Kamin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee filed an action in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) against defendants, city, police chief, and director (collectively defendants), alleging handicap discrimination, breach of contract, and wrongful termination. The trial court granted defendants summary judgment. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee was accepted by defendants as a police officer. But while at the academy his blood pressure was found to exceed academy regulations. The applicant was disqualified. 29 U.S.C.S. § 794 of the Federal Rehabilitation Act of 1973 (Act) prohibited discrimination against otherwise qualified handicapped person in federally funded programs. The employee argued that defendants perceived his hypertension as a handicap under the Act, and that except for the perceived handicap the applicant could perform his job. The court found that those allegations stated a cause of action under the Act. The fact that the city was merely following state law in denying the employment did not free the city from liability. Compliance with state law was not a valid defense when certification was conditioned on otherwise discriminatory practices. The trial court properly dismissed the wrongful discharge and breach of contract claims. State law required that police receive state certification. But the employee failed to complete the course required for certification, and thus the city was forced to discharge him as a police officer.


OUTCOME: The court, in an employment dispute, reversed the decision of the trial court to dismiss the employee's handicap discrimination claim. The court affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the employee's breach of contract and wrongful discharge claims.

South Tucson v. Industrial Comm'n


No. 1 CA-IC 3798


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


156 Ariz. 543; 753 P.2d 1199; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 99; 6 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 27



April 14, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Special Action--Industrial Commission, ICA CLAIM NO. 569-90-0012, CARRIER NO. 86-06171, Administrative Law Judge Bill H. Enriquez, AWARD SET ASIDE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a special action review, petitioners, city and its workmen's compensation carrier (carrier), appealed a decision by respondent Industrial Commission (commission) (Arizona) that excused respondent claimant's late protest and awarded worker's compensation benefits to the claimant who was a prisoner and was injured while working for the state under an intergovernmental agreement with the state corrections department.


OVERVIEW: The claimant injured his back when assisting in garbage collection while on a work release program from prison. The intergovernmental agreement between the state corrections department and the city was authorized under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 41-124.01(B) and required the city to pay a set salary for prisoner labor. The carrier had denied compensation because the claimant was not a city employee. It mailed a notice to his last known address and made no other effort to locate him. When the claimant was released from prison, he filed a late protest. On appeal, the court set aside the award for the claimant. The court reasoned that the commission properly excused the late filing because of the carrier's failure to make a reasonable effort to notify the claimant. However, the claimant was being compensated under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 31-254(I) and thus, the exclusion of worker's compensation benefits under that section also applied to the claimant. The statute was constitutional because although the legislature had authority to extend compensation coverage to prisoners, the mandatory coverage for public employment did not extend to prisoners who did manual labor for a city.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the worker's compensation award granted in favor of the claimant. The court held that the statutory exclusion of worker's compensation coverage to prisoners was constitutional.

State v. Richey


No. 1 CA-CIV 9400


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


158 Ariz. 298; 762 P.2d 585; 1988 Ariz. App. LEXIS 91; 6 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 16



April 12, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted September 23, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Apache County, Cause No. C-8036, The Honorable John L. Claborne, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Apache County (Arizona), which convicted him of driving without an Arizona operator's license and failure to register a vehicle in Arizona.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of his traffic violation convictions, defendant argued that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-102(A)(1), which defined "resident" for purposes of registering and operating a vehicle in Arizona, violated the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and unconstitutionally burdened the right to travel. Defendant argued that the residency definition violated the Equal Protection Clause because the State failed to show that the statute promoted any compelling state interest. The court disagreed and affirmed and held that the residency requirement was not a durational residency statute. It did not discriminate between old and new residents, and, thus, did not violate equal protection. The court found that the statute required all residents to register their vehicles and to obtain licenses. Further, Arizona had the right to prescribe reasonable, uniform, vehicle registration and licensing requirements because they were necessary to insure public safety. The court held that defendant was not entitled to a jury trial because the offenses charged were petty offenses. The possible six-months in jail was not so severe as to require a jury trial. The fine imposed was under $ 1,000.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Brooks

March 29, 1988

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilt to attempted trafficking in stolen property. Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Pinal County (Arizona), which sentenced defendant to the maximum prison term.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that there was not a factual basis for the guilty plea and that the trial court erred in sentencing defendant to a term of imprisonment. The court held that defendant's statements at the change of plea hearings, combined with the information contained in the presentence report, were ample to establish a factual basis for his guilty plea to attempted trafficking. Defendant also argued that the trial court should not have imposed a prison term. The court held that the sentencing court was free to reject a probation officer's recommendation of probation and to sentence defendant to a term of imprisonment even where probation was recommended. Accordingly, the court affirmed the trial court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Roberts v. Mesa

*  Cameron, J., of the Supreme Court, did not participate.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inhabitants challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Court of Maricopa County, Arizona, that granted appellee cities' motions for summary judgment in consolidated cases challenging annexations by the City of Phoenix and the City of Mesa.


OVERVIEW: The inhabitants of two cities contended that the trial court erred in granting the cities' motions for summary judgment in consolidated cases challenging annexations by the City of Phoenix and the City of Mesa. The inhabitants contended that the legislation underlying the annexations was unconstitutional. The court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-471 (1984) did not violate due process because it did not delegate a significant portion of the legislature's powers in the annexation context to private individuals who were free to exercise the delegated powers without reference to any standard or rule. Accordingly, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting the inhabitants' motions for summary judgment in consolidated cases challenging annexations by the City of Phoenix and the City of Mesa.

State v. Vess

DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which convicted him of child molesting, sexual abuse, and furnishing obscene materials to a minor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for child molesting, sexual abuse, and furnishing obscene materials to a minor. During his trial, the prosecutor moved, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4253(A), that the testimony of the alleged victim be taken in another room and transmitted by closed circuit television to the courtroom for the jury to view. The motion was granted without requiring a showing or making a finding that there was any need to proceed in this manner. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction. Stat. § 13-1416 a number of statements by the alleged victim to teachers, child protective service workers, police officers, psychologists, and foster parents. The court held that was prejudicial because at the jury's request that taped statement was replayed during its deliberations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment.

Gehres v. City of Phoenix

Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B

November 30, 1987

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and tavern, challenged a judgment from the Superior Court Of Maricopa County (Arizona), which was entered against them and defendant driver's administrator jointly and severally in plaintiff survivors' negligence action seeking to recover for the death of their decedent in a traffic accident involving a drunk driver that was insolvent.


OVERVIEW: The decedent and the driver were killed in a collision that occurred as the driver was fleeing from city police officers. The survivors filed an action against the tavern for having furnished alcoholic beverages to the driver when he was intoxicated. It also alleged that the city police officers negligently conducted the high-speed chase of the driver immediately before the collision occurred. A jury determined that the driver was 95 percent responsible in the collision, the tavern was 3 percent responsible, and the city was 2 percent responsible. The trial court entered a judgment of joint and several liability against all defendants. On appeal, the court affirmed. Sufficient evidence of the driver's intoxication while being served drinks at the tavern was introduced to warrant denial of the tavern's motion for directed verdict. The police officer's attempt to stop the driver for drunk driving and the driver's reaction was foreseeable and was not an intervening, superseding cause of the decedent's death. The city and the tavern were liable for the full burden of the verdict regardless of the fact that the driver was found to be more comparatively negligent in the collision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of damages against the city and the tavern for injuries sustained by the decedent in the collision with the drunk driver.
