State v. Adams


No. 1 CA-CR 11179


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


156 Ariz. 88; 750 P.2d 31; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 591



November 19, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted March 8, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CR-158133, The Honorable Peter T. D'Angelo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his guilty plea in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) for trafficking in stolen property, a class three felony, with one prior felony conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his plea agreement had to be set aside because he was not informed of the specific amount of restitution that could have been ordered. The plea agreement required payment of restitution to the victim for economic loss, but did not specify the amount. Defendant was sentenced to 15 years in prison, and ordered to pay restitution of $ 100. After the plea was accepted the Arizona Supreme Court held that a plea had to be set aside if defendant was not informed of the specific amount of restitution that could have been ordered. The court affirmed, finding that the supreme court decision on informing a defendant of the amount of restitution was to be applied prospectively. To determine if a decision was to be applied retroactively or prospectively a court had to consider the purpose to be served by the new standards, the extent of reliance upon the old standards; and the effect on the administration of justice of a retroactive application of the new standard. The court found that the rights of defendants protected by a retroactive application was minimal compared to the relatively high cost to the state if pleas were reversed by retroactive application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's guilty plea to trafficking in stolen property, and his sentence.

State v. Fowler


No. 1 CA-CR 10210-PR


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


156 Ariz. 408; 752 P.2d 497; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 580



October 29, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Rule 32.9(c), Arizona Rules of Criminal Procedure, Cause No. CR-117954, The Honorable Peter T. D'Angelo, Judge. REVIEW GRANTED; RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of sexual assault, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted the state's motion to dismiss his second petition for post-conviction relief because it was precluded under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4234(F) (Supp. 1986) in that it was filed more than one year from the date of the mandate in defendant's prior appeal.


OVERVIEW: In 1981 defendant was convicted of sexual assault. The trial court denied his petition for post-conviction relief. Thereafter, his timely direct appeal was consolidated with his petition for review. In 1983, the conviction was affirmed on direct appeal and the review was granted, but relief was denied on the petition for post-conviction relief. In 1986, defendant filed the subject petition for post-conviction relief and the state argued for its dismissal under § 13-4234(F) because it was filed more than one year from the date of the mandate in the appeal. Defendant argued that § 13-4234 was unconstitutional because it invaded the rule-making power of the Arizona Supreme Court, which it had been granted under Ariz. Const. art. 6, § 5. The court granted review, granted relief, and held that although the right to post-conviction relief was substantive, the time limits in § 13-4234 were purely procedural. The court further held that the one-year time limit provided for in § 13-4234 was unconstitutional because it was in conflict with Ariz. R. Civ. P. 32 and therefore, unconstitutionally invaded the province of the Arizona Supreme Court's rule-making authority.


OUTCOME: The court granted review of defendant's petition for post-conviction relief, granted relief, and held that the one-year limitation was unconstitutional. The court remanded to the trial court with directions to reinstate the petition for post-conviction relief with instructions that the state was allowed to file an amended response to the petition for post-conviction relief.

Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


156 Ariz. 518; 753 P.2d 1174; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 607

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) in a jury trial for two counts of child molestation, two counts of sexual conduct with a minor under 15 years of age, and one count of sexual exploitation of a minor. Defendant's sentence totaled 91 years and was to be served without the possibility of parole, commutation, pardon, work furlough, or other release from confinement.


OVERVIEW: A detective interviewed defendant in his hotel room regarding his behavior towards a minor. Defendant was arrested and read his Miranda rights. Rev. The sentences specified in § 13-604.01 were mandatory, thus, no separate allegation of dangerousness was required, and defendant was properly sentenced.

Allen v. Girard

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. 237343, Honorable Bernardo P. Velasco, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with driving under the influence and for driving with a blood alcohol content greater than .10 per cent. Defendant filed a petition for special action seeking dismissal of the traffic citations. The Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) denied the petition, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that an officer did not have authority to issue the tickets because defendant was on private property when the alleged drunk driving incident occurred. Defendant contended that the court lacked jurisdiction because Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692 was restricted by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-104 to offenses that occur on a public highway or roadway. Defendant also contended that the application of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692 to private property was unconstitutional because it violates Ariz. Const. art. 4, pt. 2, § 13. The court held that under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-621 the provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692 applied throughout the state and that there was noting in either statute that restricted jurisdiction in a DUI action to a public highway. The court also held that Ariz. Const. art. 4, pt. 2, § 13 referred only to titles of acts enacted by the legislature and not to titles of sections or articles in the code. Finally, the court held that there was a compelling state interest in enforcing Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692 on private property because an intoxicated or reckless driver of an automobile on private property was just as much a menace as he was on a public highway.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling.

 

1050 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Pittsburgh & Midway Coal Mining Co. v. Arizona Dep't of Revenue


No. 2 CA-CV 87-0251


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


156 Ariz. 568; 754 P.2d 295; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 537



September 30, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted June 7, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY Cause No. C-505803, Honorable Noel Fidel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which awarded a refund with interest to appellee taxpayer for payments that it erroneously made.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer paid use taxes without protest to the state because it had determined that the transactions were not subject to sales tax in another state. The other state thereafter determined that the transactions were subject to their sales tax. The taxpayer challenged the determination in the other state, sought a refund in the state, and undertook to pay future use taxes for similar transactions under protest. After the other state successfully established its sales tax the trial court ordered a refund with interest. The state asserted that the taxes that were not paid under protest did not have to be refunded and the taxes voluntarily refunded did not bear interest. The court affirmed the decision that ordered a refund of the taxes with interest because it determined that: (1) under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42-1413(A) a refund of an erroneous overpayment did not require that the payment was made under protest as a precondition for the refund; (2) an erroneous overpayment was entitled to interest on repayment pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44-1201; and (3) a voluntary repayment was subject to interest as an indebtedness under Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44-1201.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that awarded a refund with interest to the taxpayer for payments erroneously made.

 

1051 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Westwood Homeowners Ass'n v. Tenhoff


No. 1 CA-CIV 8957


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


155 Ariz. 229; 745 P.2d 976; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 508



September 3, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted December 15, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-530432, The Honorable Thomas W. O'Toole, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, homeowners and association for retarded citizens, challenged the judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee homeowners' association in a declaratory relief action to compel the closing of a home in which six developmentally disabled persons lived. The superior court found that the home violated a restrictive covenant.


OVERVIEW: Developmentally disabled persons lived in a group home, which the homeowners association sought to remove due to a restrictive covenant. The court reversed the summary judgment granted by the trial court in favor of the homeowners association. The trial court correctly found that the facility used to care for mentally disabled individuals violated the plain words of the deed restriction. However, Arizona had adopted the public policy of assisting the developmentally disabled by promoting their deinstitutionalization. The court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 36-551.01 guaranteed to all developmentally disabled persons in the state the rights, benefits, and privileges guaranteed by the constitutions and laws of the United States and Arizona. Those rights could not be denied as the result of such disability. The court held that validation of pre-1978 restrictive covenants was contrary to the public policy set forth by the entire Developmental Disability Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment in favor of the homeowner's association. The court found that although the home for the mentally disabled violated restrictive covenants, the rights, benefits, and privileges guaranteed by the constitutions and laws of the United States and Arizona could not be denied as a result of the disability.

 

1052 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Feld


No. 1 CA-CR 9471


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


155 Ariz. 88; 745 P.2d 146; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 481



August 4, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied December 1, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause CR-148389, The Honorable Alan S. Kamin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted an individual defendants' motion to dismiss count I of a criminal indictment for conducting an illegal enterprise through racketeering in violation of the Arizona organized crime and fraud statutes (RICO), Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-2301 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The state argued that the remedies set forth in Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-2314 were constitutional or had to be interpreted as constitutional. The state also urged that even if some remedies were unconstitutional, the trial court was unjustified in finding that obscenity could not be used as a predicate offense under the state law RICO statutes. Defendants urged that the majority of the RICO remedies were unconstitutional as applied to obscenity and that it made little sense for the court to try to save any of the provisions after excising the unconstitutional portions. Defendants also argued that the crime of illegally conducting an enterprise through obscenity was unconstitutionally vague. The court concluded that the trial court erred in declaring that obscenity could not be used as a predicate offense for RICO prosecutions; and construed RICO as related to a criminal prosecution for obscenity, such that it passed constitutional muster and did not have a chilling effect on protected rights. The court also determined that the state's remedies against obscenity under RICO were more limited than the state's remedies against other forms of racketeering activity.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order that granted the defendants' motion to dismiss count I of the indictment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1053 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crego


No. 2 CA-CR 4786


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


154 Ariz. 278; 742 P.2d 289; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 474



July 23, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied September 1, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. CR-17782, Honorable Raner C. Collins, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which convicted him of two counts of child molestation and sentenced him to consecutive, aggravated prison terms of 20 years for each conviction. Defendant contended that the sentence imposed was excessive and constituted cruel and unusual punishment.


OVERVIEW: The sentence was within the statutory range, but defendant argued that the total 40-year sentence was disproportionate to the crime committed. The court found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604.01(B) mandated a presumptive prison term of 17 years for a conviction of child molestation. Section 604.01(J) required that the sentence imposed for each count be consecutive to any other sentence imposed. Under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604.01(D), the 17-year presumptive sentence could be increased or decreased by up to 5 years pursuant to the provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-702. At sentencing, the trial court found the aggravating circumstance of defendant's prior offenses, the prior sexual nature of the offense for which he had been released from prison just before the instant offenses, and his lack of remorse. There was nothing in the record that indicated an abuse of the trial court's sentencing discretion. The court concluded, based upon the gravity of the offense, the harshness of the penalty, the sentences imposed on others in the same jurisdiction, and sentences imposed on others similarly situated, the sentence imposed upon defendant did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Humana Hosp. Desert Valley v. Superior Court


Nos. 1 CA-SA 035, 1 CA-SA 034


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


154 Ariz. 396; 742 P.2d 1382; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 460



July 16, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied October 20, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: A Special Action from the Maricopa County Superior Court, Cause C-571266, Honorable Marilyn A. Riddel, Judge. RELIEF GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, hospital and physician, appealed the order of the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), which denied their motions to quash respondent patient's subpoena duces tecum and entered an order compelling production of peer review documents.


OVERVIEW: A patient brought a medical malpractice action against a physician and an action against the hospital for negligently allowing the physician to practice on its staff and for negligently supervising him. The patient's subpoena duces tecum requested the physician's application for staff privileges and records reflecting the hospital's investigation into the physician's background and experience. The hospital and physician filed special action petitions requesting review of the denial of their motions to quash. The court held that the privilege expressly conferred by Arizona's Peer Review Act (Act), particularly Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 36-445.01, applied to the credentialing records subpoenaed. The court held that the Act established an evidentiary privilege regulating the negligent supervision claim and did not violate the anti-abrogation clause of Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 6. The court held that the hospital peer review privilege did not invade the rule-making power of the supreme court. The court held that the physician and hospital's personal rights to the privilege entitled them to standing to object to the subpoenaing of information from the non-party hospitals.


OUTCOME: The court granted special action relief, reversed the order compelling production, and ordered the trial court to deny discovery of privileged documents, including the physician's applications for staff privileges at the hospital and at the non-party hospitals.

Transamerica Fin. Corp. v. Superior Court


No. 1 CA-SA 018


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


155 Ariz. 327; 746 P.2d 497; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 447



July 9, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted January 5, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: PETITION FOR SPECIAL ACTION, Maricopa County Superior Court No. C-543315, The Honorable Frank T. Galati, Judge, RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) denied petitioners parent's motion to dismiss an action by brought by real parties in interest borrowers concerning whether a private right of action existed under the Consumer Loan Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 6-601 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, parent and subsidiary, were two corporations that loaned money. One was the parent company of the other. The parent was licensed under the Consumer Loan Act (Act), Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 6-601 et. seq., requiring a set interest rate for borrowers. The subsidiary was not licensed and could set any interest rate agreed between it and real parties in interest borrowers. Borrowers' complaint alleged that the loans made by subsidiary should be attributed to parent based on an alter ego theory. The issue was whether borrowers had a private right of action under the Act. Parent's motion to dismiss based on the ground that the Act did not provide a private action was denied. On appeal, the court held that no implied private right of action arose under the Act. The court concluded that the legislature intended that the Act be enforced through administrative procedures, not by private actions. The court vacated the trial court's order and remanded the case for dismissal.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order and remanded the matter for dismissal of real parties in interest borrower's complaint. No implied private right of action arose under the Consumer Loan Act (Act); the legislature intended that the Act be enforced through administrative procedures.

 

1056 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Aikins v. Arizona Dep't of Water Resources


No. 2 CA-CV 87-0074


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


154 Ariz. 437; 743 P.2d 946; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 421



June 25, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY, Cause No. C-556148, Honorable James Moeller, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) affirming a decision by appellees, Arizona Department of Water Resources and its director, that the landowners could not irrigate their property under the Groundwater Management Act of 1980, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 45-401 to -637. The landowners' property was located with a subsequent irrigation non-expansion area (INA).


OVERVIEW: The Act totally banned any increased irrigation in subsequent INAs under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 45-437(B). The landowners argued that they made substantial capital investments in their property for irrigation purposes during appropriate time periods and that the Department's interpretation of § 45-437(B) constituted an unlawful taking of their property. The court disagreed and affirmed. The determination of whether land in a subsequent INA could be irrigated was provided by statute. It required the land to be irrigated during a specific five-year period. It did not require a substantial capital investment for irrigation purposes with no set time limits. The court rejected the landowners' interpretation because it assumed that the legislators negated the five-year limit in the second part of the statute. This would allow irrigation for any land that had been irrigated in the past and was inconsistent with the legislative intent. There was no unlawful taking because the landowners did not own the groundwater under their land. The State of Arizona always had the right to exercise its police power as to the landowners' right to use the groundwater.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

McPeak v. Industrial Comm'n


No. 1 CA-IC 3540


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


154 Ariz. 232; 741 P.2d 699; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 420



June 16, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied September 22, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action -- Industrial Commission, ICA CLAIM NUMBER 453-66-9030, CARRIER NUMBER D41-6875, Administrative Law Judge Peter J. Baum.



DISPOSITION: AWARD AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee brought a special action that challenged the decision of respondent Industrial Commission of Arizona, which entered an award setting the average monthly wage of the employee at the statutory maximum in the employee's action for workmen's compensation benefits against respondent employer.


OVERVIEW: The employee had fractured an ankle while working as an ironworker for the employer. His earnings exceeded $ 2500 per month. Respondent insurance carrier accepted the employee's claim for benefits. The industrial commission established the average monthly wage at $ 1325 per month. The employee contended that the monthly wage, although the statutory maximum, was unconstitutionally low and violated Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 8. The court affirmed, finding that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1041(E) was clear and reflected an obvious intent to limit recovery of compensation. The court found that § 23-1041(E) set the compensable range, and earnings that fell outside of it, no matter how substantial, were excluded from the determination of earning capacity. The court found that Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 8 precluded the legislature from reducing the dollar ceiling of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1041(E) without a vote of the people, likewise precluded the legislature, absent popular referendum, from maintaining that dollar ceiling constant while inflation saps its buying power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of the employer in the employee's action for workmen's compensation benefits.

Tucson Elec. Power Co. v. Swengel-Robbins Constr. Co.


No. 2 CA-CV 6001


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


153 Ariz. 486; 737 P.2d 1385; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 412



May 21, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. 228727, Honorable Robert B. Buchanan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Third-party defendant, employer of the deceased employee, appealed from the summary judgment granted by the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) to third-party plaintiff power company. In the underlying action, the surviving spouse of the deceased employee had filed a wrongful death action against the power company, and the power company had sought summary judgment, claiming indemnity under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 40-360.44(B).


OVERVIEW: The surviving spouse brought an action against the power company for the wrongful death of the employee who was electrocuted while working for the employer. The power company filed a third-party claim for indemnity, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 40-360.44(B), against the employer. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the power company. The employer appealed from the summary judgment, arguing that the indemnification statute was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court found that it was undisputed that the employer violated both §§ 40-360.42 and § 40-360.43(A) by failing to notify the power company of its activity near the power line. The power company therefore made no arrangements to prevent the injury, such as the placement of temporary barriers, deenergization of the lines, or temporary relocation of the lines. The court found no constitutional violation in the statute because the imposition of liability for what was in effect the employer's own negligence in failing to give notice and thereby enabling the power company to take action to prevent injury was a reasonable legislative choice. The court affirmed the summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court found that the indemnification statute challenged by the third-party defendant was constitutional. Accordingly, the court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the third-party plaintiff in its action seeking indemnification from the underlying wrongful death action.

Gosnell Dev. Corp. v. Arizona Dep't of Revenue


No. 2 CA-CV 87-0026


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


154 Ariz. 539; 744 P.2d 451; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 567



May 21, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 30, 1987. Review Denied October 14, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY, Cause No. C-526624, Honorable Joseph D. Howe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor sought review of a decision of the Superior Court Of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment to the Arizona Department of Revenue (department) in the contractor's action seeking a refund of taxes it paid alleging that the department refused or failed to collect similar taxes from other similar contractors.


OVERVIEW: The state imposed a transaction privilege tax on contracting businesses. The department audited one of the contractor's competitors, which used a "gross method" of calculating taxes owed, and determined that it owed additional taxes. Although an appellate court ordered judgment entered for the department, the trial court on remand refused to enter such judgment because it created a hardship and burden on the construction industry. The department prospectively applied the trial court's ruling to all contractors using the "gross method." The contractor had used a different method of calculation, and filed suit seeking a tax refund. The trial court granted summary judgment to the department; however, on appeal, the court reversed, holding that: 1) the contractor was in the same class as competitors who were excused from the privilege taxes; 2) requiring the contractor to pay taxes not also required of his competitors violated the contractor's equal protection rights; and 3) the remedy for denying the contractor equal treatment was to refund it the additional taxes it paid thereby putting it in an equal position with its favored competitors.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which granted the department's motion for summary judgment in the contractor's action for a refund of certain transaction privilege taxes, and ordered the trial court to enter judgment in favor of the contractor for an amount consistent with the court's opinion.

Arizona Farmworkers Union v. Whitewing Ranch Management


No. 1 CA-CIV 8700


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


154 Ariz. 525; 744 P.2d 437; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 570



April 30, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 18, 1987. Review Denied October 20, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yuma County, Cause No. C-51984, The Honorable Douglas W. Keddie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant union challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Yuma County (Arizona), which entered a preliminary injunction declaring the union's strike unlawful, and which enjoined its continuance and ordered all trespassers on appellee ranch to be removed. The union contended that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1385(B)(13) unconstitutionally violated U.S. Const. amends. I, XIV, and the state's due process and equal protection clauses.


OVERVIEW: The union circulated a strike declaration without evidence of a ballot authorizing the strike. The union filed a petition for a temporary restraining order, which the trial court granted. The ranch then filed a claim for injunctive relief, which the trial court granted, finding the strike unlawful. The court affirmed the judgment on appeal. The court found that neither the common law, nor the Fifteenth Amendment conferred an absolute right to strike, and held that the state could have constitutionally required that before the union could have undertaken the strike against the ranch, the strike had to have been authorized by a majority of the workers affected by the strike. The court rejected the union's contention that their due process rights were violated based on the Agricultural Employment Relations Act's lack of guidelines concerning strike votes and bargaining unit composition, as the union had due process through the judicial system. Nor was the statute vague, because a "bargaining unit" was judicially interpreted to have included all the ranch's workers who had been employed for any period of time during the year preceding the strike vote.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's preliminary injunction declaring the union's strike unlawful.

Anson v. American Motors Corp.


No. 1 CA-CIV 7625


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


155 Ariz. 420; 747 P.2d 581; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 626; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P11,357



March 31, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied August 6, 1987. Review Denied December 8, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-455742, The Honorable Warren L. McCarthy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents brought an action against defendants, manufacturer and seller, for the wrongful death of their son. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) granted the motion to dismiss of the manufacturer and seller based on the statute of limitations. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two years and eight months after the son's automobile overturned and killed him, his parents brought a wrongful death action against the manufacturer and seller of the automobile. The trial court dismissed the action because of the two-year statute of limitations set forth at Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-542(2). On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's order dismissing the case. Section 12-542(2) violated the equal protection provision in the Arizona Constitution because it precluded some plaintiffs from pursuing a cause of action before it had been discovered. The discovery rule applied to wrongful death actions. A genuine issue of material fact existed as to when the parents knew or should have known of the defects in the automobile. Moreover, if the parents' allegations about the manufacturer's concealment of the automobile's defects were true, the manufacturer's actions would also be sufficient to toll the limitation period under the doctrine of fraudulent concealment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of dismissal and remanded the parents' wrongful death action to the trial court.

State v. Mercurio


Nos. 1 CA-CR 10290, 1 CA-CR 10291, 1 CA-CR 10292


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


153 Ariz. 336; 736 P.2d 819; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 385



March 10, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 12, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause Nos. LCA-26984, LCA-27077 and LCA-27095. The Honorable Robert A. Hertzberg, The Honorable Howard V. Peterson, Judges.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed judgments from the Superior Court, Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted them of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendants challenged the validity of a provision of a city's charter that provided for the appointment of municipal court judges pro tempore. Defendants contended that the city had no lawful authority to appoint judges pro tempore to hear cases in municipal court and, therefore, the judges pro tempore who presided over their trials lacked jurisdiction. Defendants thus argued that their convictions and sentences were void or voidable. The court rejected defendants' contentions and affirmed their convictions, finding that the language of Ariz. Const. art. VI, § 31 did not require the legislature to provide for the appointment of municipal court judges pro tempore nor did it prohibit cities from so providing in their charters. Thus, the court concluded that the city's charter was not in conflict with any constitutional provision nor was in it in conflict with any other provision of law. Additionally, the court rejected the contention that the subject of the appointment of judges pro tempore had been preempted by the legislature, finding that the legislature had not enacted such laws applicable to city courts. The court refused to infer intent to preempt from legislative silence.


OUTCOME: That court affirmed judgments that convicted defendants of driving while intoxicated.

Lapare v. Industrial Comm'n


No. 1 CA-IC 3454


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


154 Ariz. 318; 742 P.2d 819; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 518



March 10, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 22, 1987. Review Denied September 15, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action -- Industrial Commission, ICA Claim No. 109-38-6181, Carrier No. C609-18545, Bill H. Enriquez, Administrative Law Judge.



DISPOSITION: AWARD AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee challenged the decision of the Industrial Commission (Arizona), which denied his claim for benefits for mental injury which allegedly arose when the employee discovered that he would probably lose his job.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for the employer as a bus driver. The employer sent a letter to its employees stating that their salaries would be reduced. Rumors began circulating regarding layoffs and the employee went to a meeting where it was determined that the drivers would lose their jobs. The employee became very upset and eventually consulted with two psychiatrists. The employee then filed a claim for workers' compensation benefits, which the industrial commission denied benefits. On review, the court found that the employee had the burden to establish all of the elements of a claim for mental injury under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1043.01(B). Thus, the employee had to show an unexpected or extraordinary stress that was related to his employment that substantially contributed to his mental injury. The court concluded that notice of a possible job loss was not sufficiently unusual to justify benefits for the employee's alleged emotional injury. Therefore, the employee was not entitled to benefits.


OUTCOME: The industrial commission's decision was affirmed.

State v. Cole


No. 1 CA-CR 9535


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


153 Ariz. 86; 734 P.2d 1042; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 367



January 29, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied April 8, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CR-149727, The Honorable Bernard J. Dougherty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which entered a judgment of conviction on a jury verdict that found defendant guilty of theft of property with a value of $ 1,000 or more.


OVERVIEW: Defendant worked for a wholesale auctioneer for licensed car dealers. His job entailed driving vehicles to and from the auction and washing cars. After defendant had been working for about two weeks, a car disappeared from the lot. Police tracked the car to defendant. At trial, defendant claimed that he bought the car from a licensed dealer whom defendant had allegedly met at the auction. His defense at trial was that he neither knew nor had reason to know that the car had been stolen. The trial court instructed the jury that the purchase of stolen property outside the regular course of business permitted a conclusion that the purchaser was aware of the risk that it had been stolen pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2305(3). Defendant was convicted. On appeal, defendant argued that the inference under § 13-2305(3) applied only to a defendant who was a dealer in property and not where the defendant merely purchased from a dealer. The court agreed and reversed. It was error to give the instruction. Although defendant did not object to the instruction at trial, the error was fundamental and the court could not say that the erroneous instruction did not contribute to the guilty verdict.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the matter for a new trial.

 

1065 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Estrada v. Arizona Bank


No. 2 CA-CV 5846


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


152 Ariz. 386; 732 P.2d 1124; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 353



January 13, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF COCHISE COUNTY, Cause No. 41946, Honorable James L. Riley, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant trust beneficiary sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Cochise County (Arizona), which granted the motion of appellees, trustee bank and holding company, for summary judgment in a case that alleged appellees mismanaged trust assets.


OVERVIEW: A trust was established on behalf of the trust beneficiary after a settlement in a wrongful death case due to the death of his mother. Appellees were named as trustees. An order was entered that allowed the trust to terminate when the trust beneficiary reached the age of 18 and a final accounting was entered upon the distribution of all trust funds. Appellees filed and gave notice of a petition for final discharge as trustees. Appellees were discharged from further claims or demands and no objections were made to the final accounting. The trust beneficiary filed a complaint that alleged the mismanagement of trust assets by appellees. The lower court granted appellees' motion for summary judgment on the ground that the complaint was barred by res judicata. The trust beneficiary appealed. The court affirmed the lower court judgment because the judicial settlement of the trust accounts barred subsequent litigation with respect to the matters disclosed. The court held that appellees complied with the notice requirements of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 14-7204 and that the trust beneficiary's complaint sought to raise defaults or defects with matters that were fully disclosed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the motion for summary judgment granted on behalf of appellees in the trust beneficiary's suit for mismanagement of trust assets.

 

1066 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Cooke v. Berlin


No. 1 CA-CIV 8529


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


153 Ariz. 220; 735 P.2d 830; 1987 Ariz. App. LEXIS 370



January 8, 1987 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] This case being settled pending appeal, Review Dismissed April 14, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-500142, The Honorable Philip W. Marquardt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant's husband was killed by a woman who received outpatient treatment from appellee psychiatrist at appellee state mental health facility. The wife alleged that the facility and the psychiatrist owed a duty to any third party foreseeably at risk from the negligent diagnosis and treatment of the patient. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) entered summary judgment for appellees. The wife contested the judgment on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Several months after the patient unilaterally terminated treatment, she formed the intent to kill the wife's husband, a disc jockey. The intent was never revealed to the psychiatrist or staff at the state facility. The patient believed she was under surveillance and that the wife's husband was responsible. After she shot and killed the husband, she received a revised diagnosis of "atypical psychosis." New medicine was administered and her condition improved. The wife contended that appellees failed to meet an appropriate standard of care in the diagnosis and treatment of the patient's mental condition. The court affirmed. First, the court held that there was no general common law duty to control the acts of another. Second, the court held that the duty to control should not be imposed solely because of the psychiatrist-patient relationship. Third, the relationship between appellees and the patient was completely bereft of any right, opportunity, or ability to control her conduct. Finally, the court held that policy considerations did not warrant the imposition of a duty to control, absent a showing of a specific threat to a specific victim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of the psychiatrist and the state mental health facility in the wife's suit alleging that they were liable for the negligent diagnosis and treatment of an outpatient that killed the wife's husband.

 

1067 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


In re Guardianship of Reyes


No. 2 CA-CV 5759


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


152 Ariz. 235; 731 P.2d 130; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 674



December 31, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PINAL COUNTY, Cause No. P-11455, Honorable E. D. McBryde, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged an order from the Superior Court of Pinal County (Arizona), which found his wife to be in need of a guardian, and consigned her to a nursing home, not at home with her husband. The husband argued that the Arizona guardianship laws were unconstitutional on the burden of proof requirement and the "incapacitated person" definition of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14-5101 was vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: A husband's wife was found to be in need of a guardianship and the appointed guardian consigned her to a nursing home, not at home with her husband. The hearing had been held under a preponderance of the evidence burden of proof standard, not clear and convincing evidence, as required in an involuntary civil commitment for treatment of mental illness hearing. The Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14-5101 definition of "incapacitated person" was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The court remanded the case for proceedings consistent with its opinion. The court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14-5101 "incapacitated person" was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad; therefore, it would define it to mean that a determination that an adult could not make "responsible decisions concerning his person" and was therefore incompetent, could be made only if the putative ward's decisionmaking process was so impaired that he was unable to care for his personal safety or unable to attend to and provide for such necessities as food, shelter, clothing, and medical care, without which physical injury or illness could occur. The court applied a clear and convincing burden of proof standard.


OUTCOME: The court defined the Arizona guardianship statute to bring it into constitutional compliance, applied a clear and convincing burden of proof standard, but denied a finding that the guardian's statutory powers were overbroad where the trial court could modify them; therefore, it remanded the case to the trial court for proceedings consistent with its opinion.

State v. Tyrrell


No. 2 CA-CR 4342


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


152 Ariz. 580; 733 P.2d 1163; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 719



December 30, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied March 10, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. CR-15486, Honorable Raner C. Collins, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which, in two separate jury trials, convicted him of one count of unlawful possession of a narcotic drug and of one count of unlawful transportation of marijuana. Defendant was sentenced to four years' probation and to five years' probation, to be served concurrently.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the prosecution engaged in improper cross-examination of defendant and "vouched" for the credibility of a State's witness during the first trial. He also contended that he was deprived of effective assistance of counsel when, during the second trial, his own lawyer elicited testimony from a police officer about an unrelated drug incident. Finally, defendant challenged the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3405(A)(3) because it violated the proscription against disproportionate penalties in U.S. Const. amend. VIII. The court affirmed defendant's conviction because there was no constitutional violation and there was no merit in his contentions. Defendant waived any error in the first trial be failing to raise an objection at trial. Further, the witness's testimony simply demonstrated that the witness had no motive to testify falsely. The court concluded that defendant was not prejudiced by his counsel's examination of a police officer about a "white powder residue" in defendant's car trunk. The evidence clearly supported the guilty verdict on the charge of unlawful transportation of marijuana.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Tucson v. Fleischman


No. 2 CA-SA 0452


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


152 Ariz. 269; 731 P.2d 634; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 672



December 26, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] SPECIAL ACTION PROCEEDINGS, Cause No. 223601, Relief Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner city sought special action relief from respondent judge's order entered in the Superior Court, Pima County (Arizona) denying the city's motion to dismiss the negligence action filed by the real parties in interest, claimant and her husband.


OVERVIEW: After the car in which she was riding was involved in an automobile accident, the claimant filed a negligence action against the city and the driver of the other vehicle. The city filed a motion to dismiss the claimant's action for failure to comply with the notice requirements of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-821(A), which was denied. The city sought special action relief. The court affirmed, in part, and remanded. The court held that although the city was a political subdivision and that the notice requirements set forth in § 12-821(A) applied to the claimant's action, dismissal under § 12-821(A) was not proper. The court held that the trial court erred in finding that the conduct of the claimant's counsel in failing to file the notice in a timely manner was due to excusable neglect. The court found that once the claimant told her attorney when the accident occurred, the attorney should have known of the claims statute and notice requirement and should have filed the claim before the expiration of the statutory period. The court allowed the action to proceed and held that the city was entitled to seek indemnity against the attorney if judgment was entered against it.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the matter for the trial court to make the determination that the conduct of the claimant's counsel in failing to timely file her claim constituted neglect and allowed the action to proceed.

State v. Rambeau


No. 1 CA-CR 9618


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


152 Ariz. 174; 730 P.2d 883; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 664



December 18, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County Cause No. CR-148898, The Honorable David L. Grounds, Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which found him not guilty of arson of an occupied structure by reason of insanity pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-502, found under § 13-502(D) that but for his insanity he would have been convicted and that his acts involved substantial risk of physical injury to another, and ordered him committed to the state hospital as required by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3994.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended on appeal that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3994 was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the order. The court concluded that § 13-3994(D), which had previously been found unconstitutional, was severable from the remainder of the statute and that § 13-3994(B), which provided a procedural safeguard to protect the acquittee's liberty interest, provided an adequate and constitutional basis for the issuance of the trial court's commitment order in the case. The court noted that the Supreme Court of the United States had held that a finding of not guilty by reason of insanity was sufficient foundation for automatic commitment. The court held that because automatic commitment of a defendant to a mental health agency, after a verdict of not guilty by reason of insanity, was constitutional, the trial court did not err in entering its order committing defendant to the state hospital.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court committing defendant to the state mental hospital after finding him not guilty of arson by reason of insanity.

 

1071 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Delk


No. 1 CA-CR 10280


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


153 Ariz. 70; 734 P.2d 612; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 724



December 18, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied March 17, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. LCA 27070.

The Honorable Howard V. Peterson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with violations of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692(A), (B). He entered into a plea agreement under which he agreed to plead guilty to driving while intoxicated in violations of § 28-692(A). The other charges were dismissed and the lower court imposed an agreed upon alternative sentence. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) affirmed the conviction and sentence, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant conceded he had no right to a plea bargain, but argued that he had a procedural right to plea bargain, and that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692(C) unconstitutionally infringed upon that right. He argued that because the judicial branch of government had the power to promulgate rules of procedure, pursuant to Ariz. Const. art. 6, § 5, it was a violation of the separation of powers doctrine for the legislature to pass a law which infringed upon plea bargaining in a driving while intoxicated case. The State argued that defendant had no standing to challenge the constitutionality of § 28-692(C). The court agreed and held that only those who were injured by an unconstitutional statute could object to its constitutionality. The court held that defendant was not injured. Nothing appeared in the record to indicate that the prosecutor had any desire to offer a plea agreement different than the one offered and accepted by defendant. The court also held that defendant had no right to a plea agreement, and without such a right, he had no personal stake in any unconstitutional infringement by a statute upon the discretion of the prosecutor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Tocco


No. 1 CA-CR 7480


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


156 Ariz. 110; 750 P.2d 868; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 777



December 2, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Appellant's Motion for Reconsideration Granted and Opinion Modified January 15, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. CR-129027, The Honorable Robert S. Hertzberg, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed count-one of an amended information that charged defendant with leading organized crime, a class two felony, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2308, arguing that the statute was not vague.


OVERVIEW: The state appealed from the dismissal of count-one of an amended information that charged defendant with leading organized crime in violation of § 13-2308. The trial court determined that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. Defendant argued that the statute did not adequately define the term "criminal syndicate" even though it was an underlying element of the crime of leading organized crime. The court reversed and held that § 13-2308 was constitutionally valid. A commonsense reading of the statute demonstrated a legislative intent to punish only those persons who cooperated with a combination of individuals or businesses with the intent to assist them in violating Arizona's felony statute on a continuing basis. The statute did not reach any constitutionally protected conduct, and its prescriptions were easily understood by persons of ordinary intelligence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of count-one of the state's amended information that charged defendant with leading organized crime, and remanded the case for further proceedings that were consistent with the court's opinion.

Browning v. Corbett


No. 2 CA-CIV 5776


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


153 Ariz. 74; 734 P.2d 1030; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 732



November 20, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied January 6, 1987. Review Denied March 24, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. 224681, Honorable Leslie Miller, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen challenged the order of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which awarded summary judgment to appellees, county and state officials, and dismissed the citizen's class action for an injunction and accounting on the basis that the mandatory marriage dissolution filing fee paid under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-311.01(E) violated the Arizona Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The citizen was required to pay a fee under § 25-311.01(E) when he filed for divorce. The citizen paid the fee and filed a class action that alleged the fee violated the Arizona Constitutional guarantees of equal protection and due process, and the prohibition on special legislation. The superior court awarded summary judgment to appellees, and dismissed the citizen's action. The citizen appealed and the court affirmed. The court found that the fee was subject to the rational basis standard of review and that the fee funded domestic violence shelters and child abuse prevention and treatment, which were legitimate state interests and reasonably related to the fee payment for marriage dissolution. The court noted that the funds were also funded from marriage licenses and that the dissolution filing fee was not the sole source of funding. The court rejected the citizen's citation to other state constitutions because Arizona's Constitution lacked comparable provisions. The court found that the § 25-311.01(E) was not special legislation but one rationally related legitimate state purposes and the fee payers were those reasonably calculated to benefit the most from the funds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the superior court, which had awarded summary judgment to appellees and dismissed the citizen's class action state constitutional challenge to a mandatory court filing fee.

Picture Rocks Fire Dist. v. Pima County


No. 2 CA-CV 5762


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


152 Ariz. 442; 733 P.2d 639; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 706



November 18, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied February 24, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. 225451, Honorable William L. Scholl, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, fire districts and the taxpayers, challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which held that 1985 Ariz. Sess. Laws, 1st Reg. Sess. ch. 278, was constitutional, finding in favor of appellees, Pima County and its officials. The issues were whether the statute impaired contracts, was a local or special law, and violated equal protection or privileges and immunities under the federal and Arizona constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Appellants argued that a state senator's deposition, offered as evidence of both the legislature's intent and individual legislators' mental processes, was erroneously excluded at trial and was necessary to their claim that the statute was an unconstitutional local or special law. The court held there was no error in excluding the evidence because a single legislator was incompetent to testify about legislative intent in passing a law. The court noted that the parties' agreed statement of facts made it unnecessary to make findings on undisputed matters. The court rejected the argument that the statute violated the constitutional prohibition against impairing contracts in U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 because the revenue lost by withdrawals from the fire district might make it unable to meet certain contractual obligations. The court pointed out that the statute did not change any obligation to the contracts. The court concluded that the statute affected neither elections nor assessment and collection of taxes, and the legislature could have concluded that the County was the only area that needed immediate relief from abusive practices by fire districts, so there was a rational basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision declaring the statute constitutional.

Bussanich v. Douglas


No. 2 CA-CV 5780


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


152 Ariz. 447; 733 P.2d 644; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 707

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff coworker sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which granted defendant fellow employee's motion for summary judgment based on the Arizona Constitution and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1022. The trial court held that the coworker's exclusive remedy was for the receipt of workmen's compensation benefits. The coworker filed a negligence action against her fellow employee for damages for personal injuries.


OVERVIEW: Both parties were public employees working for a state mental health agency. During an "in-service" workshop on handguns, the fellow employee was negligent in his handling of a firearm that discharged and seriously injured the coworker. The fellow employee's motion for summary judgment was based on § 23-1022 and the 1980 amendment to Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 8. Stat. § 23-1022 was unconstitutional as applied to public employees. The court also rejected the argument that the constitutional amendment did not authorize the legislature to enact any statutes limiting public employees who had been negligently injured by a fellow employee in the course of their employment to compensation benefits. The court found that the intention of the legislature and the people who voted for the amendment was to bar double recoveries by all injured workers covered by the Workmen's Compensation Act, whether they were public or private employees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Plowman v. Arizona State Liquor Bd.


No. 2 CA-CIV 5735


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


152 Ariz. 331; 732 P.2d 222; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 688



October 9, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied November 17, 1986. Review Denied January 27, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. 226198, Hon. J. Richard Hannah, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Arizona State Liquor Board and the Arizona Department of Liquor Licenses and Control, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which reversed the Board's finding that appellee licensees committed numerous violations of Ariz. Rev. Stat. tit. 4 and which held that the revocation of the licensees' license was excessive. The trial court also remanded the case to the Board.


OVERVIEW: The Board found that the licensees violated Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 4-244(9), (14), (23); 4-241(A), as well as Ariz. Admin. Code 4-15-234 (1982). Most of the violations involved the presence of underage patrons and underage drinking. The Board recommended revocation of the licensees' license, but the trial court held that revocation was an excessive penalty. The trial court also reversed all of the Board's findings on the ground that reputation and hearsay evidence was admitted. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred as to all but two of the counts against the licensees. The Board's decision as to numerous counts was supported by the evidence, and the trial court could not reweigh the evidence or substitute its findings for that of the Board. Rather, judicial review was limited to deciding whether the Board's action was illegal, arbitrary, capricious, or an abuse of discretion. The court rejected the trial court's conclusion that the introduction of some reputation evidence and some "unreliable" hearsay affected the licensees' rights. However, the evidence might have resulted in an injustice with respect to the penalty recommended by the Board.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment as to only two counts. The court otherwise reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the Board for the imposition of a penalty.

Barsema v. Susong


No. 2 CA-CV 5794


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


156 Ariz. 304; 751 P.2d 964; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 779



October 9, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted March 17, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY, Cause No. C500504, Honorable Paul W. LaPrade, Judge (Deceased).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which entered judgment on a jury verdict in favor of appellee physicians, and from a denial of the patient's motion for new trial by the superior court.


OVERVIEW: The court had to determine whether the trial court erred in not allowing the patient to demonstrate a physician's agency, bias, and prejudice by cross-examining him about his employment relationship with an his insurer, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-569. On appeal, the court held that Ariz. R. Evid. 411, Ariz. R. Sup. Ct. 17A, and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-569, were clearly in conflict. The court held that evidence of the defendant physician's bias, interest, and agency would clearly have been admissible under Ariz. R. Evid. 411, whereas this evidence was clearly inadmissible under the statute. The court held that under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-569, evidence of a financial interest in the operation of a health care insurer could not be received in evidence for any purpose no matter what type of financial interest the witness possesses in the company. Because the court found that § 12-569 could not be reconciled with the supreme court's evidentiary rule 411, the court held that the statute was unconstitutional. However, the court held that any error in the court's refusal to allow cross-examination of the physician regarding his employment relationship with his insurer was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which entered judgment on a jury verdict in favor of physicians and denied a patient's motion for a new trial. The court held that a statute making evidence of a financial interest in the operation of a health care insurer inadmissible was unconstitutional, but the trial court's error in refusing to permit certain cross-examination was harmless.

 

1079 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Marriott Corp. v. Industrial Comm'n


No. 1 CA-IC 3521


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


156 Ariz. 74; 750 P.2d 17; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 773



October 7, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Special Action -- Industrial Commission, ICA Claim NO. 560-84-4975, Carrier No. 152-82214-BG, Administrative Law Judge James A. Overholt.



DISPOSITION: AWARD AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent claimant filed a request for a hearing to protest respondent Industrial Commission of Arizona's average monthly wage determination. Petitioner employer also requested a hearing to review the determination. The Commission subsequently entered an award granting the claimant's request to withdraw her request for a hearing and dismissing the employer's request for a hearing. The employer filed a special action to review the award.


OVERVIEW: The claimant injured her arm while working for the employer. After the Commission issued an average monthly wage determination, the claimant timely requested a hearing. The claimant asserted that the Commission's determination was too low. The employer subsequently determined that the determination overstated the claimant's average monthly wage. Accordingly, the employer also requested a hearing. The next day, the claimant filed a written withdrawal of her hearing request. The Commission allowed the claimant to withdraw her request, but dismissed the employer's request for a hearing as untimely. The affect was to finalize the Commission's original determination. On review, the court held that although the employer had a right to request a hearing under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-947, the request was untimely because it was not made within the statute's 90-day period. The claimant's timely request of a hearing did not protect the employer from the operation of the 90-day period. The Commission properly allowed the claimant to withdraw her request for a hearing because the employer failed to exercise due diligence in detecting and raising the issue of the overstated wage determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commission's award.

 

1080 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Brown Wholesale Elec. Co. v. H.S. Lastar Co.


No. 1 CA-CIV 7735


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


152 Ariz. 90; 730 P.2d 267; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 635



September 2, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied December 5, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-448269, The Honorable Bernard J. Dougherty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a contractor and its surety, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona). The lower court granted the motion for summary judgment of appellee supplier in its claim on a contractor's license bond for recovery for materials it had furnished on a public works construction project.


OVERVIEW: A supplier brought an action against a contractor and its surety to recover for materials provided on a public works project. The lower court granted summary judgment to the supplier. The contractor and surety sought review, claiming that amendments to Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 32-1101 and 32-1152 32-1101 prevented the supplier's recovery by limiting construction bonds to residential construction. On review, the court considered whether the supplier acquired a vested right in the bond because it delivered materials to the contractor prior to the effective date of the amendments, even though the materials were not used until after the effective date. The court concluded that the legislature did not require the materials to be used before the cause of action would arise because it provided for the limitations period to run from the time of delivery of goods. However, the court also concluded that failure to use the materials in residential construction as required by the amended statute was a condition subsequent that defeated the supplier's right of recovery. The court held that the supplier's rights on nonresidential claims were not vested at the time when the statute was amended.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that summary judgment was improperly granted to the supplier. The court reversed and remanded the case for entry of judgment in favor of the contractor and its surety.

 

1081 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Ranch 57 v. Yuma


Nos. 1 CA-CIV 8150, 1 CA-CIV 8631


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


152 Ariz. 218; 731 P.2d 113; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 665



September 2, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 8, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yuma County, Cause No. C-50037, The Honorable William W. Nabours, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner brought an action against appellee city and county (the government), alleging an improper regulatory taking of his property without just compensation in violation of U.S. Const. Amend V and Ariz. Const. art. II, § 17. The Superior Court of Yuma County (Arizona) granted summary judgment in favor of the government. The owner appealed the dismissal of its cause of action.


OVERVIEW: The landowner contended that the zoning ordinance that allowed the government to take his property constituted an unconstitutional exercise of police power. The landowner further argued that the condemnation of the property violated U.S. Const. Amend V and Ariz. Const. art. II, § 17. The court found that the condemnation of the landowner's property was constitutional. In so holding, the court found that (1) Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-550, which set a four-year statute of limitations for actions other than for recovery of real property for which no other limitation had been prescribed, was applicable to a regulatory takings case involving municipal and county governments; (2) the zoning ordinance that allowed the government to condemn the landowner's property for airport use was a valid exercise of municipal police power; (3) the condemnation of the land did not violate the U. S. or Arizona constitutions; and (4) the trial court properly found that the government had not deprived the landowner of all economically viable use of his property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's ruling granting summary judgment in favor of the government.

 

1082 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


James v. Phoenix Gen. Hosp.


Nos. 1 CA-CIV 8251, CV-86-0535-PR


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


154 Ariz. 588; 744 P.2d 689; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 760



August 28, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-499758, The Honorable Howard V. Peterson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant survivors, citing Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 12-564(A), 12-542, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, hospital and doctors, in the survivors' wrongful death action.


OVERVIEW: The survivors' decedent died over two years after having surgery, allegedly of complications from the surgery, and the action had been brought over two years after that. The survivors contended on appeal that the trial court erred in failing to hold that the three-year limitation period for medical malpractice actions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-564(A) did not start to run until the decedent's death. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held that both § 12-564(A) and the two-year wrongful death statute of limitations, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-542, were applicable to the claim, and that the survivors were entitled to the benefit of the longer of the two periods. The court held that the three-year period in § 12-564(A) began to run from the date of "injury" to the decedent around the time of the surgery, and rejected the contention that the "injury" was that suffered by the survivors upon his death. The court noted that § 12-542 began to run on the date of death, and held that the suit was time barred by statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the hospital and doctors.

 

1083 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Deskins


No. 2 CA-CR 4279


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


152 Ariz. 209; 731 P.2d 104; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 678



August 19, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 6, 1987.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. CR-15886, Honorable Michael Alfred, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which convicted them, upon a jury verdict, of three counts of negligent child abuse in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3623(C).


OVERVIEW: Defendants were the parents of three minor children. At trial, the jury heard evidence that the children lived in unsanitary conditions, including a leaking portable toilet; that they slept in close proximity to animals which appeared to be diseased and scrap metal automobile parts, tin cans and other discarded items; and that the children, who were kept barefoot, were not protected from scrap lumber with protruding nails and were exposed to the animal feces. In addition, there was evidence that defendants were given one week in which to make changes that were indicated by a caseworker, but failed or refused to do so. The jury convicted defendants of negligent child abuse. Defendants argued that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3623(C) was unconstitutionally void for vagueness and was overbroad because the conduct of endangerment was not defined. The court held that term "endangered" was not unconstitutionally vague and neither was it overbroad. The State had a rational basis for prohibiting defendants from allowing their children to live in conditions that endangered their health. Defendants had fair notice of their legal duty as parents and of the conduct that was statutorily proscribed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Griffin


No. 2 CA-CR 4136


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


154 Ariz. 481; 744 P.2d 8; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 759



August 19, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. CR-14554, Honorable Gilbert Veliz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County, Arizona, which convicted him of attempted second-degree murder and sentenced him to 21 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted second-degree murder and aggravated assault. He argued that his aggravated 21-year sentence for attempted second-degree murder was illegal because it was one year greater than what he could have received for second-degree murder. The court agreed in part and remanded for resentencing. The court held that a sentencing scheme providing a greater maximum sentence for attempted murder than for murder violated the third prong of the proportionality test, which compared the sentence imposed to the sentences imposed on other criminals in the same jurisdiction. The court held that any sentence to a term of imprisonment for less than 20 years, the maximum sentence for second-degree murder, would not violate the proportionality requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and remanded for resentencing.

State v. Pacheco


No. 2 CA-CR 4026-2


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


152 Ariz. 85; 730 P.2d 262; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 645



July 24, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied December 16, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. CR-13293, Honorable Robert O. Roylston, Retired Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which resentenced him following a remand from the court. He sought a reduction of the sentence on Eighth Amendment grounds.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of criminal damage for damaging a family member's car while on probation. He admitted two prior felony convictions and was sentenced to 3.75 years' imprisonment. Probation was revoked and defendant was sentenced to a presumptive term of five years in prison. The court held that imposition of the sentence was not cruel and unusual. Under Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-701(B)(5) and 13-604.02(B), 3.75 years was the minimum sentence possible for the criminal damage crime committed while defendant was on probation. Section 13-604.02(B) also required the sentence to be consecutive to the sentence imposed on the probation revocation. The court held that the factors used to determine whether a sentence was unconstitutionally excessive supported defendant's sentence. The offense involved violence and was sufficiently grave to warrant enhanced punishment. The sentence was not too harsh, as defendant was a repeat offender. The sentence was proportional to sentences imposed for similar crimes in the jurisdiction. Finally, the classification of the offense by the dollar amount of damages did not result in disproportionality with other jurisdictions.


OUTCOME: The court modified the date from which the sentence ran, modified the amount of presentence credit given, and affirmed the judgment as modified.
