Stuart v. Insurance Co. of N. Am.


No. 1 CA-CIV 7805


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


152 Ariz. 78; 730 P.2d 255; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 628



July 15, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-461494, The Honorable David L. Grounds, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant estate, surviving husband, and children sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), granting summary judgment to appellee insurer in an action involving uninsured motorist coverage.


OVERVIEW: The wife was killed in an automobile accident. Two weeks before the accident, the Arizona legislature enacted Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 20-259.01 giving insureds the option of increasing their uninsured motorist coverage to the policy limits. After the accident, the husband sent the insurer a check requesting that the uninsured motorist coverage on his policy be increased retroactively to the policy limits. The insurer applied the check to the policy renewal period and the estate brought suit against the insurer. The trial court found for the insurer and the court affirmed. The court noted that the cardinal rule of statutory construction was to ascertain the statute's meaning and the legislature's intent. Reading the statute as a whole, the court concluded that the insurer was under no obligation to notify its insureds that they had the option to increase uninsured motorist coverage. The court also held that the estate failed to argue its breach of contract claim and that the claim was therefore waived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the insurer but denied the insurer's request for attorney's fees.

Allen v. Industrial Comm'n


No. 1 CA-IC 3412


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


152 Ariz. 403; 733 P.2d 288; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 697



July 15, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Special Action - Industrial Commission, ICA Claim No. 454-62-6461, Carrier No. 029715, John B. Galloway, Administrative Law Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought a special action review of a decision of respondent, the Industrial Commission of Arizona, which entered an award that denied compensation to the employee on the basis of a lack of jurisdiction, in favor of respondents, the employer and its carrier. The administrative law judge (ALJ) found that the Commission had no jurisdiction to consider the claim, which had been filed more than one year after the injury occurred.


OVERVIEW: The employee claimed that he injured his back when he fell off a ladder in the course of his employment. More than a year later, he filed a claim for compensation for back surgery, which he alleged was causally related to the industrial incident. The carrier raised the issue of untimely filing, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1061(D). A hearing limited to the issue of jurisdiction was held and the ALJ found that the employee did not fall within any of the statutory exceptions to the one-year filing limitation. On appeal, the employee argued that the 1980 statutory amendments to § 23-1061(A) violated Ariz. Const. art. XVIII, § 8 as interpreted by the Arizona Supreme Court. The court affirmed. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1061(A) expressly provided that, subject to the exceptions set forth in the statute, neither the Commission nor any court would have jurisdiction to consider a claim that was not timely filed. The doctrine that the Commission somehow possessed inherent constitutional powers, which were not subject to legislative restriction, was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Commission.

 

1088 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Martin


No. 1 CA-CIV 7959


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


156 Ariz. 440; 752 P.2d 1026; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 778



July 15, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County, Cause No. C-41378, The Honorable James Hancock, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wife filed an action in the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona) seeking dissolution of her marriage to defendant husband. In dividing the property, the trial court determined that a trust, some securities, and the husband's salary earned while the parties were separated were community property and awarded the wife one-half. The trial court also granted the wife a money settlement and spousal support. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: During the marriage, the husband became the beneficiary of a one-fifth interest in a trust. He commingled the income from the trust with marital funds and purchased an additional two-fifths interest in the trust and oil company stock. Husband and wife separated. He lived in their marital residence in California and she lived in their retirement home in Arizona. On appeal, the court found that the one-fifth share in the trust was separate property, but that the two-fifths shares in the trust and the oil company stock were purchased with commingled funds and were community property. As an issue of first impression, the court determined that Arizona community property law governed a dissolution action filed in Arizona, even where one spouse was the resident of another state. The husband's earnings while the parties were separated were community property. The trial court erred in granting the wife monetary settlements. The trial court exceeded its authority in considering assets no longer in existence at the time of dissolution. The trial court did not err in granting the wife spousal support.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part. The trial court erred in granting the wife the monetary settlements. Upon remand the trial court was to consider whether the spousal support was sufficient based upon a division of property which did not include the monetary settlements.

State v. Bowling


No. 2 CA-CR 4048


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


151 Ariz. 230; 726 P.2d 1099; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 579



July 10, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied September 30, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PINAL COUNTY, Cause No. CR-11376, Honorable Robert R. Bean, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Pinal County (Arizona), which convicted defendant of second degree murder and two counts of aggravated assault and which imposed a 15 year sentence for the murder, a 12 year sentence for the first assault, and a term of seven and one half years for the second assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his wife separated. The wife developed a relationship with another man and was helping him move when defendant followed them and another man into a trailer park. Defendant then shot the wife's friend, threaten to kill the wife, and pointed his gun at the other man. Furthermore, challenges to grand jury testimony were not reviewable on appeal. As for defendant's contention that he had newly discovered evidence, the court could not review his claim because the proper action was to file a petition for post-conviction relief.

1090 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Phoenix v. Campbell


No. 1 CA-CIV 8561


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


151 Ariz. 497; 728 P.2d 1247; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 649



July 10, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied August 8, 1986. Review Denied December 2, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-434987, The Honorable Barry G. Silverman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant condemnees appealed from the order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which denied the condemnees' application for an award of compound interest at a rate in excess of the 10 percent per annum provided by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1201(A) on the award to be paid over time made to the condemnees in petitioner city's eminent domain action.


OVERVIEW: The city brought an eminent domain action to take the condemnees' land. At trial, the condemnees produced expert testimony on the rate of return a prudent investor would have achieved with the condemnees' resources, to support their application for compound interest in excess of the rate in § 44-1201(A). The jury awarded the fair market value of the property to the condemnees, but the superior court denied the excess interest and refused the compounding of interest. The condemnees appealed. The court affirmed. The court found that the income bracket of the condemnees was irrelevant, because there was a goal of uniformity in treatment of condemnees and the financial status of the condemnee was an inappropriate test for the constitutionality of § 44-1201(A). The court found that the prudent person investor standard was limited to the restriction of obligations comparable to the condemnor even when that was not the highest yield. The statutory interest rate of § 44-1201(A) was presumed reasonable and compounding of interest was not an element of the constitutional right to just compensation. The superior court had not erred in denying compound interest in excess of § 44-1201(A).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the superior court, which denied the condemnees' application for compound interest in excess of the statutory rate as compensation for the city's taking of the condemnees' land.

Fund Manager, Pub. Safety Personnel Retirement Sys. v. Phoenix Police Dep't Pub. Safety Personnel Retirement Sys. Bd.


No. 1 CA-CIV 8314


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


151 Ariz. 487; 728 P.2d 1237; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 652



July 1, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied December 2, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County Cause No. C-504991 The Honorable Paul W. LaPrade, Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the fund manager of a retirement system (fund manager), sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee injured party, holding that appellee retirement system board (board) was correct in awarding the injured party accidental disability benefits.


OVERVIEW: When the injured party was hired, state law provided that he would receive an accidental disability pension if an injury incurred in the performance of his job prevented him from performing his regularly assigned duties. Nine years later, the law was amended to provide for a disability pension only if an employee was unable to perform a reasonable range of duties within his department. Several months later, the injured party was injured while on duty. The board awarded the injured party accidental disability benefits, applying the definition of accidental disability in effect when the injured party was hired. The fund manager petitioned the board for rehearing, asserting that the injured party's eligibility should have been determined pursuant to the 1980 amendment to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 38-842(1). The board upheld its decision, and the fund manager appealed to the trial court. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of the injured party. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that the right to an accidental disability pension did not vest until the contingent event of injury occurred; therefore, the amended version of § 38-842(1) applied.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order, which granted summary judgment in favor of the injured party, was reversed and remanded.

Sahf v. Lake Havasu City Ass'n for Retarded & Handicapped


No. 1 CA-CIV 8488


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


150 Ariz. 50; 721 P.2d 1177; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 486



June 17, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-516221, The Honorable Rudolph J. Gerber, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted appellee group home's motion to dismiss and appellee State's motion for summary judgment. The guardian brought an action on behalf of the ward, her son, and in her individual capacity for the ward's personal injuries that resulted from negligent care.


OVERVIEW: The ward had been mentally retarded since birth and was adjudged an incapacitated person and placed under the guardianship of his mother. The trial court held that the group home was not a licensed health care provider; that the two-year statute of limitations for ordinary negligence, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-542, was applicable; and that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-502 did not toll the period of limitations because the ward had a guardian. The court found that appointment of a guardian for an insane person did not constitute removal of the insane person's disability for purposes of the tolling statute, § 12-502; thus, as to the ward, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-542 was not a bar to the litigation. However, the court concluded that the guardian's individual claims were not tolled. The court found that the group home was not a "licensed health care provider," because it did not have a license from the Arizona Department of Health Services. Thus, the court concluded that the group home was not subject to suit for medical malpractice, and the guardian's individual claims against the group home and the State were barred by § 12-542.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court dismissing that portion of the complaint seeking recovery by the guardian in her individual capacity against the group home and the State. The court reversed the judgments in favor of the group home and the State on the claims of the ward brought on his behalf by the guardian and remanded the matter to the trial court for proceedings in accordance with its opinion.

Tiffany v. Arizona Interscholastic Ass'n


No. 1 CA-CIV 8359


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


151 Ariz. 134; 726 P.2d 231; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 573



June 12, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied October 7, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-493565, The Honorable B. Michael Dann, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant interscholastic association appealed an order from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which held that defendant acted unreasonably, capriciously, and arbitrarily in failing to exercise its discretion in considering plaintiff student's waiver from disqualification from athletic competition due to age and that plaintiff had a property interest in participating in high school athletics.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff student filed a suit against defendant interscholastic association requesting that defendant be enjoined from disqualifying plaintiff from interscholastic athletic competition and that defendant's actions be declared unconstitutional as a denial of due process. The lower court granted a preliminary injunction and found that defendant acted unreasonably in considering plaintiff's waiver from disqualification and that plaintiff had a sufficient liberty interest in high school athletics so as to have rendered defendant's denial a constitutional violation. The court affirmed the lower court's order in part and reversed in part. The court held that defendant did act arbitrarily in exercising its discretion in denying plaintiff's waiver because although defendant's bylaws allowed for a waiver of disqualification upon the showing of hardship, defendant also had a policy of not making any exceptions to an age eligibility requirement under which plaintiff took exception. However, the court held that friendship, discipline, and regulation involved in playing varsity sports were all insufficient to assert a cognizable interest under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for constitutional protection.


OUTCOME: An order finding that defendant interscholastic association failed to properly exercise discretion and violated plaintiff student's constitutional right by disqualifying him from interscholastic sports due to his age was affirmed in part on the grounds that a policy of not making any exceptions to age eligibility was contrary to bylaws allowing for waiver and reversed in part because plaintiff failed to assert a cognizable interest.

 

1095 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Superior Court


No. 2 CA-CIV 5598


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


155 Ariz. 403; 747 P.2d 564; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 768



June 2, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County, Cause No. 223752, Honorable Jack T. Arnold, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) that ordered a preliminary hearing to be held on defendant's motion to suppress evidence of her refusal to submit to an intoxilyzer test following her arrest for driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for driving while intoxicated (DWI) in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692(A). Following her arrest, police officers asked that she submit to an intoxilyzer test. Defendant refused, and the Arizona Motor Vehicle Division (MVD) suspended her license for 12 months pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-691(D). The MVD later reinstated her license after receiving evidence that defendant was psychologically unable to comprehend the implied consent law warning given to her by police. Prior to defendant's trial on the DWI charge, defendant moved to suppress evidence of her refusal to take the intoxilyzer test. The trial court ordered a preliminary hearing to be held on the motion, and the state appealed. The court reversed and remanded. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692(K) provided that the issue of refusal was to be an issue of fact to be determined by the trier of fact in all cases. As such, the trial court only was permitted to hold a preliminary hearing on the issue of whether there was an issue of refusal. However, here, there was no issue of refusal because defendant admitted that she refused to take the test; she only contested the voluntariness of her refusal.


OUTCOME: The judgment ordering a preliminary hearing on defendant's motion to suppress evidence of her refusal to take an intoxilyzer test following her arrest for driving while intoxicated was reversed and remanded.

Borja v. Phoenix Gen. Hosp.

Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B

Defendants challenged the denial of their request for attorneys' fees.

The court affirmed the denial of defendants' request for attorneys' fees, holding that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 12-341.01 was inapplicable to this type of tort action.

Cause No. C-526859.

Honorable Conrad W. Sanders, Judge Pro Tempore and Honorable Robert C. Broomfield, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) in which the court found that appellant violated the Arizona Securities Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1801 et seq., and the Consumer Fraud Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1521 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of an order finding that appellant violated the Arizona Securities Act (ASA), Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1801 et seq., and the Consumer Fraud Act (CFA), Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1521 et seq., arising out of the sale of unregistered gold and silver in the form of investment contracts. Appellee alleged that appellant made numerous deceptive acts and material misrepresentations. The court affirmed, holding that appellant violated the ASA by selling unregistered securities and the CFA by failing to disclose material information. The court held that the investment contracts constituted securities which were required to be registered. The court further held that appellant violated the CFA by failing to disclose that appellant's sale staff lacked expertise and certain background information regarding the sale of securities and by misrepresenting that the invested silver was being stored when the commodity was never purchased.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment because appellant violated the Arizona Securities Act and the Consumer Fraud Act by selling unregistered securities and by failing to disclose material information regarding appellant's sale staff and the invested silver.

 

1099 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Acolla v. Peralta


No. 2 CA-CIV 5671


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


150 Ariz. 35; 721 P.2d 1162; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 496



April 10, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-478448, Honorable John J. Trombino, Judge Pro Tempore.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review from the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which awarded plaintiff judgment on plaintiff's complaint alleging fraud and violations of the Arizona Racketeering Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-2301-2317, following a loan brokerage deal.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought a fraud and RICO action after defendants promised to broker a loan that never was made. Defendants sought review from the judgment of the lower court, contending they were entitled to a new trial because of the Arizona Racketeering Act (RICO) was unconstitutional and because the jury instructions were erroneous. Finding no merit to the defendants' contentions, the court affirmed the judgment of the lower court. The court held that defendants they had no standing to raise constitutional issues predicated on the argument the RICO act made the charges a criminal proceeding. The court found that defendants were not entitled to the criminal due process protections because the trial was civil, not criminal. The court noted that the statute specifically created the civil claim which was brought against the defendants. The court also found that defendants raised no objection to any of the jury instructions and failed to ask for an instruction on the crime of scheme or artifice to defraud. The court therefore found that any error was waived by defendants' failure to raise the issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court which entered a jury verdict against the defendants.

 

1100 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Sanchez-O'Brien Minerals Corp. v. State


No. 1 CA-CIV 7442


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


149 Ariz. 258; 717 P.2d 937; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 453; 90 Oil & Gas Rep. 23



March 27, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the County of Maricopa Cause No. C-420468 The Honorable William T. Moroney, Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Arizona State Land Department and a subsequent lessee, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which declared void the Department's order rejecting appellee lessee's "surrender and refile" application for non-competitive oil and gas leases. The trial court also ordered the Department to issue leases to the lessee and awarded attorney's fees to the lessee.


OVERVIEW: The lessee acquired oil and gas leases from the Department. Because such leases were non-renewable, the Department acquiesced in a "surrender and refile" procedure whereby a lessee could surrender its lease before its expiration date and refile for a new lease. Before the effective date of legislation raising the rental rates for such leases, the lessee surrendered its leases and filed new applications. The Department refused to issue new leases except at the higher rental rate. When the lessee refused to agree to the new rate, the Department issued leases to the subsequent lessee. The lessee filed suit, and the trial court found in its favor. On appeal, the court rejected the Department's contention that the lessee failed to exhaust its administrative remedies. However, the court held that the "surrender and refile" procedure was invalid because it contravened the statutory goal of requiring lessees to actively seek and produce oil and gas on State lands. The fact that the Department had operated under the "surrender and refile" procedure for over 24 years did not affect the court's decision. The lessee was not entitled to attorney's fees under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-341.01(A).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and denied the lessee's request for attorney's fees.

 

1101 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mohr


No. 1 CA-CR 8837


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


150 Ariz. 564; 724 P.2d 1233; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 544



March 20, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied April 29, 1986. Review Denied September 9, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County, Cause No. CR-11113, The Honorable James Hancock, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona) in which he was convicted of one count of trafficking in stolen property, a violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2307(A), and one count of theft, a violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1802(A)(1).


OVERVIEW: The issue on appeal was whether the jury was improperly instructed as to the inference to be drawn from possession of recently stolen property. At the close of evidence, the trial judge instructed the jury that that proof that defendant was in possession of property recently stolen, unless satisfactorily explained, gave rise to an inference that defendant in possession of the property was aware of the risk that it had been stolen or in some way participated in its theft. Defendant raised a variety of objections to the instruction. The instruction was substantially identical to the statutory inference created by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2305(1). The court held that the instruction created an unconstitutional burden-shifting presumption. The jury was instructed that proof that defendant possessed recently stolen property, "gave rise to the inference" that he was aware of the risk that it had been stolen, unless he satisfactorily explained his possession of the property. The instruction unconstitutionally shifted the burden of proof to defendant on an element of each offense--trafficking and theft--in violation of the principles enunciated in previous case law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

 

1102 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


First Baptist Church v. Arizona State Liquor Bd.


No. 2 CA-CIV 5655


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


149 Ariz. 20; 716 P.2d 81; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 437



March 14, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY, Cause No. C-468160, Hon. Armando DeLeon.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an applicant for a retailer's liquor license (retailer) and the Arizona State Liquor Board, challenged an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) which, relying on Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-207, overturned the Board's administrative decision approving the retailer's application despite the opposition of appellee, a neighboring church. Because the license had been issued, the order was stayed pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: When the Board approved the license application despite the church's opposition, the church appealed. The superior court then reversed the Board's ruling, finding no substantial evidence to support it and ruling that the Board acted arbitrarily and capriciously and abused its discretion. On appeal, the court found both that the Board had acted illegally and that § 4-207(A)(1) was unconstitutional. On the first point, the court held that because the proposed establishment was within 300 feet of the church, the Board could not have lawfully considered measurements from other beginning and ending points, its ruling improperly disregarded the evidence, and its decision completely disregarded legislative requirements. On the second point, the court held that subsection (A)(1) was unconstitutional because it gave veto power over the issuance of the liquor license to the church in violation of the Establishment Clause. However, because subsection (A)(1) was properly severed from the balance of the statute, the court held that a new hearing was necessary in order to determine whether the city council, absent the influence of the church's veto, wished to approve the license.


OUTCOME: The court held that to the extent it allowed the church to exercise a veto over the license, the statute was unconstitutional. It ordered that the matter be submitted to local government authorities once again for a new hearing. If the local government authorities recommended approval, the existing license was to be validated. Otherwise, it was to be rescinded.

 

1103 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Leonard


No. 1 CA-CR 8658


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


151 Ariz. 1; 725 P.2d 493; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 560



March 13, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied June 4, 1986. Review Denied September 16, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County Cause CR-10929 The Honorable James B. Sult, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona), which found defendant guilty of driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor with two prior convictions within a period of 60 months.


OVERVIEW: After a police officer observed defendant's erratic driving, defendant was stopped and arrested. The jury found him guilty of driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor with two prior convictions within a period of 60 months, and on appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court determined that the trial court had the power to retroactively apply a procedural rule that dealt with the foundation for admitting defendant's breath tests into evidence. Jurors did not receive information from an outside source when a juror narrated his personal experiences with drunk driving incidents. Any error in admitting a horizontal nystagmus test was harmless considering the amount of admissible evidence that showed that defendant was intoxicated. The police did not unreasonably interfere with defendant's ability to make phone calls to find a physician to administer an independent blood alcohol test because defendant was allowed to make several phone calls before he was transferred to another facility. Although the trial court erred in not accepting defendant's stipulation that he had two prior convictions, it was harmless error in light of the overwhelming evidence against him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for the crime of driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor with two prior convictions within a period of 60 months.

 

1104 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Continental Tel. Co. v. Blazzard


No. 2 CA-CIV 5605


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


149 Ariz. 1; 716 P.2d 62; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 426



February 20, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 4, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF NAVAJO COUNTY, Cause No. C-18847, Honorable Edward L. Dawson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee phone company filed suit against appellant litigants for interfering with their attempt to lay buried cable on the litigants' property. The litigants counterclaimed, seeking damages for breach of contract and for trespass. The litigants filed a third party claim against the county. In a jury trial, the Superior Court of Navajo County (Arizona) awarded monetary damages to each party that cancelled one another out. The litigants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The phone company installed underground cable across the property in 1978. The phone company argued they had authority to enter and lay the cable by way of an easement from 1957. In mid-1980, the phone company obtained a permit from the county to work on a public right of way to lay a second underground cable 33 feet off the center line of the road across the litigant's property. The litigants blocked the laying of cable. The trial court awarded partial summary judgment, holding the road was a public highway and the county had authority to grant franchises for utility use. The county was dismissed from the suit. The trial court ruled the easement was no longer in effect and the county could grant a right of way 33 feet on either side of the center line of a county highway. The court held that (1) where the county was no longer a party to the suit, the litigant's claim that their property was taken without just compensation was not properly before the court, (2) the litigant's failed to produce evidence of prejudice or an unjust result, and (3) a proper foundation was laid for the admission of the document the phone company relied on as authority for laying of the first cable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the offsetting awards in favor of each party. The court held the litigants failed to produce evidence of prejudice or an unjust result. The court held the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the litigants' motion for a new trial or for additur.

Appeal in Pima County Mental Health Case


No. 2 CA-CIV 5587


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


149 Ariz. 594; 721 P.2d 142; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 489



February 19, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 28, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause No. MH 1717-1-85, Honorable Gordon S. Kipps, Court Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant psychiatric patient sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which ordered the psychiatric patient committed to a mental health facility.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ordered the psychiatric patient committed to a mental health facility. In her appeal, the psychiatric patient attacked the constitutional validity of the recently amended Arizona civil commitment law. The psychiatric patient contended that the definition of "danger to others" in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 36-501(3) was insufficient as a basis for commitment. The psychiatric patient argued that no finding of danger to others was constitutional unless predicated on recent dangerous conduct. Affirming, the court held that the standard in the definition was constitutional. The court found that the requirement of "competent medical opinion" in § 36-501(3) was not an unlawful delegation of legislative power and did not serve to deprive her of a neutral fact finder on the issue of dangerousness. The court doubted the applicability of the notion of "fair warning" to a class composed of those mentally incompetent to make judgments. The court found an implicit requirement of imminence of danger in § 36-501(3). The court held that Miranda warnings were not required before the psychiatric patient gave responses to a physician in the commitment process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1106 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Samaritan Health Servs. v. Glendale


No. 1 CA-CIV 7470


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


148 Ariz. 394; 714 P.2d 887; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 414



February 6, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-456666. The Honorable David L. Roberts, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff health clinic challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County, which granted the summary judgment motion of defendant city and Department of Public Safety (department) in the health clinic's declaratory judgment action, alleging that the city and the department used search warrants for the purpose of seizing patients' medical records in violation of the U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OVERVIEW: The health clinic sought relief from the city's and the department's continued use of search warrants without a determination of whether the medical records to be seized were subject to the physician-patient privilege. The trial court found that the health clinic had standing and that the use of search warrants for the seizure of medical records of the health clinic's patients was not unconstitutional. The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the city and the department and held that the health clinic was not required to assert the physician-patient privilege under Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 12-2235 and 13-4062(4) when served with a search warrant for medical records. The court reasoned that the statutory scheme provided no scheme under which the health clinic was required to assert such privilege. The court further reasoned that the legislature had found certain societal interest sufficiently important to override the state's general interest in protecting confidential patient information from disclosure to third parties. However, the court held that the health clinic had standing to attack the validity of the search warrants in a declaratory judgment action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the city and the department in the health clinic's declaratory judgment action.

 

1107 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Christi


Nos. 1 CA-CR 8739, 1 CA-CR 8740


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


149 Ariz. 323; 718 P.2d 487; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 460



February 4, 1986 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause Nos. LCA-25284 and LCA-25308, The Honorable Ed W. Hughes, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a conviction and sentence from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) for prostitution in violation of Scottsdale, Ariz., Rev. Code § 7-304(B)(1). Defendant was sentenced to the mandatory minimum sentence of 10 days in jail. The issue was whether Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3214(B), which allowed municipalities to regulate prostitution, was unconstitutional as either a local or special law or a denial of equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that while another case held that a similar ordinance was not a special law, it did not reach the question of whether the enabling legislation, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3214(B), was special or local legislation. The court rejected defendant's contention that the legislature had indirectly accomplished through the enabling statute what it could not directly accomplish. The court did not see how § 13-3214(B) bestowed favors on any locality or preferred class. The court held that the statute operated uniformly and without favoritism across its jurisdiction, neither mandating that a city or town impose restrictions on prostitution greater than those otherwise applied under Arizona law, nor preventing an unincorporated area from attaining city status and acting on the statute. The court opined that the Arizona legislature properly delegated authority to punish prostitution so that each locality could tailor ordinances to fit individual needs. The court concluded that the legislature could rationally decide that various cities had different problems that required solutions tailored to fit local conditions and that the problem was more prevalent in urban than in rural areas.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for prostitution.

Arizona Dep't of Revenue v. Robinson's Hardware


No. 1 CA-CIV 7640


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


149 Ariz. 589; 721 P.2d 137; 1986 Ariz. App. LEXIS 409



January 30, 1986 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 28, 1986. Review Denied July 15, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-475001, The Honorable David L. Grounds, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant store challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment to appellee Arizona Department of Revenue (department), upholding the department's assessment against the store for a transaction privilege tax deficiency.


OVERVIEW: The department audited the store, and issued an assessment alleging a transaction privilege tax deficiency resulting from the store's failure to include its sales to Mexican customers in its gross sales proceeds or gross income. The court affirmed the district court's decision to grant summary judgment to the department. The court determined that the tax was directly and specifically on the store for the privilege of conducting business within the state of Arizona. Arizona's transaction privilege tax met the requirements of not interfering with United States foreign policy or creating conflicts and trade barriers between the states, and therefore it was constitutionally permissible. The court found that the tax was purely a domestic, intrastate exaction properly imposed on the store in return for the store's fair share of the benefits and protection afforded to its business by the state of Arizona. The court concluded that the district court did not abuse his discretion by reversing its position on the store's tax liability after there was a fundamental change in law. The court denied the department's request of an award of attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the department.

1110 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Franks v. United States Fidelity & Guar. Co.


No. 1 CA-CIV 7012


COURT OF APPEALS OF ARIZONA, DIVISION ONE, DEPARTMENT D


149 Ariz. 291; 718 P.2d 193; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 842



December 19, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-470503, The Honorable William T. Moroney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, employee and his wife, challenged the judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted defendant workers' compensation insurer's motion to dismiss the employee's tort action for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and for failure to state a claim on which relief could be granted.


OVERVIEW: The employee argued that the tort of bad faith was an independent cause of action and that damages for pain and mental distress were not compensable under the Workers' Compensation Act (Act). The insurer argued that under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1022(A) (Supp. 1985), recovery under the Act was the employee's exclusive remedy. The court held that the Act's exclusive remedy provision did not apply because bad faith by a carrier in the handling of a workers' compensation claim did not arise out of and in the course of employment. The court found determinative the finding by the Industrial Commission's hearing officer that the insurance carrier had not acted in good faith. The court found that the Act did not address the injuries claimed by the employee. The court also held that the trial court had jurisdiction over the employee's claim because the employee's right to bring the tort action was guaranteed by Ariz. Const. art. 18, § 6. The court reasoned that the employee's injury from the insurer's bad faith was separate and distinct from the original industrial injury and was not compensable under the Act. To hold otherwise would have abrogated the employee's constitutional right.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court in dismissing the tort action of the employee and his wife for lack of jurisdiction and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

1111 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Superior Court


No. 2 CA-SA 0317


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


149 Ariz. 169; 717 P.2d 473; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 834



December 18, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied January 28, 1986. Review Denied April 8, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: SPECIAL ACTION PROCEEDINGS, Relief Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners brought an action against respondent trial court seeking relief from the trial court's decision to hold them in contempt for refusing to testify before a grand jury after having been granted use immunity under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4064.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners were convicted and sentenced in a separate criminal matter. They were thereafter subpoenaed to testify before the grand jury, and although both appeared, they refused to answer questions, asserting their Fifth Amendment privilege against compulsory self-incrimination. At the state's request, petitioners were granted immunity and ordered to testify. When they again refused to answer questions on Fifth Amendment grounds, the trial court held them in contempt and ordered them incarcerated until they answered the questions. Petitioners brought an action in the court seeking relief from the trial court's order. The court held that: (1) petitioners' challenge to the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4064 was properly before the court; (2) where the statute's grant of immunity could be construed in a manner that was coextensive with the Fifth Amendment's protection against self incrimination, it was constitutional; and (3) petitioners could testify before the trial court after the dissolution of the grand jury, and where it their refusal to testify could be based on their hope for a remedy, there was no cause to hold that further incarceration was punitive.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioners' request for relief from the trial court's decision.

Patchell v. State


No. 2 CA-SA 0292


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


147 Ariz. 508; 711 P.2d 647; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 738



November 7, 1985 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a judgment from respondents, the Pima County Court, in and for the State of Arizona, (Arizona), which subpoenaed him to testify before a grand jury. He asserted his Fifth Amendment privilege against self-incrimination. The State then requested a superior court to grant the petitioner use immunity and ordered him to testify pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4064. Petitioner claimed § 13-4064 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was subpoenaed to testify before a grand jury. He appeared but refused to testify, asserting his Fifth Amendment privilege against self-incrimination. The state then requested the superior court to grant petitioner use immunity and ordered him to testify pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4064. He refused and was found in contempt. Petitioner challenged the constitutionality of Arizona's "use immunity" statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-4064, on constitutional grounds. The court held that the practice of granting immunity from prosecution in exchange for compelled incriminating testimony, while consonant in principle with the Fifth Amendment prohibition against compulsory self-incrimination, it does not preclude prosecution of the witness other than on the basis of his testimony or evidence derived therefrom. The court found the "use immunity" statute was constitutional and denied petitioner relief.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petitioner relief and found that the Arizona "use immunity" statute was constitutional as applied.

Gurr v. Willcutt


No. 1 CA-CIV 7426


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


146 Ariz. 575; 707 P.2d 979; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 637

Cause No. C-477077

The Honorable Marilyn A. Riddel, Judge

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, physicians and corporations, in plaintiffs' medical malpractice suit.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff patient filed a medical malpractice action against defendants, physicians and corporations, after he felt he was given unneeded medical treatment and an unneeded pacemaker. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, physicians and corporations, in plaintiff's medical malpractice action. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court had jurisdiction and legal authority to grant a motion for summary judgment prior to any action by a medical liability review panel. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendants, physicians and corporations, in plaintiff patient's medical malpractice action holding that the trial court had jurisdiction and authority to grant summary judgment prior to any action by a medical liability review panel, and that expert letters confirmed plaintiff's diagnosis, and that neither letter described a failure to use the proper degree of care.

 

1114 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Phoenix v. West Publishing Co.


No. 1 CA-CIV 6716


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


148 Ariz. 31; 712 P.2d 944; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 758



September 17, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 14, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-407753, The Honorable Robert W. Pickrell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by appellant city for taxes allegedly due, the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) found appellee publisher's activity within the city was insufficient to establish the necessary constitutional nexus justifying imposition of the city privilege license tax. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The publisher was a Minnesota corporation involved in the publication and sale of legal books and periodicals. The publisher did not own or lease an office or other facility in Arizona nor did it maintain an inventory in the state. The publisher's sales agent happened to live in the city, and this was the only direct contact with the city that the publisher had. On these facts, the trial court found the publisher's activity within the city was insufficient to establish the necessary constitutional nexus justifying imposition of the city privilege license tax. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the imposition of the city's privilege license tax on the publisher violated the due process clauses of the United States and Arizona Constitutions. This was because the nature and quantity of the publisher's activity in the city was not sufficient to provide the requisite constitutional nexus for the tax sought to be imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court ruling and found the publisher's activity within the city insufficient to justify the imposition of the city privilege tax.

Mathis v. Liquor Bd.


No. 1 CA-CIV 7155


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


146 Ariz. 570; 707 P.2d 974; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 638



August 13, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied September 23, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. C-470080

The Honorable Warren L. McCarthy, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state appealed the grant of a summary judgment for plaintiff sellers in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which lifted the Arizona State Liquor Board's (board) stay on a transfer and suspension of a liquor license.


OVERVIEW: After the buyer became delinquent in taxes for an inn and defaulted on his obligations to sellers, the sellers obtained a judgment against the buyer and repurchased their inn. The board suspended the inn's license and stayed transfer of the license until back taxes were paid. The trial court granted summary judgment for sellers. The trial court ordered a lifting of the board's stay on transfer and of the suspension of the license. On appeal, the court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 4-210(A)(5) did not limit the board's sanctioning power to the licensed business, which incurred delinquent taxes. The Department of Revenue's foreclosed junior tax liens did not preclude sanctions against a liquor license. The delinquent taxes were a legitimate basis for sanctions. The liquor board's sanctions were not arbitrary, capricious and did not involve an abuse of discretion in violation of due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1116 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. McInelly


No. 1 CA-CR 8135


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One


146 Ariz. 161; 704 P.2d 291; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 572



July 18, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF YAVAPAI COUNTY

Cause No. 10751

Honorable James B. Sult, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona), which convicted him of possession of marijuana for sale, transportation of marijuana, and possession of an imitation controlled substance with intent to distribute. Imposition of sentence was suspended for a period of two years, and defendant was placed on probation pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-901(A).


OVERVIEW: After a law enforcement officer discovered illegal substances in the car in which defendant and two other persons were travelling, defendant was convicted of possession of marijuana for sale, transportation of marijuana, and possession of an imitation controlled substance with intent to distribute. Defendant was placed on probation. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that although defendant was charged as a principal, the trial court did not err in giving an instruction on accomplice liability because there was no distinction between accomplice and principal liability. Defendant's conviction for "transportation" did not require proof of a change in locality. The statute that criminalized transportation of marijuana separately from, and more severely than, the mere possession of the drug was upheld under the rational basis test. Convictions for possession and transportation of marijuana were permissible under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-116 because the sentences were concurrent. The trial court had the right under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-702 to defer the designation of defendant's conviction for possession of an imitation controlled substance until probation was completed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Scotia


No. 1 CA-CR 8200


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One


146 Ariz. 159; 704 P.2d 289; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 573



July 18, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF YAVAPAI COUNTY

Cause No. CR-10887

Honorable James B. Sult, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona), which convicted him of transportation of marijuana in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3405(C)(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of transportation of marijuana. On appeal, defendant contended that § 13-3405(C)(3) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad because the word "transport" was not defined in the statute and because a person of ordinary intelligence could not understand the meaning of the word. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that a person of average intelligence could understand the meaning of the word "transport" within the statute and that the fact that the statute did not indicate the means of transportation, the distance required to be traveled, or the quantity of marijuana needed for conviction did not render the statute unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. The court found that the statute gave sufficient warning to the public to allow persons to conform their conduct accordingly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for transportation of marijuana.

The Honorable Paul G. Rosenblatt, Judge

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona) dismissing his appeal from an order of the city court finding him guilty of violating Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1253 and suspending his driver's license. His appeal was dismissed because he failed to pay for transcripts or attempt to secure a stipulation with the prosecutor that the tapes of the city court proceedings be sent untranscribed to the superior court.


OVERVIEW: After the city court entered its judgment, defendant filed a notice of appeal to the superior court. He made a motion to be found indigent pursuant to Ariz. Super. Ct. R. App. P. Crim. 5. The superior court ordered that defendant either pay for the transcripts or stipulate with the State that the tapes of the city court proceedings be sent untranscribed to the superior court. After defendant failed pay for the transcripts or enter into a stipulation, the State filed a motion to dismiss the appeal. Defendant failed to appear at oral argument on his motion to be found indigent, and the superior court dismissed his appeal. The only issue preserved for appeal was the superior court's dismissal of his appeal from the city court. The court dismissed defendant's appeal, holding that its jurisdiction was limited by Ariz. Crim. 13(b), no appeal lay with the court. Defendant's remedy was by way of special action pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. §12-2001 et seq.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

 

1119 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Mountain Shadows Resort Hotel v. Industrial Comm'n


No. 1 CA-IC 3120


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


147 Ariz. 411; 710 P.2d 1066; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 717



July 5, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied September 6, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action - Industrial Commission, ICA Claim No. 349-28-2956, Carrier No. 4001240-008, Lawrence P. Nicholls, Administrative Law Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an employer and its insurance carrier, brought a special action to challenged an order of the Industrial Commission of Arizona, which allowed respondent claimant to change physicians and awarded benefits for the total loss of use of the claimant's leg. The claimant requested the award be set aside on the basis that it was error to find that his condition was stationary.


OVERVIEW: The claimant's physician believed nothing more could be done for claimant's knee, but he recommended treatment transfer to a consulting surgeon, who recommended another operation. The carrier denied the claimant's request to change physicians. The administrative law judge (ALJ) granted the change of physician. The carrier appealed. The court set aside the award. Although Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1071(B) was written in negative terms, the legislative intent was to allow the claimant to change physicians with the consent of his attending physician. Section 23-1071(B) applied because the employer had not elected to provide medical benefits under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1070, which would have triggered Ariz. Comp. R. & Regs. R4-13-113(C). It was undisputed that the claimant had a 10 percent impairment, but the ALJ failed to find if the disability had been truly measured. Although the ALJ stated the total disability was based on the claimant's testimony, the record contained no testimony that he was incapable of obtaining employment. The evidence was insufficient to enable an informed comparative evaluation. The conclusion that claimant's condition was stationary was legally sound.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the award made by the Commission.

 

1120 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hicks


No. 1 CA-CR 8573


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One


146 Ariz. 533; 707 P.2d 331; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 635



June 20, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied July 18, 1985. Review Denied October 16, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF MARICOPA COUNTY

Cause No. CR-140258

Honorable Elizabeth Stover, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a criminal action against defendant, the state appealed an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which suppressed evidence that was seized upon a search warrant.


OVERVIEW: Following a shooting from a certain apartment, police officers were admitted to the apartment by the manager. The officers seized several weapons, and one of the officers became suspicious of expensive stereo components, which he moved to locate and record the serial numbers. On checking the computer and department records, the officer learned that the components had been taken in an armed robbery, and he secured a search warrant and seized the components. In the criminal action against defendant, the trial court entered an order suppressing the evidence of the components, and the state appealed. The court affirmed the order of suppression, finding that the recording of the serial numbers was unrelated to the exigency justifying entry and involved an additional search not necessitated by the exigency. It was plainly unlawful, and the subsequent warrant did not validate the earlier illegal search. Police officers could not launder their prior unconstitutional behavior by presenting the fruits of it to a magistrate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of suppression in the criminal action against defendant.

Shew v. Jeffers


No. 2 CA-CIV 5321


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


147 Ariz. 192; 709 P.2d 549; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 721



June 20, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 27, 1985. Review Denied November 26, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY; Cause No. 217949, Honorable Harry Gin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a decision from the Superior Court, Pima County (Arizona), which dismissed their complaint against appellees, tax assessor and sheriff, that challenged the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-204 et seq., and the manner in which unpaid property taxes were collected through a property seizure.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers had not paid a personal property taxes. The assessor issued a tax bill to the sheriff pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-611. The sheriff notified the taxpayers property would be seized and sold if the taxes were not paid. The taxpayers' action for injunctive relief was dismissed and the sheriff entered the taxpayers' business and seized personal property. The taxpayers then filed an action for damages that challenged the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 42-204 et seq. and the seizure procedure. The trial court dismissed that action. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal of the constitutional challenge to § 42-204 because it had been sustained numerous times. However, the court reversed as to the taxpayers' damage complaint, which was based on the use of a tax bill rather than a judicial warrant to obtain entry to the taxpayers business, where the seizure of their property occurred. Because the taxpayers had stated a valid damage complaint, the action was remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the taxpayers constitutional challenge to the tax protest statute and reversed the dismissal of the taxpayer's complaint that alleged a violation of constitutional rights by the improper manner in which their property was seized.

State v. Poehnelt


No. 2 CA-CR 2860


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department B


150 Ariz. 136; 722 P.2d 304; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 862



June 7, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY, Cause Nos. CR-06965 and CR-07589 (Consolidated), Honorable Robert B. Buchanan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, stepfather and mother, sought review of their convictions for intentional or knowing child abuse under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3623(B)(1) from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona). The stepfather argued that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, challenged the sufficiency of the evidence, and argued that his sentence was excessive in light of those historically imposed for such crimes.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the stepfather was not denied effective assistance of counsel due to his attorney's failure to investigate and present a defense in the face of a psychiatrist's determination that the stepfather did not have a mental disorder and was able to assist in his defense. Based on the child's statements, the child's physical condition, the stepfather's admission that he struck the child, the court also concluded that the evidence was sufficient to sustain the stepfather's conviction of intentional or knowing child abuse. Further, the evidence directly from the victim was inconsistent with a less culpable mental state. Finally, the court held that the sentence imposed was not excessive. The stepfather's higher culpability, enormous physical abuse over a period of years to the child, and the stepfather's age and higher level of mental functioning distinguished the examples relied upon by the stepfather. In addition, the defendants who received lesser sentences displayed a cooperative attitude of an admission of guilt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and sentences.

In re Appeal in Maricopa County, Juvenile Action


No. 1 CA-JUV 271


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


145 Ariz. 405; 701 P.2d 1213; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 530



May 7, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied June 25, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. JS-5894

The Honorable C. Kimball Rose, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which terminated the parent-child relationship between the mother and her child. Appellee Respondent Department of Economic Security had filed an action against the mother seeking to find the child to be dependent and to terminate the mother's parent-child relationship with the child.


OVERVIEW: Shortly after the mother, who had a history of mental illness, gave birth to the child, the department initiated a dependency proceeding, and the child was adjudicated dependent and placed in its custody. Then, it sought to terminate her relationship with the child. The trial court granted the petition, finding that she could not discharge her parental responsibilities. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the mother had no standing to raise the issue of the termination of the natural father's parent-child relationship with the child because she was not an "aggrieved party" under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-236(A), as such judgment did not operate to deny her any rights; (2) the term "parental responsibilities" did not intend to encompass any exclusive set of factors but intended to establish a standard that permitted flexibility in considering the unique circumstances of each termination case; (3) the statements of a caseworker concerning events which occurred immediately after the child's birth were not hearsay because they were offered to show the basis for the initiation of the investigation; and (4) grounds for termination had to be based upon clear and convincing evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Hutchinson


No. 1 CA-CR 7315


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One


145 Ariz. 27; 699 P.2d 402; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 484



April 25, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Mohave County

Cause No. CR-5993 and CR-6051

The Honorable Gary R. Pope, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Arizona sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Mohave County (Arizona), which found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1503(A) violated defendants rights under the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I., in an appeal by defendant from his conviction in municipal court for violating § 44-1503(A).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, the owner and operator of a motel, was charged and convicted in municipal court of violating § 44-1503(A), which required operators of motels, who maintained outdoor signs that advertised rates, to set forth both the minimum and maximum room or other rental unit rate for accommodations offered for rental. On appeal to the superior court, defendant filed a motion to dismiss the criminal charges on the basis that § 44-1503(A) violated his First Amendment free speech rights. The superior court found, inter alia, that the statute was unconstitutional on its face. The court reversed and remanded, noting that the speech at issue involved commercial speech. Also, the court found that defendant had the burden of proof on the issue of whether the statute was more extensive than reasonably than necessary to further substantial interests. Because defendant had the burden of proof, the court would not presume the unconstitutionality of the statute. Rather, the presumption was that the statute was constitutional until proven otherwise. The court held that § 44-1503 was facially constitutional and that defendant did not meet his burden of proof as to "unreasonableness."


OUTCOME: the court reversed the judgment of the superior court and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Salazar


No. 2 CA-CR 3420


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


146 Ariz. 547; 707 P.2d 951; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 641



April 24, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 31, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY

Cause No. CR-10968

Honorable J. Richard Hannah



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of conviction of manslaughter, endangerment, and driving while intoxicated entered by the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) and the sentences it imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of manslaughter, endangerment, and driving while intoxicated. The trial court imposed presumptive concurrent sentences on the convictions of manslaughter and endangerment. On appeal, the court affirmed. First, the court held that the trial court erred in denying defendant the right to cross-examine the victim's widow concerning the wrongful death action. Even though a default judgment may have been entered in the civil action, it was for the jury to determine whether the witness had a motive to testify to facts consistent with the position she had taken in the wrongful death case. The test results of a blood sample taken with probable cause were admissible.

1127 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Serrano


No. 2 CA-CR 3584


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two, Department A


145 Ariz. 498; 702 P.2d 1343; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 541



March 11, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 7, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY

Cause No. CR-10701

Honorable Michael J. Brown, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment rendered by Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) convicting defendant of criminal trespass with a prior conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after looking through a dormitory window. The court rejected defendant's contention that the "peeping tom" statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1504(A)(2), was unconstitutionally vague. Applying the statutory definition of recklessness to the "peeping tom" statute, the court concluded that the State had to first establish that, under all the circumstances and evidence, the risk that there would be an infringement on the inhabitant's right of privacy was so great that disregard of it constituted a gross deviation from the standard of conduct that a reasonable person would observe in the situation. This facet of recklessness was objectively based. The State had to further prove defendant's actual awareness of the risk that there would be an infringement of the inhabitant's right of privacy. This second facet of recklessness required defendant's subjective knowledge of the risk before conviction could be had. Because the twofold standard of recklessness was sufficiently precise to be understood and applied by persons of ordinary intelligence, § 13-1504(A)(2) was not impermissibly vague. The crime was complete regardless of what or whom was subject to defendant's gaze.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction.

Corrigan v. Scottsdale


No. 1 CA-CIV 6300


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


149 Ariz. 553; 720 P.2d 528; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 851



February 28, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County Cause No. C-359908, ASC# 18239-PA The Honorable James Moeller, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner sought review of a judgment entered in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) dismissing plaintiff's action against defendant city for a declaratory judgment establishing the invalidity of Scottsdale, Ariz., Ordinance 455 § 6.800-.807 (1977), which created a conservation area district where development was prohibited.


OVERVIEW: A city ordinance prohibited development in an area on which the landowner owned undeveloped property. The trial court denied the landowner's allegation that the ordinance brought about an unconstitutional taking of her property. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment, holding that the ordinance was not a proper exercise of the city's police power, but was instead an illegal confiscation without just compensation. The court held that the there was no legitimate state interest advanced by the ordinance and that there was no deplorable condition or substantial threat to public safety in the absence of the ordinance. The court held that the ordinance denied the landowner the economically viable use of her property in violation of Ariz. Const. art II, § 17, under which the transfer of density credits could not meet the constitutional requirement mandating that compensation for a taking be made by payment of money in an amount judicially determined. The court also held that the trial court did not err in refusing to consider the landowner's contention that the city had no statutory authority to enact the ordinance because plaintiff had failed to raise that issue in a timely manner.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment dismissing the landowner's action for a declaratory judgment establishing the invalidity of the city's ordinance prohibiting development in a conservation area district where the landowner owned undeveloped property. The court held that the ordinance was an unconstitutional taking of the landowner's property.

Boswell v. Phoenix Newspapers


No. 1 CA-CIV 6123


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


152 Ariz. 1; 730 P.2d 178; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 879



February 28, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-366121, The Honorable John H. Seidel, Judge, Nos. 18159-PR, May 20, 1985.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, defamed persons, appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) for defendants, newspaper and reporter. The defamed persons alleged that the trial court erred in refusing to grant a motion for a directed verdict, that emotional distress was an element of damages, that the corrections statute, was unconstitutional, and that jury instructions and rulings on evidence were improper.


OVERVIEW: The reporter wrote a story for the newspaper in which it was incorrectly stated that the defamed persons pleaded guilty to burglary. The newspaper corrected the story. The defamed persons filed a defamation action. A judgment was entered for the newspaper and the reporter. The defamed persons appealed. The court reversed and held that testimony on the reporter's procedures was admissible as habit evidence under Ariz. R. Evid. 406 and that the absence of expert testimony was not fatal. Based on the uncontradicted evidence, reasonable minds could only conclude that the reporter and the newspapers were negligent. The trial court erred in the way it submitted the issue of liability to the jury. The defamed persons were not allowed to recover damages for emotional distress because under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-653.03 that was not an element of damages for defamation. However, the corrections statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-653.01 et seq., violated the due process clauses of the federal and state constitutions by eliminating such recovery. The corrections statute also violated Ariz. Const. art 18, § 6, so the court struck it and decided the claims solely on the state constitutional ground.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which found in favor of the newspaper and the reporter in the defamed persons' defamation action.

Behavioral Health Agency (BHACA) v. Casa Grande


No. 2 CA-CIV 5172


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two


147 Ariz. 126; 708 P.2d 1317; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 697



February 19, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 11, 1985. Review Denied October 29, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PINAL COUNTY Cause No. 33743 Honorable E.D. McBryde, Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicants sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Pinal County (Arizona), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, city and city council, in the applicants' action alleging that the city council's denial of a conditional use permit was arbitrary and capricious and that the city zoning ordinance was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The applicants filed for a conditional use permit to operate a group home for the elderly in an area zoned for single-family residences. The planning and zoning commission denied the permit and the city council upheld the denial. The applicants filed the action in the trial court alleging that the city council's actions were arbitrary and capricious and that the city ordinances were unconstitutional. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the city and the city council. The appellate court affirmed. The court held that the home for the elderly was not a permitted use under the city zoning ordinance and that the city council's denial of a conditional use permit was not arbitrary, capricious, or unreasonable. The court found that unrelated elderly people living together did not constitute a "family" within the meaning of the city zoning ordinance. In addition, the city council did not act wrongfully in failing to grant the conditional use permit because the proposed use was not a group home, as defined by the ordinance, but a boarding house. The court concluded that the zoning ordinance was constitutional because it bore a rational relationship to a permissible goal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the city and the city council.
