Toto v. Industrial Comm'n


No. 1 CA-IC 3073


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


144 Ariz. 508; 698 P.2d 753; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 470



February 7, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied April 16, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Special Action - Industrial Commission

ICA Claim No. 301-22-3206

Carrier No. 79 C 69 50 01

Peter J. Baum, Administrative Law Judge



DISPOSITION: AWARD AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review of a decision of respondent Industrial Commission (the commission) (Arizona), which denied her claim for workers' compensation benefits in connection with her emotional problems.


OVERVIEW: The employee was terminated after suffering a work-related injury. The employee also alleged that the termination caused her to suffer from emotional problems, so she filed a workers' compensation claim. The commission denied the claim concluding that the employee's emotional problems were not compensable pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1043.01(B). The employee alleged that § 23-1043.01(B) was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed the commission's decision holding that because § 23-1043.01(B) treated all persons within a class equally, it did not violate the equal protection clause. The court further held that the higher evidentiary burden that was placed on claims for mental injuries under the statute was reasonable in light of the problems associated with establishing a causal nexus between mental illness and the workplace. Finally, the court held that because the employee's firing, which caused her emotional problems, was not substantially related to her work-related injury, the commission correctly concluded that the employee's emotional problems were not compensable under § 23-1043.01(B).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision of the commission, which denied the employee's claim for workers' compensation benefits in connection with her emotional problems.

 

1132 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Hills v. Salt River Project Ass'n


No. 1 CA-CIV 6975


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


144 Ariz. 421; 698 P.2d 216; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 471



January 29, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied April 9, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. C-465092

The Honorable I. Sylvan Brown, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff widow brought a wrongful death suit against defendant employer, co-workers, and manufacturers after the employee was electrocuted when power lines came into contact with his truck. Plaintiff had previously received worker's compensation benefits for the employee. The Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) granted defendants' motions for summary judgment, and plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the trial court's decision. It held that worker's compensation was the employee's and his survivors' exclusive remedy against the employer. It rejected plaintiffs' argument that the "dual capacity" doctrine allowed her to proceed against the employer because it had participated in manufacturing the truck and boom involved in the accident and because it was a supplier of electricity, stating that the doctrine conflicted with Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1022(A), providing for the exclusive remedy, and subverted the legislature's intent in enacting the statute. It held that because plaintiff had not filed a tort action within one year of the accident, her claims against third parties were assigned to the employer, which was self-insured, under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1023. It stated that this rule applied to the claims against the co-workers as well. It rejected plaintiff's argument that the assignment of her claim after one year violated due process and equal protection, stating that the statute did not treat employees of self-insured carriers differently from other employees and that the state supreme court had previously upheld the statute's constitutionality.


OUTCOME: In plaintiff's wrongful death suit, the court affirmed the trial court's decision granting summary judgment to defendants.

 

1133 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Cagle v. Carlson


No. 1 CA-CIV 6781


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


146 Ariz. 292; 705 P.2d 1343; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 653



January 29, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied March 21, 1985. Review Denied September 4, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County, Cause No. C-305893, The Honorable David J. Perry, Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, promisor of a note, sought review of a decision in favor of appellee promisees from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which refused to set aside a sheriff's sale ordered as a result of foreclosure proceedings upon the default on a promissory note.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted the promisees' motion to dismiss. On review, the appellate court reversed. The trial court subsequently granted the promisees' motion for summary judgment. On further review, the court held that the issues before the trial court had not been previously determined when it entered summary judgment for the promisees. There was no iron clad rule that a denial of summary judgment motion was res judicata and absolutely precluded renewal or the making of a subsequent motion for the same relief. There was further discovery undertaken between the time of the first denial of the motion for summary judgment and the second filing of the new motion. Therefore, even though successive motions were filed, the court found no abuse of the system. The court held that the promisor's offer in the amended complaint to pay the amount of judgment did not satisfy the requirement of "tender" to the promisees as a condition precedent to setting aside the sale. There was no denial of due process due to lack of personal notice to the execution on the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1134 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Corella v. Superior Court


No. 2 CA-SA 0176


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two


144 Ariz. 418; 698 P.2d 213; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 469



January 25, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] SPECIAL ACTION PROCEEDINGS

Relief Granted


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner patient brought a special action from the judgment of respondent Superior Court of Arizona, which denied his motion for summary judgment in an interpleader action by the driver's insurer, naming the patient and respondent health plan as co-defendants. The patient filed a cross claim against the health plan and moved for summary judgment, which the trial court denied.


OVERVIEW: The only way the trial court could have been correct in denying the motion for summary judgment was if the health plan had a valid, perfected lien on the policy limits. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 36-2903(E) made no mention of any assignment of liability coverage. All the administrator was authorized to do was to coordinate benefits payable to an injured eligible person from third parties. The statute did not authorize him to create a lien. Any Access rules or regulations, which purported to give the health plan a lien on liability coverage, was of no effect. Nothing in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 36-2915 showed that the legislature intended it to apply retroactively. Even if the legislative intent in passing the Access program was to give the administrator broad authority under § 36-2903, the legislature could not have granted the health plan the ability to create statutory liens because that would be an unconstitutional delegation of the power to make law. The health plan was not entitled to any of the impleaded fund, and the trial court acted in excess of its authority in denying the patient's motion for summary judgment. The court vacated the trial court's order.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order denying the patient's motion for summary judgment in the insurer's interpleader action against the patient and the health plan, and it ordered the trial court to grant the motion.

 

1135 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Flowing Wells Sch. Dist. v. Vail Sch. Dist.


No. 2 CA-CIV 5170


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two


145 Ariz. 278; 700 P.2d 1378; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 520



January 14, 1985 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied April 2, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County

Cause No. 207946

Honorable Stephen M. Weiss, Judge Pro Tempore



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which denied its motion for a new trial following an adverse judgment in a declaratory judgment action brought by appellee school district which sought to find appellant liable for transportation cost for its secondary students.


OVERVIEW: Appellee filed an action for a declaratory judgment that sought to find appellant, which did not have a high school for its students, liable for the transportation costs of bringing students to appellee's high school. Appellant furnished transportation to a high school in a neighboring district but did not provide transportation to other districts, including appellee's district. The trial court ruled in favor of appellee and denied appellant's motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court reversed. Once appellant decided that transportation of students to any other than the neighboring district was not in appellant's best interest, it was a usurpation of its power for appellee to charge appellant for that transportation. The court found no express statutory language permitting appellee to charge appellant for transporting the students, and there was no implication that such charges were permissible. Absent statutory authority, common sense dictated that when high school students in a district without a high school could attend any high school district in the state, it would be impossible for the sending district to transport large numbers of pupils, each to a different high school.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that denied appellant's motion for a new trial following an adverse judgment in a declaratory judgment action brought by appellee which sought to find appellant liable for transportation cost for appellant's secondary students.

 

1136 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Loughran


No. 1 CA-CR 7562


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


143 Ariz. 345; 693 P.2d 1000; 1985 Ariz. App. LEXIS 450



January 10, 1985 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. LCA-24048

The Honorable James Moeller, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted and sentenced defendant for violation of Phoenix, Ariz., City Code § 23-52 for solicitation of prostitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction and sentence for solicitation of prostitution making several arguments. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The court rejected defendant's contention that Phoenix, Ariz., City Code § 23-52(a) was special or local legislation prohibited by Ariz. Const. art. 4, pt. 2, § 19 finding that it operated uniformly on all persons within the jurisdictional limits of the city, excluded no particular persons or locations, and that it was not a law plainly intended for a particular case. Defendant argued that § 23-52(a) violated the state and federal equal protection clauses in that an individual in the city could have been punished differently than individuals in other areas of the state for the same offense. The court found that defendant identified no fundamental right denied him by the ordinance, nor was he a member of any suspect class. The court held that by enacting Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3214(B) the legislature intended that cities and towns enact ordinances to suppress and prohibit prostitution and provide for punishment at least as stringent as a subsection A, class 1 misdemeanor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for solicitation of prostitution and upheld the city ordinance he was convicted under.

Berry v. Department of Corrections


No. 1 CA-CIV 7613


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


144 Ariz. 126; 696 P.2d 216; 1984 Ariz. App. LEXIS 596



December 11, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied February 13, 1985.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. C-501321

The Honorable John H. Seidel, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner brought suit against appellees, the State and the Department of Corrections, asserting that the inclusion of only class four, five, and six offenders in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 31-233(G) was unconstitutional. Cross-motions to dismiss were granted by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona). The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue in this case was whether the trial court erred in dismissing the prisoner's constitutional and statutory challenges to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 31-233(G), a provision that granted early parole eligibility to certain offenders. The prisoner was convicted of theft by false pretenses under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-661, the old criminal code, and subsequently applied for early parole eligibility under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 31-233(G), which he was denied. The statute allowed parole applications by certain prisoners when there was a shortage of beds within the Department of Corrections. To be eligible, a person must have been sentenced for a class four, five, and six felony. However, the prisoner was sentenced under the old criminal code, which did not contain class four, five, and six felony classifications. He was found ineligible for the early parole, and his application was denied. He appealed. The court held that an old code offender whose crime could reasonably be found equivalent to a class four, five, and six felony was eligible for early parole if other statutory criteria were met. Thus, the prisoner was eligible.


OUTCOME: The order of dismissal entered by the trial court was reversed and the case was remanded with directions to order proceedings before the Board of Pardons and Paroles consistent with the opinion.

 

1139 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


No. CA-CR 7087


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


143 Ariz. 318; 693 P.2d 973; 1984 Ariz. App. LEXIS 561



November 15, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied November 15, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. CR-127653

The Honorable Robert A. Hertzberg, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of one count of trafficking in stolen property and sentenced him to imprisonment for a term of ten years.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of one count of trafficking in stolen property and was sentenced to imprisonment for a term of ten years. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-2301 and 13-2307 did not violate equal protection by allegedly imposing a higher punishment for conduct also prohibited by the theft statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-801 et seq., where defendant made no showing that he was the subject of prosecution based on an unjustifiable selection standard. The court held the trafficking statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-2307, was not overbroad where the statute defined the crime of trafficking and did not include persons whose conduct did not fall within the purpose to be achieved by the statute. The court determined defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on entrapment where he did not admit to the elements of the crime charged. The court concluded that defendant's ten-year sentence was not excessive or disproportionate where defendant had been previously convicted of two felonies. The court found credit cards were property within the meaning of Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-2301 and 13-2307.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that convicted defendant of one count of trafficking in stolen property and that sentenced him to imprisonment for a term of ten years.

In re Appeal in Maricopa County Juvenile Action


Nos. 1 CA-JUV 246, 1 CA-JUV 247


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


143 Ariz. 178; 692 P.2d 1027; 1984 Ariz. App. LEXIS 527



October 23, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause Nos. JS 5209 and JS 4963 (Consolidated)

The Honorable James E. McDougall, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant natural mother sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which terminated her parental rights in a case brought by appellee Department of Economic Security.


OVERVIEW: The mother's problems in rearing her children were recognized when a dependency petition was filed on behalf of her six minor children. It was alleged that the mother had been physically abusing the children because of acute distress and that she was in need of psychiatric help. The court held that an objective standard should be set for termination of parental rights and found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-533(B)(3) was not unconstitutionally vague. The doctors testified that the mother's mental condition and her inability to be an effective parent would continue for a prolonged indeterminate period. The mother also argued that the evidence was not clear and convincing that she suffered from a mental illness. However, the evidence clearly showed that the mother was unable to discharge her parental responsibilities and that the mental condition that prevented her from doing so was likely to continue for a prolonged indeterminate period. Under these circumstances, the trial court found that it was in the children's best interest that they be freed for adoption. There was clear and convincing evidence to support the termination of parental rights. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that terminated a mother's parental rights.

California Portland Cement Co. v. Picture Rocks Fire Dist.


No. 2 CA-CIV 5117


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two


143 Ariz. 170; 692 P.2d 1019; 1984 Ariz. App. LEXIS 543



September 20, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied December 4, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY

Cause Nos. 201455 & 201988, consolidated

Honorable A. Alan Hanshaw, Judge Pro Tempore



DISPOSITION: REVERSED WITH DIRECTIONS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, fire district, the fire district's board, and its members (fire district), sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which entered judgment for appellee cement plant in its petition to withdraw from the fire district and ordering the refund of taxes collected.


OVERVIEW: The fire district had been organized pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-1001. A part of the cement plant was included in the district. The remaining part was annexed into the district later. The cement plant's taxes increased substantially because of being in the fire district. The court reversed the decision of the trial court. The trial court had voided the annexation because the persons who signed the petition did not reside on land contiguous to the existing fire district, and because the fire district was a quasi improvement district, which would require the cement plant to receive some special benefits before it could be validly assessed any fire district taxes. The court disagreed with the trial court and found that the annexation petition under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 9-1006.01(A) had been signed by at least 51 percent of the qualified electors. The court found that the fire district was a quasi-municipal corporation, and was not organized to benefit any particular piece of property. There was no error in denying the cement plant's petition to withdraw because there was no change in conditions and the increase in the tax bill did not make including the property improper.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the cement plant in the cement plant's action to withdraw from the fire district and the ordering the refund of taxes collected.

J.W. Hancock Enters. v. Arizona State Registrar of Contractors

Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


142 Ariz. 400; 690 P.2d 119; 1984 Ariz. App. LEXIS 489



August 21, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause Nos. C-397842 and C-397843 (Consolidated)

The Honorable David G. Derickson, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensed contractor challenged judgments of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which affirmed the decision of appellee Arizona State Registrar of Contractors (registrar) finding the contractor in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 32-1154(3) (1977) in the contractor's statutory appeal. Based on that decision, the lower court subsequently granted summary judgment in favor of appellee buyers in a declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: The contractor argued that it did not contract to install zonolite wall insulation in the house it constructed and sold to the buyers. The registrar found that the contractor and buyers had contracted for the insulation package, and the registrar ordered the contractor to either install it or have its contracting license suspended. However, the court found that the buyers did not seek attorneys' fees in the statutory appeal, so the award of attorneys' fees was reduced to only those incurred in the declaratory judgment action.

State v. Yellowmexican


No. 1 CA-CR 7162


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


142 Ariz. 205; 688 P.2d 1097; 1984 Ariz. App. LEXIS 431



June 12, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Coconino County

Cause No. CR-10212

The Honorable John H. Grace, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from a decision of the Superior Court of Coconino County (Arizona), which dismissed both counts of the indictment charging defendant with violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692.01.F, his third Driving While Intoxicated (DWI) in thirty-six months, and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692,02.A, DWI while license revoked.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving while intoxicated on May 28, 1980, and again in July, 1981. On March 2, 1983, he allegedly committed a third DWI offense while his driver's license was revoked and was charged under both § 28-692.01.F. and § 28-692.02.A. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss both charges on the ground that the application of the above statutes to him constituted a prohibited ex post facto law. The trial court agreed and dismissed both counts of the indictment. The state appealed. The court found that the punishment imposed under § 28-692.01.F. was based on the third DWI and the statute did not increase the penalty for the prior convictions. The court found that except for the third conviction, there would have been no punishment beyond that originally imposed for the first two DWI's. The court concluded that § 28-692.01.F. was an enhanced punishment statute and that no greater or additional penalty was imposed upon defendant for his earlier offenses by virtue of § 28-692.01.F. The court held that the statute was not an ex post facto law and reversed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court dismissing both counts of the indictment against defendant and remanded the case with instructions to reinstate the two charges of third DWI in thirty-six months and DWI while license revoked.

State v. Canaday


No. 1 CA-CR 6344


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


141 Ariz. 31; 684 P.2d 912; 1984 Ariz. App. LEXIS 551



May 17, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the trial court (Arizona) for conspiracy to commit a fraudulent scheme. Defendant argued that his right to confront witnesses was breached through the admission into evidence of the confession of an accomplice who was deceased at the time of trial, that prejudicial error occurred during jury voir dire, and that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-604(b) unconstitutionally discriminated for punishment enhancement purposes.


OVERVIEW: An accomplice was indicted for passing stolen checks and told the police of his and defendant's part in the scheme but he died in a car accident before trial. Defendant denied participating in the conspiracy. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. Defendant attacked the use of the deceased man's statements, a collateral inculpatory statement that implicated defendant and was collateral to the portion implicating the declarant. The admissibility of the declarations mandated that the declarant not only be unavailable but that the statement was against his penal interest and that proof of corroborating circumstances was present to clearly indicate the statement's truthfulness. The declarant had many possible motives for talking to the police that cast doubt on the truth of the declarations and there was a strong need for cross-examination. When viewed in its totality, there were insufficient indicia of the statement's trustworthiness and it was error to admit. There was a rational basis for the difference between the enhancement of punishment between the more serious and the less serious felony and the statute did not violate defendant's equal protection or due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the matter for a new trial. The court held that the statute did not violate defendant's due process or equal protection rights.

Pena v. Indus. Comm'n


Nos. 1 CA-IC 2898, 1 CA-IC 2901


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


140 Ariz. 510; 683 P.2d 309; 1984 Ariz. App. LEXIS 479



April 3, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 22, 1984.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner widow sought review of a decision of respondent Industrial Commission of Arizona, which determined the decedent's average monthly wage. The widow argued that the administrative law judge applied an improper formula in determining the average monthly wage, and questioned the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1046(C).


OVERVIEW: Following the death of the widow's husband, the commission determined the decedent's average monthly wage. The widow and respondent employer argued that an improper formula was utilized. In setting aside the award, the court held that the wrong formula was used because the record did not support the conclusion that the deceased held the same position during each of his prior periods of employment with his employer. Although Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1041(B) did not prescribe any formula to determine the amount which reasonably represented the monthly earning capacity of a decedent in the employment in which he was working at the time of the accident, the decedent's earning capacity could have been determined from similar employees' actual wages. Further, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1046(C) was held constitutional because its construction would not be extended so as to infringe upon the Constitution of the United States or to restrict the states' inherent powers.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the award that determined decedent's average monthly wage, and the administrative law judge was to apply any of the three formulas identified. The challenged statute violated neither the Supremacy Clause nor the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution.

 

1148 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


SHALIMAR ASSN. v. D.O.C. ENTERPRISES


No. 1 CA-CIV 5330


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


142 Ariz. 36; 688 P.2d 682; 1984 Ariz. App. LEXIS 615



March 27, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied May 8, 1984. Review Denied September 18, 1984.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, homeowners association, brought an action to declare and enforce against defendants, new owners, an implied restriction that limited the use of property to a golf course. The trial court ruled for the homeowners association, finding that the property was restricted to a golf course operation and that an implied covenant restricting the use of the property to a golf course arose from the sale of adjacent lots to the homeowners.


OVERVIEW: The property in question was a residential land development that consisted of a golf course and adjacent residential lots. Although no restrictions were placed against the golf course itself, other restrictions included references to golf course restrictions. The court distinguished a case that held that an equitable servitude in favor of one parcel of land and against another must have been created by a written instrument, finding that the dispute on the restrictions was against lot owners, whereas this case involved lot owners against the developer. The court found that both estoppel and part performance applied to the golf course restriction to take it out of the statute of frauds, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-101(6), because the developer had orally represented to the homeowners that the golf course retained by them was subject to restrictions until the year 2025. Thus, the parol evidence rule did not apply. The court found that the implied restrictive covenant was enforceable against the new owners as subsequent purchasers who took their ownership with notice of the restriction. The court found that changed circumstances did not warrant abrogating the restriction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1149 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Arizona Downs v. Turf Paradise


No. 1 CA-CIV 6045


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


140 Ariz. 438; 682 P.2d 443; 1984 Ariz. App. LEXIS 533



March 13, 1984 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant horse racetrack appealed and plaintiff horse racetrack cross-appealed from a judgment entered by the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), which affirmed the decision of the state racing commission (commission) concerning the allocation of racing dates, but reversed the orders that required plaintiff to pay a portion of the maintenance expenses, and allowed the commission to resolve any disputes regarding the hiring of officials.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's reversal of the commission's decision that required plaintiff to pay a prorata share of the maintenance costs of the facility at which plaintiff held its racing meeting because the commission abused its discretion in its unauthorized attempt to require plaintiff to assume obligations exceeding those agreed to by the parties. The court affirmed the trial court's ruling and held that the commission lacked the statutory authority to dictate to the parties which particular racing officials they would employ, so long as the employed officials were qualified under the applicable rules and statutes. The court rejected defendant's argument that the employment issue was not ripe for consideration; the court also held that the issue was an exception to the mootness doctrine because the issue was capable of repetition, yet evaded review. The court dismissed plaintiff's cross-appeal as moot and held that further consideration of the validity of the racing preference statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 5-110(A), was not merited because the state supreme court upheld, while this appeal was pending, the validity of § 5-110(A) and the parties' agreement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and dismissed plaintiff's cross-appeal as moot.

DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the decision of the Pima County Superior Court (Arizona) dismissing the criminal charge against defendant because Tucson City Code §11-28(3) was void for vagueness and therefore unconstitutional.

Honorable Richard J. Riley, Former Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the trial court (Arizona) for driving while intoxicated while his license was suspended in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692. Defendant was sentenced to six months in jail.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of driving while intoxicated while his license was suspended. On appeal, the court reversed defendant's conviction. 1152 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Swainston


No. 2 CA-CR 3100


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two


139 Ariz. 95; 676 P.2d 1153; 1984 Ariz. App. LEXIS 342



January 27, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Pinal County

Cause No. 10013

Honorable E. D. McBryde, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART

VACATED AND REMANDED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court of Pinal County (Arizona) for aggravated assault, criminal damage, and driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor. Defendant was sentenced in absentia.


OVERVIEW: While defendant's appeal was pending, the Arizona Supreme Court issued an opinion that a sentence could not be imposed on a convicted defendant in absentia, unless there were extraordinary circumstances. Based on the supreme court opinion, the court vacated defendant's sentence. Defendant also contended that under Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 24 he had a right to a speedy public trial by an impartial jury of the county in which the offense was alleged to have been committed. The superior court denied the motion because under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-109(B)(5), which provided that if an offense was committed within one mile of a boundary, trial may be held in any of the counties concerned, allowed the offense to be tried in the county. The constitutional provision was not designed to establish venue, but rather to preserve the right to an unbiased jury. The court found that the constitutional provision and § 13-109(B)(5) had as their basis the preservation of different rights. Thus, defendant did not carry his burden of showing beyond a reasonable doubt that § 13-109(B)(5) was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for aggravated assault, criminal damage, and driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, but vacated the sentence and remanded for resentencing when defendant was present.

In re Appeal in Maricopa County Juvenile Action


No. 1 CA-JUV 222


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


139 Ariz. 170; 677 P.2d 943; 1984 Ariz. App. LEXIS 349



January 19, 1984 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied February 28, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. J-92130

The Honorable C. Kimball Rose, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which committed defendant to the Department of Corrections, imposed a monetary assessment, and ordered restitution.


OVERVIEW: The lower court, in ordering defendant to pay restitution and in imposing a monetary assessment applied the newly effective amendment to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-241(C). The question on appeal was whether the amendment to the statute operated as an ex post facto law when applied to acts that occurred before its effective date. Defendant argued that the retroactive application of the statute operated as an ex post fact law in violation of U.S. Const. art. 1, §§ 9 and 10 and Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 25. The State admitted that the statute was applied retroactively, but argued that the statute did not violate the prohibition against ex post facto laws because it was not penal in nature. The court found that the amendment did operate as an ex post facto law and, therefore, reversed that portion of the trial court's order that imposed a monetary assessment and restitution. The statute was retrospective and disadvantaged the offender. The court affirmed that portion of the order that committed defendant to the Department of Corrections.


OUTCOME: The reversed the order requiring defendant to pay an assessment and restitution and affirmed the portion of the order that committed defendant to the Department of Corrections.

State v. Book-Cellar, Inc.


No. 1 CA-CIV 6390


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


139 Ariz. 525; 679 P.2d 548; 1984 Ariz. App. LEXIS 360



January 19, 1984 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. C-437338

The Honorable B. Michael Dann, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed the city's action against appellee bookstore and determined that Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 12-814(B), (E), 12-815, 12-616 were unconstitutional. The city also challenged the summary judgment granted in favor of the bookstore in its action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the decision to quash an ex parte temporary restraining order.


OVERVIEW: The city brought an action against the bookstore, which sought to abate an alleged nuisance and enjoin its maintenance, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-811 et seq. The city obtained an ex parte temporary restraining order and applied for a preliminary injunction. The court affirmed the decision to quash the temporary restraining order, but reversed and remanded the granting of the motion to dismiss and for summary judgment. Section 12-814(B) was not an unconstitutional prior restraint because the purpose of the temporary restraining order was to preserve evidence. However, the temporary restraining order was properly quashed because it did not meet the requirements of Ariz. R. Civ. P. 65(h). The preliminary injunction that was permitted under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-814(E) was not an unconstitutional prior restraint because it provided for adequate procedural safeguards. The court imposed a 60-day maximum limit on the time between the injunction and the final adjudication of the underlying merits of the action. The court held that the provision of § 12-816, which provided for destruction of certain items, was unconstitutional. The rest of the challenged statutes were upheld.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision to quash the temporary restraining order. The court reversed the dismissal of the city's action and the summary judgment granted in favor of the bookstore in its action under § 1983. The case was remanded to the trial court.

 

1155 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Shockey v. Industrial Comm'n


No. 1 CA-IC 2947


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


140 Ariz. 113; 680 P.2d 823; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 736



December 30, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reconsideration Denied February 22, 1984. Review Denied May 10, 1984.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee challenged an award by respondent Industrial Commission of Arizona concluding that she was entitled to temporary total benefits to a set date and that her back condition became stationary with no permanent impairment as of that date. Respondent carrier terminated her benefits on the same date. The employee argued that the provisions of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-943.F (Supp. 1983) for making a decision upon review were mandatory.


OVERVIEW: The employee contended that the administrative law judge lacked jurisdiction to issue a decision when the 60-day period for filing a review had expired. The court disagreed and affirmed. The review decision was filed more than 60 days after the date that the employer requested the review. However, the court found that the language of § 23-934.F. (Supp. 1983) was directive but not mandatory. Failure to issue the decision within 60 days did not divest the judge of jurisdiction. Further, the decision was only seven days late. The judge had to ultimately decide whether or not the employee's condition was stationary without permanent impairment. There was conflicting medical evidence and the judge's decision that stated that he considered and resolved all conflicts was specific enough to adequately dispose of the material issues. There was sufficient medical evidence in the record to support the finding that the employee's condition was stationary with no permanent impairment. The judge lacked authority to authorize the benefits for surgery that was performed when the award was still on administrative review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award.

 

1156 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Tanque Verde Enters. v. Tucson


No. 2 CA-CIV 4781


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two


142 Ariz. 544; 691 P.2d 310; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 735



December 30, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY

Cause No. 195770

Honorable Lillian S. Fisher, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED & SET ASIDE WITH DIRECTIONS IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) finding unconstitutional the original Tucson, Ariz., Code § 19-28(149) (original ordinance), which imposed an occupational license tax on swap meet proprietors, including appellee proprietor. The proprietor cross-appealed the trial court's judgment that the amended Tucson, Ariz., Code § 19-28(149) (amended ordinance) was valid.


OVERVIEW: The proprietor paid the occupational license taxes under protest and brought an action against the city, claiming that the original and amended ordinances were unconstitutional because they were confiscatory. The trial court found that the original ordinance was unconstitutional but that the amended ordinance was valid. On appeal, the court vacated the finding that the original ordinance was unconstitutional. The proprietor had not attempted to collect the tax, and so its arguments as to the tax's effects were speculative. The proprietor's survey of the vendors and testimony by an economist did not suffice to show beyond a reasonable doubt that the original ordinance was confiscatory. The original ordinance was an exercise of the power to raise revenue and not regulatory. The court affirmed the trial court's finding that the amended ordinance was valid. In so doing, the court rejected the proprietor's argument that the state constitution required occupational license taxes to be at the same rate as sales taxes. The city's council's decision to classify swap meet operators differently from retail merchants and peddlers was not arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the part of the trial court's judgment that had held that the original ordinance was arbitrary and confiscatory. The court affirmed the part of the trial court's judgment that had held that the amended ordinance was valid.

State v. Buchholz


No. 2 CA-CR 2693


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two


139 Ariz. 303; 678 P.2d 488; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 687



November 7, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 28, 1983. Review Denied March 6, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County

Cause No. CR-05264

Honorable John G. Hawkins, Judge

Honorable Thomas Meehan, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which found defendant guilty of five counts of attempted theft, in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1802(A)(5), following jury verdicts.


OVERVIEW: The police equipped an officer with electronic recording and listening devices. The officer went to defendant's place of business and offered to sell him stolen property. Defendant accepted offers on at least five occasions. The attempted thefts fell within the definition in § 13-1802(A)(5). On appeal, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his convictions, that the trial court improperly allowed evidence of prior bad actions, that the prosecutor's closing argument was improper, and that § 13-604(H) was unconstitutional. On review, the court affirmed the judgment and held that: (1) there was more than sufficient evidence of value to support the theft classification; (2) the testimony strongly implied prior criminal conduct by defendant of the same nature as the charges in the case and even without that evidence, the jury would have found defendant guilty; (3) the prosecutor's argument that without a market for what a burglar steals there would be fewer burglaries was well within the limits allowed; and (4) § 13-604(H), which allowed sentencing in accordance with prior convictions, did not violate the equal protection clause, and it was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1158 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Zack


Nos. 1 CA-CR 6297, 1 CA-CR 6391


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


138 Ariz. 266; 674 P.2d 329; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 629



October 27, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 4, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. LCA-23125

The Honorable James Moeller, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the operators of a scrap metal processing plant, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which affirmed the judgments of the municipal court finding that the operators had committed three misdemeanors in violation of the Phoenix, Ariz., Zoning Code, Ordinance G-449, Appendix A, §§ 400, 421(A)(1) and 107(B).


OVERVIEW: The appeal attacked as being unconstitutionally vague a City of Phoenix ordinance which prohibited certain types of land use in a heavy industrial district zoned A-2. They raised three issues for the court's consideration: 1. that Phoenix, Ariz., Zoning Code, Ordinance G-449, Appendix A, § 421(A)(1) was void for vagueness or uncertainty, 2. that the ordinance was discriminatorily enforced against the operators, and 3. that the state was estopped from enforcing the ordinance against the operators. On appeal, the court found that the term "offensive vibration" was not ambiguous and was susceptible to a practical definition. Thus, the court could not accept the operators' position that a person of ordinary intelligence would fail to understand what was proscribed by the terms of the zoning ordinance. Further, there was no question in this case that the vibrations emanating from the operators' lot were unpleasant to the neighboring businesses. The court also held that the contention that the vibrations would not have been offensive to persons employed by neighboring iron foundries or slaughterhouses was speculative at best. The court found that the ordinance was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments and sentences.

 

1159 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Lake Havasu City v. Mohave County


No. 1 CA-CIV 6497


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


138 Ariz. 552; 675 P.2d 1371; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 641



October 20, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 17, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Mohave County

Cause No. SA-85

The Honorable Leonard C. Langford, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review from the Superior Court of Mohave County (Arizona), which held that appellees, county and related parties, were not obligated, under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 36-190, to provide health-related services to the residents of the city after the city refused to pay a requested contribution for the health services. The city contended that the county was obligated to provide the services and also violated equal protection laws.


OVERVIEW: The county provided health services to the city, and the county health department requested a cost contribution from the city in return for continuation of the health services to the residents. The city refused to pay the contribution and filed a complaint seeking an order requiring the county to continue supplying the health services. The county filed a motion for summary judgment, and the trial court granted the motion. The city appealed, and the court affirmed. The court held that the county was not required to provide the contested health services to the city and, if it did, it could lawfully charge the city for those services because Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 36-190 did not obligate the county to provide health services to residents of the city at no charge. The court held that it was not a violation of equal protection laws to allow the county to require a cost contribution from the city, where identical services were provided to residents of the county living outside the corporate limits of the city without any additional charge. The taxpayers could not base valid equal protection claims on the fact that they did not receive tax monies to the same extent as other citizens.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and held that the county was not required to provide the contested health services to the city and, if it did, it could lawfully charge the city for those services.

State v. Olea


Nos. 1 CA-CR 5911, 1 CA-CR 5915, 1 CA-CR 5916, 1 CA-CR 5930

139 Ariz. 280; 678 P.2d 465; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 683



October 18, 1983

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

The Honorable Stephen H. Scott, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) convicting them of numerous counts of furnishing narcotic drugs and conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted for conspiring to possess, transport, import, sell, furnish, and offering to transport and furnish heroin. Through a series of wiretaps, the investigators uncovered the chain of defendants' narcotics operation. On appeal of defendants' convictions, the court affirmed. The trial court did not err by refusing to suppress the wiretaps. Evidence showed that the officers minimized their interceptions of non-pertinent calls as required, and the fact that the tapes of the conversations were sealed late did not require their suppress because defense counsel specifically stated that there was no suggestion that tape's integrity had been affected. The court held that the applications for the wiretaps were sufficient because even though they were labeled as amendments they conformed with the statutory requirements for applications, and they showed that the wiretaps were necessary and that there was probable cause. The Arizona Wiretap Statute, former Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1057, violated neither U.S. Const. amend. IV, U.S. Const. art. VI, nor 18 U.S.C.S. § 2510 et seq. The evidence was sufficient to support defendants' convictions.


OUTCOME: Defendants' narcotics and conspiracy convictions were affirmed.

St. Joseph's Hosp. & Medical Ctr. v. Maricopa County


No. 1 CA-CIV 5969


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


138 Ariz. 127; 673 P.2d 325; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 579



October 4, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. C-389354

The Honorable A. Melvin McDonald, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county appealed the order from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted appellee private hospital's motion for summary judgment in the hospital's action to recover for the care of two indigent patients, a child and an adult, who had been hospitalized for emergency treatment.


OVERVIEW: The hospital admitted for emergency treatment a child and an indigent adult. When the child later became indigent due to the hospital bill, the hospital notified the county pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 11-297.01. At the time the patient was not medically transferable. The child's parents initially refused to consent to the transfer, but did consent 12 days after the child had been declared transferable. The hospital filed a successful action against the county to recover at the full rate the services provided to the indigent patients, after the county paid the adult's costs only at the Medicare/Medicaid rate and refused to pay the child's bill due to his parent's initial refusal to transfer him. On appeal, the court affirmed the order with respect to the reimbursement allowed for the adult's emergency treatment and reversed and remanded with respect to the costs incurred from the time the child became indigent to the date of his transfer. The court held that the hospital was entitled to full reimbursement for emergency treatment, but where a service was provided under other than emergency conditions, it was entitled to reimbursement only at the Medicare/Medicaid rate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed as to the reimbursement allowed on behalf of the indigent adult and reversed with respect to the amount of reimbursement allowed on behalf of the indigent child. The court remanded the case to the trial court to determine the amount due on behalf of the indigent child from the time he became indigent to the date of his transfer, for which coverage was to be allowed at the Medicare/Medicaid rate.

Stirewalt v. P.P.G. Indus.


No. 1 CA-CIV 6075


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


138 Ariz. 257; 674 P.2d 320; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 624



October 4, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 4, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. C-413449

The Honorable Morris Rozar, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a widow and her minor children, appealed a summary judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed their wrongful death suit against defendant corporations. The trial court also denied a motion to set aside the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was fatally injured in the course and scope of his employment. The widow and children received workers' compensation death benefits but did not file a personal injury suit within one year from the date of injury. Consequently, the claim was automatically assigned by operation of law to the insurance carrier. The carrier reassigned the claim to the widow and children before the expiration of the personal injury limitations period. While the wrongful death action was pending, the Arizona Supreme Court, in an unrelated case, held that a claim assigned to an insurance carrier by operation of law could not be reassigned. As a result, summary judgment dismissing the action was entered. Thereafter, an amendment to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-1023(B), which contained a retroactive provision, authorized the reassignment of an assigned claim. The trial court denied a motion to set aside the summary judgment on that basis. The court, in reversing, held that the retroactive provision did not violate due process because there was no vested right to the defense of nonassignability of tort claims. The retroactive provision of the amended statute did not create a new substantive right.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

The Honorable Stanley Z. Goodfarb, Judge

Rev. Stat. § 12-901 et seq.


OVERVIEW: A denturist was charged with unprofessional conduct and his certificate for the practice of denture technology was suspended by the board. The court held that the disciplinary actions taken against the denturist were voidable.

The court directed that, on remand, the matter be returned to the complaint investigatory stage, where the matter was first submitted to the board.

Tuzon v. MacDougall


No. 1 CA-HC 60


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


137 Ariz. 482; 671 P.2d 923; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 545



August 9, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 16, 1983. Review Denied November 1, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. C-453604

The Honorable David G. Derickson, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) that denied his request for the issuance of a writ of habeas corpus to free him from the custody of the department of corrections.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed a request for the issuance of a writ of habeas corpus to free him from the custody of the department of corrections. The inmate contended that he was promised a commutation of the sentence he was serving for second degree murder in return for his cooperation in connection with cases arising out of a prison escape. The trial court denied his request for the issuance of a writ of habeas corpus. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court determined that the inmate did not have an agreement with any person or persons who were authorized by law to effect his release. The court agreed with the trial court's finding that even if the chairman of the board of pardons and paroles made a promise, he had no authority to speak for other members of the board and no enforceable agreement arose thereby. The court held that the trial court did not err in failing sua sponte to appoint counsel to represent the inmate and in refusing to allow advisory counsel to sit with the inmate. The court found no reversible error with respect to the trial court's evidentiary rulings and determined that the inmate received a full and very fair hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that denied the inmate's request for the issuance of a writ of habeas corpus. The court remanded the cause to the trial court with directions to order the clerk thereof to refund any filing fee paid in this case.

 

1167 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fowler


Nos. 1 CA-CR 5529, 1 CA-CR 6246-PR


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


137 Ariz. 381; 670 P.2d 1205; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 547



July 26, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 27, 1983. Review Denied October 18, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. CR-117954

A Petition for Review of Action of the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. CR-117954

The Honorable David G. Derickson, Judge

The Honorable Marilyn A. Riddel, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction and sentence by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) for sexual assault with one prior felony conviction following the entry of his Alford plea. Defendant alleged that the apparent inability of the prosecutrix to appear at trial invalidated his Alford plea and that the State failed to file a timely motion to allege his prior convictions under Ariz. R. Crim. P. 16.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with sexual assault with two prior felonies in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1406. Defendant entered an Alford plea on the day before the trial was to have begun. Defendant learned that the prosecutrix, who moved to another state, would have been unavailable to testify. Defendant alleged that prosecutrix's failure to return to Arizona constituted a recantation of her allegations and invalidated his plea. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. Defendant's allegation of a recantation by the prosecutrix was speculative and his plea was knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily made. The plea was not vulnerable to attack based on the mistake of fact that the prosecutrix was to have been available to testify. The State had no knowledge that the prosecutrix was not going to return to Arizona at the time of the entry of the plea. Given the terms of the plea, the trial court did not have to rule on an allegation of a prior conviction filed by the State outside of the time limits stated in Ariz. R. Crim. P. 16.1. The sentence required modification to provide for a term of imprisonment and not commitment to the Arizona Department of Corrections.


OUTCOME: The court modified defendant's sentence from commitment to the Arizona Department of Corrections to a sentence of imprisonment and affirmed as modified his conviction and sentence by the trial court for sexual assault with one prior felony conviction.

 

1168 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Benally


No. 1 CA-CR 6608


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


137 Ariz. 253; 669 P.2d 1030; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 524



July 21, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 29, 1983. Review Denied September 27, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Coconino County

Cause No. CR-9931

The Honorable John H. Grace, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the imposition of a six-month prison term as a condition of his suspended sentence following his conviction by the Superior Court of Coconino County (Arizona) for driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor while on a revoked operator's license in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692.02 (amended 1982).


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the six-month prison sentence imposed by the trial court under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692.02(A) (amended 1982) as a condition of his suspended sentence and probation was in conflict with Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-901, which addressed the granting of probation. On appeal, the court affirmed the sentence imposed by the trial court and found that the relevant statutory provisions, construed in pari materia, yielded the result reached by the trial court. Under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692.02(A) (amended 1982), the Arizona Legislature sought to impose more severe penalties on those drivers who operated vehicles under the influence, and for drivers who did so while their licenses were revoked, a six-month term of imprisonment was required. Under § 28-692.02(A), probation or release on any other basis was not allowed except upon the condition of a minimum six-month prison term. Section 28-692.02(A) was a special statute and did not conflict with the general provisions related to the granting of probation under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-901. The court found defendant's claim that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-692 (amended 1982) was unconstitutionally vague was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's imposition of defendant's suspended sentence and probation conditioned upon his imprisonment for six months following his conviction for driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor.

 

1169 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Newell


No. 2 CA-CR 2862


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two


137 Ariz. 354; 670 P.2d 1178; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 551



June 14, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 30, 1983. Review Denied October 25, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY

Cause No. CR-08044

Honorable Thomas Meehan, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County, Arizona, which convicted him of theft of property and fraudulent use of a credit card.


OVERVIEW: Defendant rented a car from an agency and failed to return it. One month later he was arrested. At trial, the rental agreement was entered into evidence and the jury took it with them when deliberating. The agreement stated that if the car was not returned within 72 hours the renter would be subject to 1.9 years imprisonment or a fine. Defendant argued that it was error for the jury to have before it an exhibit having information regarding punishment. He also argued that the trial court should have instructed the jury on the lesser-included offense of unlawful failure to return rental property. The court affirmed, holding that admission of the exhibit was not fundamental error. It did not go to the foundation of the case or take from defendant a right essential to his defense. Further, because admission was not fundamental error, defendant waived his right to appeal because he failed to object at trial. The court held that unlawful failure to return rental property was not a lesser-included offense of theft because theft could be committed without committing the other crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Barrio v. San Manuel Div. Hosp. for Magma Copper Co.


No. 2 CA-CIV 4651


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two


143 Ariz. 111; 692 P.2d 290; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 738



June 13, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PINAL COUNTY

Cause No. 33385

Honorable E. D. McBryde, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Pinal County (Arizona), which awarded summary judgment to defendants, the hospital and doctors, in the patient's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: When the patient was 20 years old, she filed a medical malpractice action against two doctors alleging that their medical care in connection with her birth caused serious and permanent injuries. Liability on the part of the hospital was alleged based on the theory of respondeat superior. The hospital and doctors filed a motion for summary judgment on the ground that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-564(D), the three-year statute of limitations for children's malpractice claims, barred the action. The trial court awarded summary judgment to the hospital and doctors, and the court affirmed. The court held that the rational basis test was applicable in testing the statute's constitutionality under an equal protection analysis because the legally imposed status of minority was not a suspect classification. The statute satisfied the rational basis test and was not unconstitutional. Therefore the three-year limitations period applied, and the patient's action was time-barred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of summary judgment for the hospital and doctors in the patient's medical malpractice action.

 

1171 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wolfe


No. 1 CA-CR 5978


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


137 Ariz. 133; 669 P.2d 111; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 487



June 9, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 17, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Yuma County

Cause No. CR10757

Cause No. CR-10758

The Honorable B. L. Helm, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentences affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants were convicted in a justice court of various gaming violations. Appellants sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Yuma County (Arizona), which affirmed their convictions and sentences. Appellants challenged the constitutional validity of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 17-211, which enabled game wardens to conduct warrantless searches in certain circumstances.


OVERVIEW: The issue on appeal, as framed by appellants, was that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 17-211 was unconstitutional on its face because it authorized a warrantless search without probable cause. Appellants premised their argument on the fact that § 17-211(D)(3) used the term "sufficient cause" when it referred to the authority of game rangers and wildlife managers to conduct searches without warrants. On appeal, the court disagreed with the arguments of appellants and upheld the constitutionality of the statute. The court reasoned that while § 17-211, appeared to place game rangers and wildlife managers in a separate category apart from other law enforcement officers it could not place them above the state and federal constitutions. The court construed the statute in a manner that subjected game rangers and wildlife managers to exactly the same constitutional constraints that all law enforcement officers were subject to observe. As the court construed the statute it was a codification of some of the common law exceptions to the search warrant requirement as developed in case law precedent.


OUTCOME: The convictions and the sentences were affirmed.

 

1172 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Kenyon v. Hammer


No. 1 CA-CIV 5518


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


142 Ariz. 124; 688 P.2d 1016; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 728



May 12, 1983 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the Superior Court of Mohave County

Cause No. C-14932

The Honorable Gary R. Pope, Judge



DISPOSITION: REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents' challenged a summary judgment from the Mohave County Superior Court (Arizona), which dismissed the claim on the grounds that the statute of limitations barred the action. A nurse erroneously wrote in the mother's chart that her blood type was Rh positive rather than Rh negative, resulting in not receiving RhoGAM immediately after delivery. The parents' second child was born dead and the mother required a tubal ligation.


OVERVIEW: The parents' claims in their medical malpractice action were for the wrongful death of the second baby and for personal injuries sustained by the mother, including medical expenses associated with her second pregnancy and the tubal ligation, and damages for the resulting sterility. Both claims were based on the doctor's employee's alleged negligence in incorrectly recording the mother's blood type. The court reversed the trial court's dismissal and asserted that the matter was not barred by the three-year statute of limitations. The court explained that no injury occurred to the mother until she either conceived or gave birth to her second child. The court found that had she not become pregnant a second time, no injury would have resulted. However, the court observed that ultimately the date of injury to the deceased child was the relevant trigger for the statute of limitations, not the date of injury to the mother. The court noted that injury to the deceased child could not have occurred prior to the date the child was conceived.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, as the parents' claims of medical malpractice were not barred by the statute of limitations, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

In re Appeal in Maricopa County Juvenile Action


No. 1 CA-JUV 195


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


140 Ariz. 27; 680 P.2d 163; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 707



May 3, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted June 23, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. A-27789

The Honorable C. Kimball Rose, Judge



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an aunt and uncle who were seeking to adopt their niece and nephew, challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which dismissed the adoption petition for lack of jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Before the filing of the adoption petition, the children had been adjudicated to be dependent minor children and had been made wards of the juvenile court in another county, with temporary custody awarded to a grandmother. Consequently, the trial court ordered that the adoption petition be dismissed for lack of jurisdiction. The court, in affirming, held that under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-202, the juvenile court that had found the children to be dependent children had exclusive jurisdiction over the children until such time as they were released as wards of that court. The later filing of an adoption petition did not divest the juvenile court of its continuing jurisdiction over the two dependent minor children. The court observed that where two courts had concurrent jurisdiction, the first court to acquire such jurisdiction retained it to the exclusion of the other until the case was finally determined. It would not have been in the best interests of the minor children or of an orderly judicial process for the trial court to assume jurisdiction in an adoption proceeding when there was a dependency proceeding that involved the same children in a different juvenile court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the adoption petition.

Haralambie v. Pima County


No. 2 CA-CIV 4626


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two


137 Ariz. 207; 669 P.2d 984; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 517



April 27, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 1, 1983. Review Denied September 13, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY

Cause No. 199717

Honorable Harry Gin, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorneys challenged the order of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) granting the motion of appellee county for summary judgment in an action brought by the attorneys. The attorneys sued under a contract theory to recover fees for the representation, as appointed counsel, of an indigent father and his children in a dependency proceeding and in a termination of parental rights proceeding.


OVERVIEW: A juvenile court judge issued orders authorizing compensation for the attorneys in excess of the limit imposed by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-225(A) for representing indigent parties. The county refused to pay the ordered compensation and the attorneys brought suit under a contract theory. The trial court granted the county's motion for summary judgment, and the court affirmed. The court refused to accept the attorneys' contention that § 8-225(A) was unconstitutional. Any remedy in this regard had to be obtained from the legislature and the court noted that, in fact, § 8-225(A) had been revised, subsequent to the proceedings that gave rise to the case, to delete the limit. The court appreciated the juvenile court judge's concern that court appointed counsel had to be adequately compensated for representing parties and children before the juvenile court. In spite of this desire to be equitable, the court concluded that it had to find that the juvenile court judge's orders were void ab initio. He simply did not have the authority to substitute his concept for what the law ought to be for what the statute said the law actually was.


OUTCOME: The trial court's grant of summary judgment was affirmed.

 

1175 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Godfrey


No. 1 CA-CR 5850


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


136 Ariz. 471; 666 P.2d 1080; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 468



April 21, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 2, 1983. Review Denied July 6, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Superior Court of Navajo County

Cause No. CR-6515

The Honorable Jay M. Abbey, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, following a jury trial in the Superior Court of Navajo County (Arizona), for theft. Defendant contended, inter alia, that the trial court's failure to swear the jury until the beginning of deliberations rendered the verdict a nullity.


OVERVIEW: The oath required by Ariz. R. Crim. P. 18.6(b) was not administered to the jury until after the trial was complete and shortly before the jury began its deliberations. Defendant contended that this error rendered the jury's verdict a nullity. The court disagreed and affirmed defendant's conviction. The court reviewed the decisions of other jurisdictions and concluded that the apparent majority rule was that a failure to swear the jury until the case had commenced was generally harmless error, at least, where there was no actual prejudice shown and the oath was administered prior to deliberations. The court found that the failure to administer the oath prior to trial was a technical violation of rule 18.6(b) but, because the jurors were sworn prior to their deliberations, and there was no manifest appearance or suggestion that the jurors disregarded their obligations, the court concluded that no reversible error was committed in this case. The court also found that a delay in defendant's initial appearance, 18 days after his incarceration, which was contrary to the requirements of Ariz. R. Crim. P. 4.1, did not entitle defendant to dismissal of the charges against him.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for theft was affirmed.

 

1176 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Earby


No. 1 CA-CR 5598


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


136 Ariz. 246; 665 P.2d 590; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 444



April 14, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 10, 1983. Review Denied June 22, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. CR-116832

The Honorable Howard V. Peterson, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction entered on a jury verdict in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) of manslaughter. Defendant claimed that the trial court gave improper instructions dealing with intent, flight, and self-defense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued with the victim. The victim ran from defendant whereupon defendant shot the victim twice. Defendant left the scene, spent the night with a friend, and then left the state. Defendant claimed that the instruction on general intent unconstitutionally shifted the burden of proof to defendant, that the flight instruction should not have been given because there was no evidence that defendant left the scene of the crime to evade arrest or that leaving the state was an attempted concealment and that it was error to refuse to give his tendered instruction on self-defense. The court affirmed. The instruction on intent created merely a permissive inference that allowed, but did not require the jury to infer intent from the commission of the act, and placed no burden on defendant. Merely leaving the scene of a crime was not sufficient evidence to support a flight instruction, but the jury was free to disbelieve defendant's explanation and infer that his actions were evidence of concealment. The jury was fully charged on the issue of self-defense. The trial court was not required to single out for special instruction the point made by defendant's requested instruction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SUPERIOR COURT OF PIMA COUNTY

Cause No. CR-02292

Honorable William E. Druke, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction following a jury trial by the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) for multiple counts of armed robbery, kidnapping, aggravated assault, and theft. The State filed an allegation of prior conviction and dangerous nature for enhancement of punishment. The trial court sentenced defendant to consecutive and concurrent sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction resulted from a series of robberies. The trial court initially found defendant incompetent to stand trial but found him competent several months later. The trial court denied a motion further competency proceedings under Ariz. R. Crim. P. 11.1 after defendant made a suicide attempt. On appeal, the court affirmed.
