The trial judge proceeded over the prior competency proceedings and was in a position to determine whether reasonable grounds for further proceedings were present. The denial of a continuance to allow the defense to secure the attendance of a witness was proper where there was no showing that the witness's testimony would have changed the verdict. Defendant's past conduct justified an order to inconspicuously shackle him to his chair during the trial. The sentence was in compliance with Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-708, 13-702(C). Defendant failed to establish that perjured testimony at trial entitled him to post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences by the trial court for armed robbery, kidnapping, aggravated assault, and theft.

Arizona Lotus Corp. v. Phoenix


No. 1 CA-CIV 5494


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department D


136 Ariz. 22; 663 P.2d 1013; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 426; 40 A.L.R.4th 1103



March 24, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 4, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. C-373229

The Honorable Roger G. Strand, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a group of Phoenix broadcasters and a billboard company, sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which determined that appellee city properly assessed taxes on appellants' revenues from national advertising and spot religious announcements. The city filed a cross-appeal challenging the superior court's finding that appellants' production revenues were not taxable.


OVERVIEW: The city assessed taxes against appellants pursuant to the city's privilege tax under the Phoenix, Ariz., City Code (code). The lower court found that the taxes on national advertising and spot religious announcements were permissible, but held that the appellants' production revenues were not taxable. Appellants and the city both sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the order in part and reversed it in part. The court held that even though there was a history of administrative interpretation and practice restricting the application of the city's privilege tax to local advertising revenues, § 14-44 of the code clearly permitted taxing on all advertising without a distinction between "local" or "national." The court reversed the superior court's finding that spot religious announcements were taxable and held that the announcements were not taxable because those people listening to the announcements were not "prospective purchasers" within the meaning of the code. The court affirmed the superior court's ruling that production revenues were not taxable because the transaction of filming commercials did not constitute a sale of tangible personal property as defined by the code.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order, holding that the city properly assessed taxes on appellants' national advertising and that the city could not assess taxes on appellants' production revenues. The court reversed the order permitting the city's tax on appellants' spot religious announcements.

Sample v. Sample


No. 1 CA-CIV 5546


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


135 Ariz. 599; 663 P.2d 591; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 423



February 24, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 6, 1983. Review Denied May 17, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. DR-97794

The Honorable Robert W. Pickrell, Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part; affirmed in part; remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife sought review of portions of a judgment and decree of dissolution from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which terminated her marriage to appellee husband. The wife appealed a denial of her motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife moved to Arizona in 1970 after several years of marriage in noncommunity property states. The husband had interests in a former employer's stock and a corporate pension fund. The trial court granted the bulk of the employer stock to the husband as separate property after applying Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-318 (as amended) and concluding that the laws of the state where the stock was acquired should apply where the stock was acquired before 1973. An amendment was made to § 25-318 after judgment was rendered which gave the statute retroactive application, and which, if applicable, would have treated the stock as quasi-community property. The trial court denied the wife's motion that sought to have the amendment applied. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the amendment could be applied on appeal where the judgment was not yet final. The legislature intended that the retroactivity provision of the amendment caused § 25-318 to apply to property acquired before 1973 and thus treat the stock as quasi-community property. The court affirmed the trial court's division of the corporate pension fund.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part and remanded the case to the trial court for entry of a revised judgment consistent with its opinion.

 

1180 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


De Boer v. Brown


No. 2 CA-CIV 4642


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two


138 Ariz. 178; 673 P.2d 922; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 618



January 17, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 11, 1983. Review Granted June 10, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: SPECIAL ACTION PROCEEDINGS

RELIEF GRANTED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner doctor filed a petition for a special action to challenge respondent trial court's denial of the doctor's motion for summary judgment, which raised the bar of the statute of limitations against medical malpractice action brought by plaintiff patient.


OVERVIEW: The patient's skin cancer was misdiagnosed by the doctor. Four years later, another physician diagnosed the illness. The patient filed an action against the doctor for malpractice. The doctor filed a motion for summary judgment on the grounds that the action was barred by the statute of limitations, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-564. The trial court denied the motion for summary judgment, finding that the statute, placing a three year limit from the time of injury without regard to whether the patient knew of the injury, was unconstitutional. The doctor brought a special action to challenge the respondent court's decision. The court exercised its power and reversed the decision of the trial court. The court determined that the statute was constitutional, violating neither due process or equal protection, because the action of the legislature was entitled to a presumption of constitutionality, the malpractice crisis was a rational reason for the strict limitations, and the court could offer rational reasons for the exceptions to the limitations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and directed the trial court to grant summary judgment in favor of the doctor because the malpractice action was barred by the statute of limitations.

 

1181 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


De Anza Land & Leisure Corp. v. FDIC


No. 1 CA-CIV 5538


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


135 Ariz. 537; 662 P.2d 1044; 1983 Ariz. App. LEXIS 413



January 4, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 2, 1983. Review Denied April 26, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Superior Court of Yavapai County

Cause No. C-28287

The Honorable D. L. Greer, Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee junior lienholder claimed an interest in monies due on a promissory note. Appellant FDIC owned a judgment that affected substantially the same property. The FDIC recorded its judgment in 1961, a month before the lienholder. In 1966, the lienholder sought foreclosure, thus terminating the FDIC judgment as an expired title encumbrance. The Superior Court of Yavapai County (Arizona) entered judgment for the lienholder. The FDIC appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-1612(A), the FDIC filed and recorded an affidavit for renewal of its judgment in 1966. The FDIC filed a second renewal certificate in 1971 and filed a third affidavit in 1976. The lienholder filed its action in 1973. The lienholder contended that the FDIC's judgment had expired and that successive judgment renewals were not permitted. The FDIC filed a motion to dismiss, which the trial court denied. After amendments to § 12-1612, the FDIC renewed its motion for summary judgment in 1976, which the trial court denied. The court held that successive timely judgment renewals had always been authorized by statute in Arizona. Thus, the junior lien never advanced in priority and had always been subordinate to the FDIC's lien. The 1976 amendment to § 12-1612 did not destroy any vested rights of the junior lienholder.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded.

 

1182 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Politte


Nos. 2 CA-CR 2530, 2 CA-CR 2566-2


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two


136 Ariz. 117; 664 P.2d 661; 1982 Ariz. App. LEXIS 691



December 30, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 4, 1983. Review Denied May 24, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Pima County

Cause No. CR-02500

Honorable Thomas Meehan, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona) that convicted them of various narcotics offenses and sentenced them to terms of incarceration. On appeal, they contended that the admission of a co-defendant's declarations under the co-conspirator exception to the hearsay rule denied them their constitutional right to confront the witnesses against them.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were both convicted of various narcotics offenses and of a conspiracy to commit a felony. Other defendants were indicted along with appellants. Appellants contended that the admission of a co-defendant's declarations under the co-conspirator exception to the hearsay rule denied them their constitutional right to confront the witnesses against them inasmuch as the co-defendant would have been available for cross-examination had the state entered into a plea agreement with her before appellants' trial rather than after the close of evidence. The court determined that there was no "unavailability" requirement contained in Ariz. R. Evid. 801(d)(2)(E) that would require the state to demonstrate that the co-defendant was unavailable to testify. The court also held that: (1) the trial court did not err when it denied one appellant's request for an instruction on the crime of facilitation and his motion for severance; (2) the Arizona wiretap statutes were not unconstitutional; and (3) the law enforcement authorities' application for a wiretap pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3010 was not premature given the factual circumstances. Thus, the trial court's judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court judgment that convicted appellants of various narcotics offenses and a conspiracy offense was affirmed.

In re Appeal in Maricopa County Juvenile Action


No. 1 CA-JUV 173


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


134 Ariz. 407; 656 P.2d 1268; 1982 Ariz. App. LEXIS 627



December 7, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 11, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause Nos. JS-4118/JD-529

The Honorable C. Kimball Rose, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) severing her parental rights over her three daughters in a termination action filed by appellee, the Arizona Department of Economic Security, after the daughters were sexually molested by their stepfather.


OVERVIEW: A relative removed the mother's three daughters from her home after it was learned that the girls' stepfather had sexually molested them. The children were eventually placed in foster homes. The mother knew about the abuse, but did not protect her children and refused to establish a home apart from the stepfather. The trial court severed the mother's parental rights. The mother appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the evidence was sufficient to support the trial court's finding that the mother had abandoned her daughters. The court reasoned that the evidence showed that the molestation was likely to recur and that the mother was incapable of preventing it. Further, the stepfather had not undergone therapy and the mother had a history of being unable to defend herself or her children from abuse. The court also found sufficient evidence to support the trial court's implied finding that continuing the children in a dependency status was an inadequate remedy. Further, the court concluded that the stepfather had no legal right to custody or control of the children. Finally, Arizona's termination statutes remained intact despite a recent change in the burden of proof.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment severing the mother's parental rights over her daughters.

Honorable Robert B. Buchanan, Judge

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which ruled in favor of the state and convicted defendant of contributing to the delinquency or dependency of a minor and of two counts of child abuse.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of contributing to the delinquency or dependency of a minor and of child abuse, she appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that the term "endangered" as used within Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-3623(C) was sufficiently clear to allow members of society to comprehend their legal duty and was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of contributing to the delinquency or dependency of a minor and of two counts of child abuse.

State v. Taylor


No. 2 CA-CR 2609


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two


135 Ariz. 262; 660 P.2d 863; 1982 Ariz. App. LEXIS 667



November 19, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 14, 1983. Review Denied March 1, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Gila County

Cause No. CR-7474

Honorable Edward L. Dawson, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Superior Court of Gila County (Arizona) of kidnapping under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1304, aggravated assault, and sexual assault, all with the same victim and all on the same date. Defendant was sentenced to two 20-year and one 3-year concurrent terms of imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that that the kidnapping statutes were unconstitutional; that the trial court erred in permitting the State to call an undisclosed expert witness; that the trial court should have given his requested instructions; and that error occurred in the trial court's finding on the allegation of his prior felony conviction. On appeal, the court found that defendant moved and confined the victim in his automobile with the intent to inflict a sexual offense. The victim was 15 years old and her parents had not acquiesced. A person of average intelligence should have been able to realize and have sufficient warning that such conduct was a violation of the kidnapping statutes. The prosecutor notified defense counsel of the new witness the day before trial, which still allowed four days during trial for possible interviews and other preparation. Thus, there was no error in the trial court's refusal to preclude the witness. The law contained in defendant's requested instructions was no longer viable. Lastly, in the trial court's signed minute entry judgment and sentence the court found that defendant's prior offenses were repetitive and referred to the prior felony conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

In re Contest of Certain Special Election


No. 1 CA-CIV 6254


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


135 Ariz. 149; 659 P.2d 1294; 1982 Ariz. App. LEXIS 652



November 2, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 29, 1982. Review Denied February 23, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. C-435809

The Honorable B. Michael Dann, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant special road districts sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which rejected the districts' challenge to the two-thirds affirmative voting requirement found at Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 18-259(B). The judgment complained of was rendered in the action filed by appellee voters who opposed the districts' proposal to increase the interest rate of certain of the districts' bonds.


OVERVIEW: The districts proposed to increase their bonds' interest rate to make them more attractive to investors. The districts held an election in which approximately 53 per cent of those voting approved the increase. Although Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 18-259(B) provided that bonds could be authorized only upon a two-thirds majority, the districts certified the results of the election to the Board of Supervisors as if they had received the requisite approval. Appellees filed an action challenging the results of the election, and the districts argued that the two-thirds requirement was invalid because it applied only to special road districts. The trial court granted appellees summary judgment and the districts appealed. The court affirmed. The districts argued that where legislation singled out one group for disparate treatment, proponents of the legislation were required to show a compelling state interest to justify it. The court held that so long as a super-majority vote requirement did not discriminate or authorize discrimination against any identifiable class, it did not violate the Constitution. The court stated that proponents of a bond issue were not such an identifiable class.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellees in their action challenging the districts' certification of election results that showed that less than a two-thirds majority of those voting approved the districts' proposal to increase the interest rate of the districts' bonds.

State v. Forrester


No. 1 CA-CR 5462


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B

The Honorable John H. Seidel, Judge

Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-1802, and 22 counts of fraudulent use of a credit card in violation of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-2105.

1188 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Huggins v. Deinhard


No. 1 CA-CIV 5286


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


134 Ariz. 98; 654 P.2d 32; 1982 Ariz. App. LEXIS 553



October 19, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause Nos. C-332987, C-337648 (Consolidated)

The Honorable Charles L. Hardy, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A final judgment of divorce filed in California dissolved the marriage of appellee mother and appellant father. After a California court found the father in arrears in his child support payments, the mother filed suit in the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona) to establish the California decree as a judgment and to garnish the father's Arizona bank account. The father challenged the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the mother.


OVERVIEW: Under a California divorce decree, the father was to pay child support. The father, living overseas, opened a bank account in Arizona. The mother filed a complaint in Arizona to establish the California decree in Arizona as a judgment and sought garnishment of the Arizona bank account to collect unpaid child support. Affirming the grant of summary judgment to the mother, the court held that, as to accrued child support, the California decree ordering support was final and entitled to full faith and credit in the Arizona courts. No motion to revoke or modify the support had been filed in California, and Cal. Civ. Code § 4700(a) (Supp. 1982) showed that past due child support was not subject to modification. Further, there was no unfairness in allowing the mother to realize on that debt in Arizona where the father had property, whether or not the Arizona court would have jurisdiction to determine the existence of the debt originally. The court found no error in the garnishment procedures employed or in the trial court's denial of the father's motion to quash because he was given personal notice of the garnishment and had an opportunity to present his defenses to the writ's issuance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's entry of summary judgment in favor of the mother.

 

1189 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


Trujillo v. Superior Court


No. 2 CA-CIV 4563


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two


134 Ariz. 355; 656 P.2d 644; 1982 Ariz. App. LEXIS 676



October 19, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 26, 1982. Review Denied January 7, 1983.



DISPOSITION: No error.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner tenant filed a special action challenging a decision by respondent superior court (Arizona), which found in favor of respondents, housing authority, landlord, and others, by upholding the constitutionality of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-1179, which required the tenant to post a bond in a detainer action to appeal an adverse judgment.


OVERVIEW: The landlord and the housing authority brought a detainer action against the tenant, who lived in public housing. A judgment was secured against the tenant and a writ of restitution was issued. Over objection, the tenant was ordered to pay a bond in order to appeal the adverse judgment. The tenant commenced a special action in the superior court, which found that the bond requirement of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-1179 was constitutional. On review, the court found that the superior court committed no error. The bond requirement applied to the action because it was a special rule for forcibly entry and detainer proceedings. Thus, the tenant was not permitted to file an affidavit in lieu of bond. Moreover, § 12-1179 deny unconstitutionally deny the tenant's right to equal protection of the laws. The law had a rational basis in that it served to provide adequate security before an appeal to preserve the property at issue and to guard against damage. Furthermore, the amount of the bond was barely adequate to protect the landlord's interest. Accordingly, § 12-1179 did not unconstitutionally discriminate against the poor.


OUTCOME: The court found no error and therefore declined to interfere with the superior court's proceedings.

OVERVIEW: Following defendant's conviction for second-degree murder and unlawful imprisonment, appellant sought review of the judgment. The father argued that evidence was insufficient to support a finding of abandonment.


OVERVIEW: The mother petitioned to terminate the father's parental rights to their two children on grounds that the father had abandoned the children and had not provided child support for nearly 3 years. The Honorable William P. French, Judge

The Honorable Sarah D. Grant, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmates sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which denial their petitions for writs of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmates filed petitions for writs of habeas corpus and contended that the city of Phoenix ordinance under which they were being incarcerated was unconstitutional. The trial court denied habeas relief and held that the ordinance constitutional and petitioners appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that City of Phoenix Code § 23-48.01 was not constitutionally vague or overbroad. The court also determined that the fact that transients, because they might not have anywhere else to live, sleep or sit except on the public right-of-ways, were subjected to enforcement of § 23-48.01 with greater frequency than residents of the community did not result in unconstitutional discrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the inmates' petitions for writs of habeas corpus.

Swengel-Robbins, Inc. v. Gayle Contractor


No. 1 CA-CIV 6608


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


134 Ariz. 83; 654 P.2d 17; 1982 Ariz. App. LEXIS 558



September 14, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 14, 1982. Review Denied November 23, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. C-462700

The Honorable David L. Roberts, Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bidder sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which ruled that appellee contractor was entitled to preference against the bidder for a public contract because it had asserted its right to a preference under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 34-241 (Supp. 1981).


OVERVIEW: A city sought to construct a water reservoir and accompanying transmission lines to serve the northern portions of the city. Three contractors submitted bids. The bidder submitted the lowest bid and was awarded the contract. The contractor filed a special action in the trial court that claimed that it was entitled to a five percent preference pursuant to § 34-241. The contractor had paid state and county taxes for the past two years immediately prior to submitting its bid on plant and equipment required for the performance of the project, but the bidder had not paid such taxes. The trial court ruled that the contractor was entitled to the preference against the bidder thereby making it the lowest bidder. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and held that the clear import of the language in § 34-241 was that in order to qualify for the statutory preference, a contractor had to have satisfactorily performed prior public contracts and paid state and county taxes of the kind and type specified for at least two years prior to submitting the bid. The court ruled that the classification established in § 34-241 was reasonable and furthered a legitimate state interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1196 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lycett


No. 1 CA-CR 5106


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


133 Ariz. 185; 650 P.2d 487; 1982 Ariz. App. LEXIS 487



July 29, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal From the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. CR-111896

The Honorable Cecil B. Patterson, Jr., Judge



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted defendant of conspiracy and of promoting, offering, or granting participation in a pyramid scheme, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1731. In seeking review, defendant challenged § 44-1731's constitutionality and its lawfulness as a strict liability statute and claimed the trial court had erred in admitting coconspirators' statements.


OVERVIEW: After helping with a pyramid scheme, defendant was charged with conspiracy and with participation in a pyramid scheme, pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1731. During the trial, coconspirators' statements were admitted into evidence, and thereafter, defendant was convicted. Accordingly, review was sought, and the court affirmed. In rejecting the contention that § 44-1731 was unconstitutional, the court held § 44-1731 was not vague in failing to distinguish between promoters and investors because proof of mere investing was insufficient to sustain a conviction. Likewise, the court held § 44-1731 was not overbroad because the state was entitled to regulate inherently fraudulent conduct, even among family members and social acquaintances and without regard to the degree of sophistication. Furthermore, the court held § 44-1731 was not unlawful as a strict liability statute because § 44-1731 had been enacted to protect the public from the inevitable losses incurred in pyramid schemes. Finally, the court held the coconspirators' statements had been properly admitted because the state had introduced sufficient reliable evidence of the conspiracy and defendant's participation therein.


OUTCOME: After upholding the constitutionality and the lawfulness of the comprehensive pyramid scheme statute and finding coconspirators' statements had been properly admitted, the court affirmed a judgment that convicted defendant of conspiracy and of promoting, offering, or granting participation in a pyramid scheme.

State v. Walton


No. 1 CA-CR 5130


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department A


133 Ariz. 282; 650 P.2d 1264; 1982 Ariz. App. LEXIS 495



June 29, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 6, 1982. Review Denied September 14, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Superior Court of Coconino County

Cause No. CR-9052

The Honorable J. Thomas Brooks, Judge



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Superior Court of Coconino County (Arizona) convicting him of second-degree murder while armed pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-1104, 13-604(G), and sentencing him to 10 1/2 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of second-degree murder and sentenced to 10 1/2 years in prison. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. Although defendant's sentence was greater than that recommended by the presentence report, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in giving defendant a 10 1/2 year sentence.

1198 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pike


No. 1 CA-CR 5576-PR


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department B


133 Ariz. 178; 650 P.2d 480; 1982 Ariz. App. LEXIS 501



June 22, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 18, 1982. Review Denied September 19, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Review of Action of the Superior Court of Maricopa County

17 A.R.S., Rules of Criminal Procedure, (Rule 32.9(c) 

Cause No. CR-83958

The Honorable Philip W. Marquardt, Judge

REVIEW GRANTED; RELIEF GRANTED



DISPOSITION: Relief granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the State of Arizona (state), sought review of an order entered by the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted respondent prisoner's motion to modify his sentence pursuant to Ariz. R. Crim. P. 32.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was found guilty of possessing dangerous drugs for sale. He was sentenced to prison for a term of 40 to 50 years. At the time of the prisoner's offense, a sentence of one year to life was authorized. His conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. Thereafter, he filed a petition for post-conviction relief seeking to have his sentence modified on the ground that his sentence was excessive to the point of being cruel and unusual punishment under the Eighth Amendment. The trial court granted the prisoner's petition and sentenced him to a term of 15 to 30 years. The state filed a petition for review. The court vacated the trial court's order and reinstated the original sentence. The court noted that successful challenges to the proportionality of particular sentences should be exceedingly rare and that it was appropriate for a court to interfere only in the most extreme cases. Furthermore, a sentence that was within the statutory limits was not cruel and unusual punishment when the statute fixing the punishment was constitutional. The court found that the statute under which the prisoner was sentenced did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order granting the prisoner's motion to modify his sentence. The court reinstated the prisoner's original sentence.

 

1199 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carruth


Nos. 2 CA-CIV 4403, 2 CA-CIV 4404, 2 CA-CIV 4405, 2 CA-CIV 4406, 2 CA-CIV 4420


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division Two


132 Ariz. 368; 645 P.2d 1282; 1982 Ariz. App. LEXIS 428



May 21, 1982 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PETITION FOR SPECIAL ACTION

RELIEF GRANTED



DISPOSITION: Orders dismissing criminal causes vacated; charges reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state instituted a special action against respondent trial judges of the Superior Court of Pima County (Arizona), which sought to reinstate criminal prosecutions the trial judges had dismissed because they had determined that Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-3403(A)(1) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendants were charged with violations of Ariz. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13-3403(A)(1), which prohibited intentionally inhaling toxic substances. The cases were dismissed because the trial judges determined that the statute was vague and overbroad. The state initiated a special action to reinstate the cases and asserted that the statute was not vague not overbroad. The court vacated the dismissals and reinstated the charges under the statute because it determined that § 13-3403(A)(1) was not vague since it gave clear notice to the person of reasonable intelligence of the prohibited conduct and was not overbroad as to the criminal defendants because their conduct fell directly within the terms of the prohibition. The court determined that the criminal defendants did not have standing to assert that the statute was over broad when applied to innocent parties engaged in proper conduct that could be defined as prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decisions that dismissed the criminal cause and reinstated the criminal charges.

 

1200 of 1485 DOCUMENTS


In re Appeal in Maricopa County, etc.


No. 1 CA-JUV 166


Court of Appeals of Arizona, Division One, Department C


132 Ariz. 486; 647 P.2d 184; 1982 Ariz. App. LEXIS 451



May 13, 1982 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied June 15, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Maricopa County

Cause No. JS-4130

The Honorable Edward C. Rapp, Judge



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Maricopa County (Arizona), which granted appellee Department of Economic Security's severance petition and terminated the parent-child relationship between the mother and her two daughters.


OVERVIEW: The department filed a severance petition seeking to terminate the mother's rights. The trial court granted the petition. On review, the court reversed. The court found that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-537(B), which required only a preponderance of the evidence to terminate parental rights, was unconstitutional. A juvenile court's findings with respect to grounds for termination must have been based on clear and convincing evidence. The evidence was insufficient to support an order of termination under any standard of proof, and the case was reversed. A finding of abandonment under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 8-533(B)(1) required evidence of intentional conduct on the part of a parent which demonstrated a settled purpose to forego all parental duties and relinquish all parental claims. A finding of "token efforts" standing alone did not support an order terminating parental rights, and although the interests of the children may certainly have been considered, they could not be the sole basis for termination.


OUTCOME: The court found against the department and reversed the trial court's order terminating the mother's parental rights.
